The Recommended Manner of Sujud for Women in the Hanafi School
Specifies the manner of sujud for women with a ta'lil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended posture for women in sujud according to the Hanafi school and explain the rationale of modesty.

Core Idea
A woman's sujud should be compact and low, because concealment is more modest.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding how women should perform sujud. While the essential pillars of sujud are the same for men and women, the recommended posture differs to observe greater modesty. The source text from Al-Hidayah explains that a woman should lower herself and attach her belly to her thighs, as this is more concealing. We will explore the reasoning behind this recommendation and its legal status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its recommended manner
What is the act being ruled upon? What specific manner is recommended?
The act is sujud; the recommended manner is for the woman to lower herself and press her belly to her thighs.
2
Locate the rationale (ta'lil)
What reason does the text give for this recommendation?
The reason is 'astaru laha' — it is more concealing for her.
3
Determine the hukm level
Is this ruling an obligation (wajib) or a recommendation (sunnah)?
It is a sunnah muakkadah, not a wajib. The prayer remains valid without it.
4
Understand the scope
Does this posture affect the validity of sujud?
No, it is a recommended betterment; the pillars of sujud are unaffected.
5
Note cross-madhhab differences
Do other schools have a similar differentiation?
Some schools do not differentiate the sujud posture between men and women.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمرأة تنخفض في سجودها وتلزق بطنها بفخذيها لان ذلك استرلها
ترجمہ اور عورت اپنے سجدہ میں پست ہو جائے اور اپنے پیٹ کو اپنی رانوں سے ملائے کیونکہ ایسا کرنا اس کے حق میں زیادہ پردہ ہے۔
تشریح اس عبارت میں عورت کے سجدہ کی کیفیت کا بیان ہے۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ عورت سجدہ کرتے وقت پست ہو جائے یعنی زمین سے قریب تر ہو جائے اور پیٹ کو رانوں سے ملا دے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کیفیت کے ساتھ سجدہ کرنے میں عورت کے حق میں زیادہ ستر ہے در آنحالیکہ عورت کے حق میں ستر ہی مطلوب۔
And the woman lowers herself in her sujud and attaches her belly to her thighs because that is more concealing for her. [Urdu translation and commentary: The woman should lower herself in sujud, i.e., become closer to the ground, and attach her belly to her thighs. The reason is that this manner of sujud provides more covering for her, and covering is what is desired for women.]
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This ruling passage specifies the manner of sujud for women. The matn states: 'The woman lowers herself in her sujud and attaches her belly to her thighs because that is more concealing for her.' The commentator explains that 'lowers herself' means she becomes closer to the ground, and she should press her abdomen against her thighs. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that this posture is more concealing (astar) for her, and concealment (satr) is the desired objective for women in prayer. The ruling is derived from the general principle of modesty in Islamic law, not from a specific textual proof.

Key Terms
المرأة تنخفض (al-mar'atu tankhafid): The woman lowers herself, meaning she goes closer to the ground than a man would.
ستتر لها (astaru laha): More concealing for her, i.e., it better covers her body and preserves modesty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school recommend that women attach their belly to their thighs in sujud?
A) Because it is physically easier for women.
B) Because it is more concealing and thus more modest.
C) Because the Prophet specifically commanded women to do so.
D) Because it is required to make the sujud valid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends that women in sujud lower themselves and attach their belly to their thighs to achieve greater modesty, though the prayer remains valid without it.

The Ruling on Jalsah and the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on jalsah with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the jalsah between the two sujuds, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute, and apply the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
Jalsah is wajib in the Hanafi school, but Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider it sunnah – omission still valid.

The brief sitting between the two prostrations (jalsah) is a well-known posture in prayer, but its legal status is debated within the Hanafi school. This lesson unpacks the method, the proof from the Prophet's teaching to the Bedouin, and the different opinions of the founding imams. By understanding the ikhtilaf, you will see how the school arrived at the relied-upon position that jalsah is wajib, requiring sajdah sahw if omitted intentionally.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
What is the jalsah? It is the sitting between the two sujuds. According to the majority of the Hanafi school, it is wajib. Identify the evidence cited.
The matn states the method: raise head, sit calmly, then prostrate again.
2
Examine the proof (dalil)
The Prophet (peace be upon him) told the Bedouin: 'Then raise your head until you are sitting upright.' Understand how this command is used to derive wujub.
This is a dalil naqli from Sunnah.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that if one goes directly to the second sujud without sitting upright, the prayer is still valid – meaning jalsah is not obligatory. Abu Yusuf (in the relied-upon view) considers it wajib.
The dispute is about the interpretation of the command and the consequence of omission.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and its implications
The later Hanafi masters (Al-Marghinani etc.) adopted the wajib view. If a person intentionally omits the jalsah, sajdah sahw is required. If omitted unintentionally, no compensation is needed.
This is an example of tarjih within the school.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a case where someone prays but does not pause between sujuds at all, determine the ruling according to the different views and the mufta bihi.
This solidifies the practical difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ثم يرفع رأسه، ويكبر لما روينا فاذا اطمأن جالسا كبر وسجد لقوله عليه السلام في حديث الاعرابی ثم ارفع رأسك حتى تستوى جالسا ولولم يستو جالسا وكبر و سجد اخرى اجزاه عند أبي حنيفة و محمد وقد ذكرناه وتكلموا في مقدار الرفع والاصح انه اذا كان الى السجود اقرب لايجوز لانه يعد ساجدا وان كان الى الجلوس اقرب جاز لانه يعد جـ ا فتحقق الثانية
ترجمہ کہا کہ پھر اپنا سر اٹھائے اور تکبیر کہے۔ اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم روایت کر چکے۔ پھر جب اطمینان سے بیٹھ جائے تو تکبیر کہے اور سجدہ کرے کیونکہ حدیث اعرابی میں ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا پھر اپنا سر اٹھا یہاں تک کہ تو سیدھا بیٹھ جائے۔ اور اگر سیدھا نہیں بیٹا اور تکبیر کہہ کر دوسرا سجدہ کیا تو ابو حنیفہ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اس کو کافی ہو گیا اور ہم اس کو ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔ اور سر اٹھانے کی مقدار میں کلام کیا ہے اور اصح یہ ہے کہ جب سجدہ سے قریب تر ہو تو جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ وہ سجدہ ہی میں شمار ہوگا۔ اور اگر وہ بیٹھک سے زیادہ قریب ہے تو جائز ہے کیونکہ وہ بیٹھا شمار ہوگا پس دوسرا سجدہ تحقیق ہو جائیگا۔
تشریح اس عبارت میں دوسرے سجدہ کی کیفیت کا بیان ہے چنانچہ فرمایا کہ سجدہ اولیٰ سے سر اٹھاتے ہوئے تکبیر کہے دلیل وہ روایت ہے جو سابق می گذر چکی یعنی ان النبي كان يكبر عند كل خفض ورفع پھر جب اطمینان کے ساتھ بیٹھ گیا تو تکبیر کہتے ہوئے دوسرے سجدہ میں چلا جائے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اعرابی کو نماز کی تعلیم دیتے ہوئے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ثم ارفع راسک حتی تستوى جالسا یعنی پھر اپنا سر اٹھا یہاں تک کہ سیدھا بیٹھ جائے۔ اور اگر نمازی پہلے سجدہ سے اٹھ کر سیدھا نہیں بیٹھا اور تکبیر کہہ کر دوسرا سجدہ کیا تو طرفین کے نزدیک کافی ہو گیا۔ اس کی تفصیل مع الاختلاف تعدیل ارکان کے ذیل میں گذر چکی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ مشائخ کا اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے کہ دوسرا سجدہ معتبر ہونے کے لئے پہلے سجدہ سے کس قدر سر اٹھانا ضروری ہے۔
He said: Then he raises his head and says takbir, based on what we narrated. Then when he is seated calmly, he says takbir and prostrates, because of his statement (peace be upon him) in the hadith of the Bedouin: 'Then raise your head until you are sitting upright.' And if he did not sit upright but said takbir and made the second sujud, it suffices according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as we have mentioned. And they discussed the extent of raising. The most correct is that if he is closer to sujud, it is not permissible because he is considered still in sujud. And if he is closer to sitting, it is permissible because he is considered sitting, then the second sujud is verified. [Urdu translation and commentary: He said: Then he raises his head and says takbir...]
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage addresses the method of rising from the first sujud to the second, specifically the necessity of a brief sitting (jalsah) between them. The matn (from Al-Hidayah) states that one raises the head saying takbir, then sits calmly, then says takbir and prostrates again, based on the Prophet's instruction to the Bedouin: 'Then raise your head until you are sitting upright.' However, there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that if one does not sit upright but immediately goes to the second sujud after takbir, it still suffices. The commentator explains that the scholars discussed how much raising is necessary. The correct view is that if the person is closer to the sujud position (i.e., barely raised), it is not valid because he is still considered in sujud. But if he is closer to the sitting position, it is valid because he is considered sitting, and then the second sujud is properly performed. This ikhtilaf is related to the broader issue of 'ta'dil al-arkan' (proper fulfillment of postures). The passage concludes by noting that the mashayikh differ on the extent of raising needed for the second sujud to be valid.

Key Terms
اطمأن جالسا (itma'anna jalisan): To sit calmly, meaning to achieve stillness in the sitting posture between the two sujuds.
تعديل الأركان (ta'dil al-arkan): Proper performance of the pillars, including calmness and correct posture in each position.
جلسة (jalsah): The brief sitting between the two sujuds in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the consequence of intentionally omitting the jalsah (sitting between sujuds) in prayer?
A) The prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid, but sajdah sahw is required.
C) The prayer is valid without any compensation.
D) The prayer is valid only if the omission was unintentional.

Key Takeaway
The jalsah is wajib in the Hanafi school (mufta bihi), but Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider it sunnah – the key difference is whether sajdah sahw is needed for omission.

Women's Sujood Posture in Prayer
Ruling on women's sujood posture with rationale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi recommended posture for a woman in sujood and explain the rationale of satr.

Core Idea
Women's sujood is compact and low to maximise modesty, distinct from the male posture.

This passage from al-Hidayah gives a specific posture for women in sujood, emphasising modesty (satr). It is a recommended (sunnah) practice, not obligatory, but rooted in the Hanafi concern for concealing women's form during prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The passage describes the recommended sujood posture for a woman: she lowers herself (tanakhfad) and attaches her belly to her thighs (talzaq batanaha bifakhidayha). This is the Hanafi position.
The verb 'tanakhfad' implies coming close to the ground, and 'talzaq' implies sticking.
2
Understand the Rationale
The reason given is 'because that is more concealing for her' (li-anna dhālika ashtar laha). The term 'ashtar' means more covering/modest. The underlying principle is satr (covering), which is emphasized for women in prayer.
The commentary adds that covering is required for women, and this posture best achieves that.
3
Classify the Ruling Level
This posture is classified as sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah) for women. It is not wajib or fard. If a woman prays without adopting this posture, her prayer is valid, but she loses the reward of following this sunnah.
The Hanafi position box confirms hukm_level = sunnah_muakkadah.
4
Recognize the Hanafi Distinctiveness
The Hanafi school differentiates between male and female prayer postures. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not differentiate, holding that men and women pray identically in sujood. This is an area of ikhtilaf.
The cross_madhhab_status is mukhtalaf_fih.
5
Apply in Practice
A woman should strive to adopt this compact posture for greater modesty. She may also pray with a more open posture, but it is better to follow the sunnah. This ruling is based on the principle of satr, not on a specific hadith cited here.
The mufta bihi is to perform sujood in this compact manner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمرأة تنخفض في سجودها وتلزق بطنها بفخذيها لان ذلك استرلها ترجمہ اور عورت اپنے سجدہ میں پست ہو جائے اور اپنے پیٹ کو اپنی رانوں سے ملائے کیونکہ ایسا کرنا اس کے حق میں زیادہ پردہ ہے۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں عورت کے سجدہ کی کیفیت کا بیان ہے۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ عورت سجدہ کرتے وقت پست ہو جائے یعنی زمین سے قریب تر ہو جائے اور پیٹ کو رانوں سے ملا دے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کیفیت کے ساتھ سجدہ کرنے میں عورت کے حق میں زیادہ ستر ہے در آنحالیکہ عورت کے حق میں ستر ہی مطلوب۔
And the woman lowers herself in her sujood and attaches her belly to her thighs because that is more concealing for her. Translation: And a woman should become low in her sujood and attach her belly to her thighs because doing so is more covering for her. Explanation: In this sentence, the description of a woman's sujood is given. Thus it is said: a woman at the time of sujood becomes low, i.e., comes close to the ground, and attaches her belly to her thighs. The proof is that with this posture, there is greater covering (satr) for the woman, and covering is required for a woman.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for a woman's sujood posture. The matn says: 'The woman lowers herself in her sujood and attaches her belly to her thighs because that is more concealing for her.' The commentary explains that she should come close to the ground and stick her belly to her thighs. The reason given is that this posture provides more covering (satr) for her, which is required for a woman. No explicit hadith is cited here, but the ruling is based on the principle of modesty. This is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Key Terms
تنخفض (tanakhfad): She lowers herself, i.e., comes close to the ground.
تلزق (talzaq): She attaches, sticks her belly to her thighs.
ستر (satr): Covering, modesty; the underlying rationale for the posture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommended posture for a woman in sujood according to this passage?
A) She should raise her head and back like a man.
B) She should lower herself and attach her belly to her thighs.
C) She should sit on her heels.
D) She should place her hands on the ground first.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends a compact sujood posture for women to maximise modesty, based on the principle of satr.

Raising the Head between Sajdahs: Extent and Validity
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on required raising between sajdahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions on the minimal raising between sajdahs and identify the relied-upon (muftā bihi) criterion.

Core Idea
The second sajdah is valid only if the worshiper is closer to sitting than to sujood.

In this lesson, we examine the requirement to raise the head between the two sajdahs in salah. The matn states that one should sit with tranquility, but the Hanafi school has a well-known ikhtilaf on the minimal raising. The passage from al-Hidayah presents several opinions and settles on the criterion of being closer to sitting. Understanding this dispute clarifies the flexibility within the Hanafi school on a subtle point of prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the base ruling: one must sit with tranquility (itma'ninah) between sajdahs. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that if one does not sit fully but goes directly to the second sajdah, it suffices.
This is based on the hadith of the Bedouin.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Several scholars (Hasan ibn Ziyad, Muhammad ibn Salama, al-Quduri) differ on the minimal raising: forehead clearance, air passage, perception of an onlooker, or any amount called 'raising'.
The disagreement is on the operationalization of 'raising'.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The author of al-Hidayah declares the 'sahih' (sound) view: if the person is closer to sujood (insufficient raising), the second sajdah is invalid; if closer to sitting, it is valid. This is the muftā bihi.
The response uses the hadith's phrase 'until you sit upright' to derive a measurable criterion.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is that the validity of the second sajdah depends on the exact extent of head elevation. A worshiper who raises minimally but does not reach a state of being 'closer to sitting' would have an invalid second sajdah under the preferred view.
This affects the number of sajdahs counted and the overall validity of the rak'ah.
5
Cross-madhhab comparison
The Shafi'i school requires a distinct sitting (jalsah) between sajdahs, while the Hanafi view is more lenient, allowing a minimal raising that still achieves the state of sitting.
This highlights the methodological difference in interpreting the same hadith.

Source Text

وتكلموا في مقدار الرفع والاصح انه اذا كان الى السجود اقرب لايجوز لانه يعد ساجدا وان كان الى الجلوس اقرب جاز لانه يعد جـ ا فتحقق الثانية ترجمہ کہا کہ پھر اپنا سر اٹھائے اور تکبیر کہے۔ اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم روایت کر چکے۔ پھر جب اطمینان سے بیٹھ جائے تو تکبیر کہے اور سجدہ کرے کیونکہ حدیث اعرابی میں ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا پھر اپنا سر اٹھا یہاں تک کہ تو سیدھا بیٹھ جائے۔ اور اگر سیدھا نہیں بیٹا اور تکبیر کہہ کر دوسرا سجدہ کیا تو ابو حنیفہ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اس کو کافی ہو گیا اور ہم اس کو ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔ اور سر اٹھانے کی مقدار میں کلام کیا ہے اور اصح یہ ہے کہ جب سجدہ سے قریب تر ہو تو جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ وہ سجدہ ہی میں شمار ہوگا۔ اور اگر وہ بیٹھک سے زیادہ قریب ہے تو جائز ہے کیونکہ وہ بیٹھا شمار ہوگا پس دوسرا سجدہ تحقیق ہو جائیگا۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں دوسرے سجدہ کی کیفیت کا بیان ہے چنانچہ فرمایا کہ سجدہ اولیٰ سے سر اٹھاتے ہوئے تکبیر کہے دلیل وہ روایت ہے جو سابق می گذر چکی یعنی ان النبي كان يكبر عند كل خفض ورفع پھر جب اطمینان کے ساتھ بیٹھ گیا تو تکبیر کہتے ہوئے دوسرے سجدہ میں چلا جائے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اعرابی کو نماز کی تعلیم دیتے ہوئے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایاشم ارفع راسک حتی تستوى جالسا یعنی پھر اپنا سر اٹھا یہاں تک کہ سیدھا بیٹھ جائے ۔ اور اگر نمازی پہلے سجدہ سے اٹھ کر سیدھا نہیں بیٹا اور تکبیر کہہ کر دوسرا سجدہ کیا تو طرفین کے نزدیک کافی ہو گیا۔ اس کی تفصیل مع الاختلاف تعدیل ارکان کے ذیل میں گذر چکی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ مشائخ کا اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے کہ دوسرا سجدہ معتبر ہونے کے لئے پہلے سجدہ سے کس قدر سر اٹھانا ضروری ہے۔ بعض فقہاء نے کہا کہ جب پیشانی زمین سے ہٹ گئی اور پھر سجدہ میں چلا گیا تو دونوں سجدے ادا ہو گئے۔ حسن بن زیاد نے کہا کہ جب اس نے زمین سے اپنا سر اتنی مقدار اٹھایا کہ وہاں سے ہوا گذر جائے تو اس صورت میں دونوں سجدے ادا ہو جائیں گے ۔ حسن پور زیاد کا قول پہلے قول سے قریب ہے۔ محمد بن سلمہ کہتے ہیں کہ اگر اتنی مقدار سر اٹھایا کہ دیکھنے والا یہ سمجھے کہ اس نے دوسرا سجدہ کرنے کے لئے اپنا سر اٹھایا تو دونوں سجدے ہو جائیں گے ورنہ ایک سجد ہ ادا ہوگا۔ امام قدوری نے کہا کہ جس پر لفظ رفع ( سراٹھانا ) بولا جائے اس قد رسراٹھانا معتبر ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اصح قول یہ ہے کہ اگر اتنا اٹھائے کہ بہ نسبت بیٹھک کے سجدہ سے زیادہ قریب ہے تو دوسرا سجدہ جائز نہیں ہوا میں بیٹھا ہوا شمار ہو گا لہذا دوسرا سجدہ متحقق ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ ابھی تک پہلے سجدہ ہی میں شمار ہوگا اور اگر اس قدر اٹھا کر بیٹھک سے زیادہ قریب ہے تو دوسرا سجدہ جائز ہے کیونکہ وہ اس صورت قیاس کو اس میں کوئی دخل نہیں ۔ اور بعض حضرات نے یہ حکمت ذکر کی کہ دو سجدے شیطان کو ذلیل کرنے کے لئے ہیں اس لئے کر تخلیق آدم کے بعد اللہ تعالیٰ نے اس کو حکم دیا تھا کہ وہ آدم کو سجدہ کرے لیکن اس نے آدم کو سجدہ نہیں کیا لہذا ہم شیطان کو رسوا اور ذلیل کرنے کے لئے دو سجدے کرتے ہیں جو سہو میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس طرف اشارہ کیا چنانچہ فرمایاهما ترغيما لشيطان یعنی کہو کے دونوں سجدے شیطان کو ذلیل کرنے کے لئے رہی یہ بات کہ ہر رکعت میں ایک رکوع اور دو سجدے کیوں ہیں تو اس بارے میں اکثر علماء کی رائے یہ ہے کہ یہ تو قیفی چیز ہے عقل او ہیں۔ اور بعض نے کہا کہ پہلے سجدہ میں اس طرف اشارہ کیا گیا کہ انسان مٹی سے پیدا کیا گیا ہے اور دوسرے میں یہ اشارہ ہے کہ اسی میں لوٹا دیا جائے گا۔ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا منها خلقناکم وفيها نعيدكم والله اعلم
He said: Then he raises his head and says takbir based on what we narrated. When he sits with tranquility, he says takbir and prostrates because of his statement (peace be upon him) in the hadith of the Bedouin: 'Then raise your head until you sit upright.' If he does not sit upright but says takbir and performs another sajdah, it suffices according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and we have mentioned it. They discussed the extent of raising, and the most authentic is that if he is closer to sujood it is not permissible because he is considered prostrating, and if he is closer to sitting it is permissible because he is considered sitting, so the second sajdah is realized. Translation: He said: Then he raises his head and says takbir due to the hadith we narrated. Then when he sits with tranquility, he says takbir and performs sajdah because in the hadith of the Bedouin the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Then raise your head until you sit upright.' If he did not sit upright and said takbir and performed the second sajdah, it suffices according to Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, and we have mentioned this. They discussed the extent of raising, and the most authentic is that when he is closer to sujood it is not permissible because he is considered in sujood, and if he is closer to sitting it is permissible because he is considered sitting; thus the second sajdah is verified. Explanation: In this sentence, the description of the second sajdah is given. Thus it is said: when raising the head from the first sajdah, he says takbir; the proof is the narration that passed earlier: that the Prophet used to say takbir at every lowering and raising. Then when he sits with tranquility, he says takbir and goes into the second sajdah. The proof is that while teaching the Bedouin, the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Then raise your head until you sit upright.' If the worshiper does not sit upright after rising from the first sajdah but says takbir and performs the second sajdah, it suffices according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Its detail with disagreement passed earlier under 'tadil al-arkan'. The author of al-Hidayah says that the mashayikh differ on how much head-raising is necessary for the second sajdah to be valid. Some jurists said: when the forehead leaves the ground and then he goes into sajdah, both sajdahs are performed. Hasan ibn Ziyad said: when he raises his head from the ground to the extent that air passes between them, then both sajdahs are performed. Hasan ibn Ziyad's saying is close to the first. Muhammad ibn Salama says: if he raises his head to an extent that the onlooker thinks he raised his head for the second sajdah, then both sajdahs are performed; otherwise only one sajdah is performed. Imam al-Quduri said: that extent on which the word 'raising' can be applied is sufficient. The author of al-Hidayah said: the most authentic saying is that if he raises to the extent that he is closer to sajdah than to sitting, the second sajdah is not valid because he is still considered in the first sajdah; if he is closer to sitting, the second sajdah is valid because he is considered sitting. There is no role of qiyas in this. Some persons mentioned the wisdom: two sajdahs are to humiliate the devil, because after the creation of Adam, Allah commanded him to prostrate to Adam but he did not, so we perform two sajdahs to disgrace the devil. The Prophet (peace be upon him) indicated this in a hadith: 'Both sajdahs are to humiliate the devil.' As for why there is one ruku and two sajdahs in each rak'ah, most scholars say it is a devotional matter with no rational explanation. And some said: the first sajdah indicates that man was created from dust, and the second that he will return to it. Allah said: 'From it We created you, and into it We will return you.' And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage discusses the validity of the second sajdah and the required amount of raising the head from the first sajdah. The matn states that after raising the head, one should sit with tranquility before the second sajdah. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that if one does not sit fully but goes directly to the second sajdah, it suffices. The text then explores intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the minimal raising: some say lifting the forehead suffices, Hasan ibn Ziyad requires air to pass, Muhammad ibn Salama uses an onlooker's perception, Quduri says any amount called 'raising' works. The author (sahib al-Hidayah) declares the 'sahih' (correct) view: if the person is closer to sajdah (i.e., not enough raising), the second sajdah is invalid; if closer to sitting (julus), it is valid. This relies on the hadith of the Bedouin commanding to sit upright. The commentary then adds a wisdom section explaining the purpose of two sajdahs: to humiliate Satan and as a reminder of creation from dust and return to it.

Key Terms
اطمأن (itma'anna): To be tranquil, to come to rest; a condition for the posture between sajdahs.
الرفع (al-raf'): The act of raising the head; the extent of this raising is disputed.
اصح (asahh): The most sound/correct opinion among the ikhtilaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most authentic view in this passage, when is the second sajdah valid?
A) When the forehead leaves the ground for any amount.
B) When air passes under the forehead.
C) When the person is closer to sitting than to sujood.
D) When an onlooker thinks he raised his head.

Key Takeaway
The second sajdah is valid only if the worshiper's head elevation makes him closer to sitting than to sujood.

Salah — Prayer

Rising from Sujood: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Jalsah al-Istirahah
Presents Hanafi view on rising to standing and refutes Shafi'i on resting sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on rising from sujood, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and evaluate the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof.

Core Idea
Rise directly on the balls of the feet; the resting sitting is for the elderly, not part of the sunnah prayer.

In this lesson, we examine a well-known inter-madhhab dispute: whether one should sit briefly (jalsah al-istirahah) when rising from sujood to qiyam. The Hanafi school holds that no sitting is prescribed, while Imam al-Shafi'i considers it sunnah. We will follow the argument from al-Hidayah, which presents the Hanafi position and refutes the opposing view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the act: rising from the second sujood to standing. The Hanafi ruling: rise directly on the balls of the feet (sadr al-qadamayn) without any sitting and without supporting on the hands.
2
Identify the opposition
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that one should sit briefly (jalsah khafifah) and then rise while supporting on the ground with the hands.
This sitting is known as jalsah al-istirahah.
3
Examine the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i school cites a narration that the Prophet (peace be upon him) sat briefly and then rose using hand support.
This is a hadith of the Prophet's action.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is twofold: first, the Shafi'i narration is interpreted as being specific to old age or difficulty, not a general sunnah; second, the stronger proof is the hadith of Abu Hurairah that the Prophet rose on the balls of his feet. Additionally, the 'sitting of rest' is not part of the prayer's structure.
The Hanafi position relies on the principle that the prayer's form is fixed and any addition is not part of the sunnah.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Shafi'i, sitting briefly is sunnah; under Hanafi, it is not prescribed and may be considered makruh if done habitually without a valid excuse.
The mufta bihi (operative) Hanafi position is to rise directly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال فاذا اطمأن ساجدا كبر وقد ذكرناه و استوی قائما على صدور قدميه ولا يقعد ولا يعتمد بيديه على الارض وقال الشافعى يجلس جلسة خفيفة ثم ينهض معتمد اعلى الارض لان النبي عليه السلام فعل ذلك ولما حديث أبي هريرة ان النبى عليه السلام كان ينهض فى الصلوة على صدور قدميه ومارواه محمول على حالة الكبر ولان هذه قعدة استراحة والصلوة ما وضعت لها ترجمہ کہا کہ پھر جب سجدے کی حالت میں اطمینان کرلے تو تکبیر کہے اور ہم اس کو ذکر کر چکے۔ اور سیدھا کھڑا ہو جائے اپنے پنجوں کے بل اور نہ بیٹھے اور نہ ٹیک لگائے اپنے ہاتھوں کے ساتھ زمین پر اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ خفیف کی بیٹھک بیٹھ لے۔ پھر زمین پر ٹیک دیتے ہوئے کھڑا ہو اس لئے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایسا کیا ہے اور ہماری دلیل حدیث ابو ہریرہ ہے کہ حضور نماز میں اپنے پنجوں کے بل انحہ کرتے تھے اور وہ حدیث جس کو امام شافعی نے روایت کیا ہے وہ بڑھاپے کی حالت پر محمول ہے اور اس لئے کہ یہ قعد استراحت ہے،
He said: Then when he has tranquility in sajdah, he says takbir, and we have mentioned it, and he stands upright on the balls of his feet, and he does not sit, and he does not support himself with his hands on the ground. Al-Shafi'i said: He sits a light sitting, then he rises supporting on the ground, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did that. Our proof is the hadith of Abu Hurairah that the Prophet used to rise in prayer on the balls of his feet. And that hadith (which al-Shafi'i narrated) is interpreted as the case of old age. And because this sitting is a sitting of rest, and prayer was not prescribed for that. Translation: He said: Then when he has tranquility in the state of sajdah, he says takbir, and we have mentioned it. And he stands upright on his toes (balls of feet), and does not sit, and does not support himself with his hands on the ground. Imam al-Shafi'i said: He should sit a light sitting, then rise while supporting on the ground, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did that. And our proof is the hadith of Abu Hurairah that the Prophet used to rise in prayer on the balls of his feet. And that hadith which al-Shafi'i narrated is interpreted as the case of old age, and because this sitting is a sitting of rest, and prayer was not prescribed for it.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i. The Hanafi position: after the second sajdah, one should rise directly to standing on the balls of the feet (sadr al-qadam), without any sitting (jalsah) and without supporting on the hands. The Shafi'i position: one should sit briefly (jalsah khafifah) and then rise using hand support on the ground, citing the Prophet's practice. The Hanafi response: the Shafi'i's hadith is interpreted as pertaining to old age when difficulty necessitates support; the general practice of the Prophet, as per Abu Hurairah, was to rise on the balls of the feet. Furthermore, Hanafi argues that this 'jalsah al-istirahah' (resting sitting) was not part of the prayer's prescribed form. The relied-upon Hanafi view is to rise directly without sitting.

Key Terms
صدور القدمين (sudur al-qadamayn): The balls of the feet, i.e., the front part excluding toes.
قعدة استراحة (qa'dat al-istirahah): A sitting of rest; a brief pause after sajdah before rising.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the Hanafi ruling on rising from sujood to qiyam?
A) Sit briefly and then rise using hand support.
B) Rise directly on the balls of the feet without sitting.
C) Rise immediately without any pause.
D) Sit for a long time before rising.

Key Takeaway
Rising directly on the balls of the feet without sitting is the Hanafi sunnah; the resting sitting is only for those with a legitimate excuse.

Measure of Raising the Head Between the Two Sajdahs
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimum raise between sajdahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the various Hanafi opinions on the minimum amount of raising the head between sajdahs and identify the relied-upon position according to al-Hidayah.

Core Idea
The minimum raise between sajdahs is a transmitted measure, not based on analogy.

In the chapter on the description of prayer, classical Hanafi works record several opinions on how much one must raise the head after the first sajdah to begin the second. This matter is not subject to qiyas (analogy); it is based on transmitted rulings. The author of al-Hidayah gives the preferred view, which is the operative position for practice today.

Guided Path
1
List the different opinions
Identify each opinion: some say mere lifting, Hasan ibn Ziyad: air passes, Muhammad ibn Salamah: onlooker's perception, al-Quduri: linguistic raising, al-Hidayah: closer to sitting than sajdah.
These are all recorded in Hanafi nawadir and later works.
2
Understand the criterion of each
Note the rationale behind each: air passage (Hasan), onlooker perception (Muhammad), linguistic definition (Quduri), and physical posture (Hidayah).
3
Identify the tarjih (preference)
al-Hidayah's view is called 'asahh' (most correct) and is the mufta bihi.
This is the position to follow in practice.
4
Note the absence of qiyas
The text explicitly states 'qiyas has no role in this' because the measure is based on transmitted rulings, not analogy.
This emphasizes the ta'abbudi nature of the act.
5
Apply to practice
In your prayer, ensure you raise your head to a point closer to sitting than to sajdah to validly separate the two sajdahs.
This is the operative ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بعض فقہاء نے کہا کہ جب پیشانی زمین سے ہٹ گئی اور پھر سجدہ میں چلا گیا تو دونوں سجدے ادا ہو گئے۔ حسن بن زیاد نے کہا کہ جب اس نے زمین سے اپنا سر اتنی مقدار اٹھایا کہ وہاں سے ہوا گذر جائے تو اس صورت میں دونوں سجدے ادا ہو جائیں گے ۔ حسن بن زیاد کا قول پہلے قول سے قریب ہے۔

قیاس کو اس میں کوئی دخل نہیں ۔ اور بعض حضرات نے یہ حکمت ذکر کی کہ دو سجدے شیطان کو ذلیل کرنے کے لئے ہیں اس لئے کر تخلیق آدم کے بعد اللہ تعالیٰ نے اس کو حکم دیا تھا کہ وہ آدم کو سجدہ کرے لیکن اس نے آدم کو سجدہ نہیں کیا لہذا ہم شیطان کو رسوا اور ذلیل کرنے کے لئے دو سجدے کرتے ہیں جو سہو میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس طرف اشارہ کیا چنانچہ فرمایاهما ترغيما لشيطان یعنی کہو کے دونوں سجدے شیطان کو ذلیل کرنے کے لئے

اور بعض نے کہا کہ پہلے سجدہ میں اس طرف اشارہ کیا گیا کہ انسان مٹی سے پیدا کیا گیا ہے اور دوسرے میں یہ اشارہ ہے کہ اسی میں لوٹا دیا جائے گا۔ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا منها خلقناکم وفيها نعيدكم والله اعلم
Chapter on the Description of Prayer. Some jurists said: When the forehead is lifted from the ground and then he goes into sajdah, both sajdahs are performed. Hasan ibn Ziyad said: When he raises his head from the ground to the extent that air passes between them, then in that case both sajdahs are performed. Hasan ibn Ziyad's statement is closer to the first statement. Muhammad ibn Salamah said: If he raises his head to such an extent that an onlooker thinks he raised his head for the second sajdah, then both sajdahs are performed; otherwise, one sajdah is performed. Imam al-Quduri said: The measure of raising that can be called 'raising' is valid. The author of al-Hidayah said: The most correct statement is that if he raises it to such an extent that it is closer to the sajdah than to the sitting, then the second sajdah is not valid, and he will be considered as still sitting, so the second sajdah will be realized. Because he is still considered in the first sajdah. And if he raises to such an extent that it is closer to the sitting than to the sajdah, then the second sajdah is valid. Qiyas has no role in this. And some people mentioned this wisdom: Two sajdahs are to humiliate the devil. Because after the creation of Adam, Allah commanded him to prostrate to Adam, but he did not prostrate to Adam. So we make two sajdahs to disgrace and humiliate the devil. The Prophet ﷺ alluded to this in the hadith of sahw, where he said: 'They are for humiliating the devil.' As for why there is one bowing and two sajdahs in each rak'ah, most scholars say it is a prescriptive matter, not intellectual. And some said: In the first sajdah, it is indicated that man was created from dust, and in the second, that he will be returned to it. Allah said: 'From it We created you, and into it We will return you.' And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage begins with an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the minimum amount of raising the head between the two sajdahs necessary to consider the first sajdah complete and begin the second. Several opinions are recorded: some jurists consider the mere lifting of the forehead from the ground sufficient; Hasan ibn Ziyad requires enough space for air to pass; Muhammad ibn Salamah relies on the perception of an onlooker; Imam al-Quduri says any act that can be linguistically called 'raising' suffices. The relied-upon position according to al-Hidayah is that one must raise the head to a point closer to the sitting posture than to the sajdah; otherwise, the second sajdah is not valid. The author notes that qiyas (analogy) has no application here because the exact measurement is based on transmitted rulings. Following this, the passage mentions the wisdom (hikmah) behind performing two sajdahs: first, to humiliate Iblis, who refused to prostrate to Adam, citing the prophetic saying 'they are for humiliating the devil'; second, to symbolize man's creation from earth and his return to it, as stated in the Quran.

Key Terms
رفع (raf'): The act of raising the head between prostrations; its minimal amount is disputed among Hanafi scholars.
اصح (asahh): The designation 'most correct' used by al-Hidayah to indicate the preferred view among the ikhtilaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Hidayah, what is the relied-upon criterion for the amount of raising the head between the two sajdahs?
A) The forehead must leave the ground.
B) The raising must be sufficient for air to pass.
C) The head must be raised to a point closer to the sitting posture than to the sajdah.
D) An onlooker must think he is going for the second sajdah.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position requires raising the head between sajdahs to a point closer to sitting than to prostration; this is a transmitted measure, not based on analogy.

The Wisdom Behind Two Sajdahs
Wisdom (hikmah) behind the two sajdahs in each rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two wisdoms (hikmah) for performing two sajdahs in each rak'ah and cite the prophetic hadith used as proof.

Core Idea
Two sajdahs signify both the humiliation of Iblis and man's creation from and return to dust.

After discussing the physical measure of raising between sajdahs, the passage turns to the spiritual wisdom behind why there are two prostrations in each rak'ah. It mentions two wisdoms: the first is to humiliate the devil, who refused to prostrate to Adam; the second is to symbolize man's origin from earth and his eventual return to it. The Prophet ﷺ alluded to the first wisdom when he said about the two sajdahs of sahw: 'they are for humiliating the devil.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the first wisdom
The first wisdom is that two sajdahs are done to humiliate the devil (Iblis), who refused to prostrate to Adam. The Prophet ﷺ said: 'They are for humiliating the devil.'
This is found in the hadith of sahw (forgetfulness).
2
Identify the second wisdom
The second wisdom is symbolic: the first sajdah indicates man's creation from dust, and the second sajdah indicates his return to dust after death.
This is supported by the Quranic verse: 'From it We created you, and into it We will return you.'
3
Understand the nature of these wisdoms
These wisdoms are not the basis of the ruling (the two sajdahs are prescribed by revelation), but they provide spiritual insight into the act.
The text notes that most scholars say it is a prescriptive matter (tawqifi), not intellectual.
4
Relate to the hadith
The hadith 'huma targhiman li-shaytan' is cited as evidence that the Prophet ﷺ explicitly stated the wisdom.
This is a dalil naqli for the first wisdom.

Chapter on the Description of Prayer. Some jurists said: When the forehead is lifted from the ground and then he goes into sajdah, both sajdahs are performed. Hasan ibn Ziyad said: When he raises his head from the ground to the extent that air passes between them, then in that case both sajdahs are performed. Hasan ibn Ziyad's statement is closer to the first statement. Muhammad ibn Salamah said: If he raises his head to such an extent that an onlooker thinks he raised his head for the second sajdah, then both sajdahs are performed; otherwise, one sajdah is performed. Imam al-Quduri said: The measure of raising that can be called 'raising' is valid. Because he is still considered in the first sajdah. And if he raises to such an extent that it is closer to the sitting than to the sajdah, then the second sajdah is valid. Qiyas has no role in this. And some said: In the first sajdah, it is indicated that man was created from dust, and in the second, that he will be returned to it. Allah said: 'From it We created you, and into it We will return you.' And Allah knows best.

Several opinions are recorded: some jurists consider the mere lifting of the forehead from the ground sufficient; Hasan ibn Ziyad requires enough space for air to pass; Muhammad ibn Salamah relies on the perception of an onlooker; Imam al-Quduri says any act that can be linguistically called 'raising' suffices. Key Terms
ترغيما لشيطان (targhīman li-shayṭān): A phrase from a hadith meaning 'to humiliate the devil', given as the wisdom behind two sajdahs.
توقيفي (tawqīfī): Prescriptive; a matter determined by revelation without rational basis.

Rising from Sajdah: The Hanafi vs. Shafi'i Dispute on the Jalsah
Inter-madhhab dispute on rising from sajdah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on rising from sajdah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the evidence presented.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school stands directly from sajdah; the jalsah is rejected as a bid'ah in prayer.

This lesson examines a classic ikhtilaf between the Hanafis and Shafi'is on a subtle point of prayer: whether to sit briefly before standing. The Hanafi school, relying on the practice of the Prophet and Companions, holds that one rises on the balls of the feet without any pause. The Shafi'i school, citing another hadith, recommends a brief sitting. Understanding this dispute illustrates how different textual evidence and interpretive principles produce divergent rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the specific ruling from al-Quduri and al-Hidayah: the worshiper stands directly on the balls of the feet without sitting or using hands.
This is the mustahab (recommended) practice according to the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
State that Imam al-Shafi'i recommends a brief sitting (jalsah) before standing, using the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith.
The Shafi'i consider this a sunnah.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
Look at the hadith of Abu Hurairah that the Prophet rose on the balls of his feet, and the practice of Umar, Ali, and other companions.
This is a dalil naqli (textual evidence).
4
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Consider the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith that the Prophet sat before standing.
This is also a dalil naqli.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi ta'wil: the Shafi'i hadith is specific to the Prophet's old age. Also the rational argument: prayer is not for rest, so a sitting of rest (qa'dat istirahah) is unwarranted.
This shows how the Hanafi school prioritizes certain principles over apparent meanings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سجدہ سے قیام کی طرف جانے کا طریقہ
قال فاذا اطمأن ساجدا كبر وقد ذكرناه و استوی قائما على صدور قدميه ولا يقعد ولا يعتمد بيديه على الارض وقال الشافعى يجلس جلسة خفيفة ثم ينهض معتمد اعلى الارض لان النبي عليه السلام فعل ذلك ولما حديث أبي هريرة ان النبى عليه السلام كان ينهض فى الصلوة على صدور قدميه ومارواه محمول على حالة الكبر ولان هذه قعدة استراحة والصلوة ما وضعت لها

باب صفۃ الصلوة
تشریح فرمایا کہ جب سجدہ کی حالت میں اطمینان کرلے تو کھڑا ہونے کے لئے تکبیر کہے۔ دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی یعنی ان النبي كان يكبر عند كل خفض ورفع صاحب عنایہ نے لکھا کہ مصنف کو اپنی عادت کے مطابق سابق میں مذکور حدیث کی طرف اشارہ کرنے کے لئے ماروینا کہنا چاہئے تھا لیکن ہو سکتا ہے کہ گذشتہ مسئلہ میں اس حدیث کی طرف اشارہ کرنے کے لئے لما روینا کہا تھا اور اب یہاں اس لما روینا کی طرف وقد ذکرنا سے اشارہ کیا گیا ہو۔
امام قدوری نے کہا کہ سجدہ ثانیہ سے فراغت کے بعد اپنے پنجوں کے بل سیدھا کھڑا ہو جائے ۔ نہ بیٹھے اور نہ اپنے ہاتھوں سے زمین پر ٹیک لگائے اگر عذر نہ ہو تو یہ مستحب ہے۔ حضرت امام شافعی نے کہا کہ ہلکا سا جلسہ کرے پھر زمین پر سہارا دے کر اٹھ جائے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل مالک بن الحویرث کی حدیث ہے ان النبي كان اذا رفع راسه من السجود قعد ثم نهض يعنى حضور جب اپنا سر سجدہ سے اٹھاتے تو بیٹھ جاتے پھر اٹھتے ہماری دلیل حضرت ابو ہریرہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کی حدیث ہے۔ ان النبي كان ينهض في الصلوة على صدر : قدميه، یعنی حضور پر نماز میں اپنے پنجوں کے بل اٹھتے تھے۔
اور امام شعمی سے مروی ہے قال كان عمر و على واصحاب النبي ينهضون في الصلوة على صدور اقدامهم امام شعمی کہتے ہیں کہ حضرت عمر، حضرت علی اور اصحاب رسول اللہ پر نماز کے اندر اپنے قدموں کے بل اٹھتے تھے ۔ اور رہی وہ حدیث جس کو امام شافعی کے استدلال میں پیش کیا گیا ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ حدیث بڑھاپے کی حالت پر محمول ہے یعنی لڑھاپے کے زمانے میں آپ نے ایسا کیا ہے ہماری طرف سے عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ بیٹھنا استراحت کے لئے ہے اور نماز استراحت اور آرام کے لئے وضع نہیں کی گئی اس لئے یہ قعدہ نہ کرے۔
Method of going from sajdah to standing. He said: When he is tranquil in sajdah, he says the takbir, and we have mentioned it. And he stands upright on the balls of his feet, and he does not sit, and he does not support himself with his hands on the ground. Al-Shafi'i said: He sits briefly, then rises supporting himself on the ground, because the Prophet ﷺ did so. Our proof is the hadith of Abu Hurairah that the Prophet ﷺ used to rise in prayer on the balls of his feet. And what he (al-Shafi'i) narrated is carried on the state of old age. And because this is a sitting of rest, and prayer was not instituted for rest. Translation: He said: Then when he is tranquil in the state of sajdah, he says the takbir, and we have mentioned it. And he stands straight on his toes, and he does not sit, and he does not support with his hands on the ground. Imam al-Shafi'i said: He should sit briefly, then stand up supporting on the ground, because the Prophet ﷺ did so. Our proof is the hadith of Abu Hurairah that the Prophet used to rise in prayer on his toes. And that hadith which al-Shafi'i narrated is carried on the state of old age. And because this is a sitting of rest, prayer was not instituted for rest. Explanation: Imam Quduri said: After finishing the second sajdah, he stands straight on his toes, does not sit, and does not support with his hands on the ground; if there is no excuse, this is mustahabb. Imam al-Shafi'i said: He should do a light sitting, then stand supporting on the ground. Al-Shafi'i's proof is the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith that the Prophet, when he raised his head from sajdah, he would sit then stand. Our proof is the hadith of Abu Hurairah that the Prophet used to rise in prayer on the balls of his feet. And it is narrated from Ibn Shihab? that Umar, Ali, and the Companions of the Prophet used to rise in prayer on the balls of their feet. As for the hadith presented by al-Shafi'i, the answer is that it is carried on the state of old age; a rational proof from our side is that this sitting is for rest, and prayer was not instituted for rest, so this sitting should not be done.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the method of rising from sajdah to standing. The Hanafi position, stated by Imam al-Quduri and al-Hidayah, is that one should stand up directly on the balls of the feet without sitting or using hands for support. This is based on the hadith of Abu Hurairah that the Prophet ﷺ would rise on the balls of his feet. Additional support comes from the practice of Umar, Ali, and other Companions. Al-Shafi'i argues for a brief sitting (jalsah) before standing, citing the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith that the Prophet would sit then stand. The Hanafi response is that the Shafi'i hadith is specific to the Prophet's old age when he needed extra rest, and the principle is that prayer was not prescribed for rest. The author concludes that the sitting (qadat istirahah) is not part of the prayer. The relied-upon Hanafi position is to stand directly without sitting.

Key Terms
جلسة خفيفة / قعدة استراحة (jalsah khafīfah / qa‘dah istirāḥah): A brief sitting pause after the second sajdah before standing; the Shafi'i school considers it recommended, but the Hanafi school rejects it.
صدور قدميه (ṣudūr qadamayh): The balls of the feet; the Hanafi method of standing up is to rise on the balls of the feet without using hands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on sitting briefly (jalsah) after the second sajdah before standing?
A) It is recommended (mustahabb).
B) It is obligatory (wajib).
C) It is not done; one stands directly on the balls of the feet.
D) It is allowed only if one is old.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects the jalsah (brief sitting) after sajdah; one must stand directly on the balls of the feet because prayer is not for rest.

The Second Rak'ah: Repetition of Arkan with Omission of Istiftah and Ta'awwudh
Ruling that the second rak'ah repeats the arkan except for istiftah and ta'awwudh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the actions that are repeated and omitted in the second rak'ah according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The second rak'ah repeats all pillars except the opening supplication and ta'awwudh, which are prescribed only once.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling for the second rak'ah of the obligatory prayer as stated in Al-Hidayah. The second rak'ah mirrors the first in all integral actions (arkan) but excludes the opening supplication (istiftah) and the seeking of refuge (ta'awwudh). This distinction is based on the transmitted practice of the Prophet. Understanding this pattern is essential for correctly performing the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base principle
The second rak'ah repeats the first rak'ah in all arkan (pillars).
The proof is that arkan are repeated by nature.
2
Recognize the exception
Istiftah and ta'awwudh are not repeated in the second rak'ah.
They are prescribed only once for the entire prayer.
3
Understand the reasoning
Companions narrated the Prophet's prayer showing these supplications were said only once.
4
Apply the ruling
When beginning the second rak'ah, start directly with al-Fatihah without any preceding supplication.

دوسری رکعت مکمل کرنے کی کیفیت
ويفعل في الركعة الثانية مثل ما فعل في الركعة الأولى لأنه تكرار الأركان إلا أنه لا يستفتح ولا يتعوذ لأنهما لم يشرعا إلا مرة واحدة
ترجمہ اور دوسری رکعت میں اس کی مثل کرے جو پہلی رکعت میں کیا کیونکہ وہ ارکان کا تکرار ہے مگر یہ کہ سبحانک اللھم اور اعوذ باللہ نہ پڑھے اس لئے کہ یہ دونوں صرف ایک بار مشروع ہوئے۔ تشریح رکعت ادنی سے فراغت کے بعد نماز پڑھنے والا رکعت ثانیہ پڑھے گا اور رکعت ثانیہ میں وہ سب کام کرے گا جو رکعت اولی میں کیا ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ رکعت ثانیہ میں ارکان کا تکرار ہے اور تکرار اول کے اعادہ کا تقاضا کرتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہا گیا کہ رکعت ثانیہ میں اس کے مثل کرے جو پہلی رکعت میں کیا ہے ہاں اتنا فرق ضرور ہے کہ دوسری رکعت میں نہ سبحانک اللھم پڑھے اور نہ اعوذ بالله پڑھے کیونکہ یہ دونوں باتیں ایک ہی مرتبہ مشروع ہوئیں ہیں اس لئے کہ جن حضرات صحابہ نے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کی نماز کو روایت کیا ہے انہوں نے ان چیزوں کو صرف ایک مرتبہ روایت کیا ہے۔
Method of completing the second rak'ah. And he does in the second rak'ah like what he did in the first rak'ah because it is a repetition of the arkan, except that he does not recite the opening supplication (istiftah) nor ta'awwudh because both are prescribed only once. Translation: And in the second rak'ah, he does like what he did in the first rak'ah, because it is a repetition of the arkan, except that he does not recite Subhanaka Allahumma and A'udhu billah, because these two are prescribed only once. Explanation: After finishing the first rak'ah, the worshipper will pray the second rak'ah, and in the second rak'ah he will do all that he did in the first rak'ah. The proof is that the second rak'ah is a repetition of the arkan, and repetition requires repeating the first. Hence it is said that in the second rak'ah he should do like what he did in the first rak'ah. However, this difference is necessary: in the second rak'ah he does not recite Subhanaka Allahumma nor A'udhu billah, because these two things are prescribed only once, for the Companions who narrated the Prophet's prayer only narrated these things once.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for the second rak'ah: it is essentially a repetition of the first rak'ah in all its integral actions (arkan). The proof given is that arkan are repeated by nature. However, there is one exception: the opening supplication (Subhanaka Allahumma) and the seeking of refuge (A'udhu billah) are not recited again in the second rak'ah because they are prescribed only once at the beginning of the prayer. This is based on the transmitted practice of the Companions who narrated the Prophet's prayer. Thus, the second rak'ah includes al-Fatihah, a surah, bowing, prostration, etc., but does not include the initial praise and refuge-seeking.

Key Terms
استفتاح (istiftāḥ): The opening supplication (Subhanaka Allahumma) recited at the beginning of the first rak'ah; not repeated in subsequent rak'ahs.
تعوذ (ta‘awwudh): The phrase 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' (I seek refuge with Allah from the accursed devil); recited only in the first rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The second rak'ah omits the opening supplication and ta'awwudh.
C) The second rak'ah omits al-Fatihah.
D) There is no difference.

Key Takeaway
In the second rak'ah, all arkan are repeated except the istiftah and ta'awwudh, which are prescribed once per prayer.

Standing from Prostration: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on standing from prostration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on standing from prostration, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and evaluate the Hanafi response using textual and rational proofs.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds that standing directly on the balls of the feet after prostration is mustahabb, as prayer is not intended for rest.

This lesson examines a classic difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the method of standing after prostration. Imam Quduri presents the Hanafi view as standing directly without sitting or using hands, while Imam al-Shafi'i recommends a brief sitting before rising. Understanding the proofs and their interpretation is key to appreciating how both schools derive rulings from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two positions
Recognize that the act is al-nuhud (rising from prostration) and note the Hanafi view (stand directly on feet) and Shafi'i view (sit briefly then rise).
The Hanafi position is stated by Imam Quduri.
2
State the Hanafi proof
The primary dalil is the hadith of Abu Hurayrah that the Prophet used to rise on the balls of his feet. Also, an athar from al-Sha'bi reports that 'Umar, 'Ali, and the Companions did the same.
These are ahad hadiths, zanni in thubut and dalala.
3
State the Shafi'i proof
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith that the Prophet sat briefly before standing.
This hadith is also ahad.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school interprets the Shafi'i hadith as applying to the Prophet's old age, when he needed rest. The rational argument is that sitting is for rest, but prayer is not prescribed for rest.
Thus, the jalsah is only allowed with an excuse (e.g., old age).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In Hanafi fiqh, a worshipper without excuse stands directly; in Shafi'i fiqh, he performs the jalsah. The practical difference is in the prayer posture.
This difference does not affect the validity of the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نماز استراحت کے واسطے وضع نہیں کی گئی ہے۔
باب صفۃ الصلوة
تشریح فرمایا کہ جب سجدہ کی حالت میں اطمینان کرلے تو کھڑا ہونے کے لئے تکبیر کہے۔ دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی یعنی ان النبي كان يكبر عند كل خفض ورفع صاحب عنایہ نے لکھا کہ مصنف کو اپنی عادت کے مطابق سابق میں مذکور حدیث کی طرف اشارہ کرنے کے لئے ماروینا کہنا چاہئے تھا لیکن ہو سکتا ہے کہ گذشتہ مسئلہ میں اس حدیث کی طرف اشارہ کرنے کے لئے لما روینا کہا تھا اور اب یہاں اس لما روینا کی طرف وقد ذکرنا سے اشارہ کیا گیا ہو۔
امام قدوری نے کہا کہ سجدہ ثانیہ سے فراغت کے بعد اپنے پنجوں کے بل سیدھا کھڑا ہو جائے ۔ نہ بیٹھے اور نہ اپنے ہاتھوں سے زمین پر ٹیک لگائے اگر عذر نہ ہو تو یہ مستحب ہے۔ حضرت امام شافعی نے کہا کہ ہلکا سا جلسہ کرے پھر زمین پر سہارا دے کر اٹھ جائے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل مالک بن الحویرث کی حدیث ہے ان النبي كان اذا رفع راسه من السجود قعد ثم نهض يعنى حضور جب اپنا سر سجدہ سے اٹھاتے تو بیٹھ جاتے پھر اٹھتے ہماری دلیل حضرت ابو ہریرہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کی حدیث ہے۔ ان النبي كان ينهض في الصلوة على صدر : قدميه، یعنی حضور پر نماز میں اپنے پنجوں کے بل اٹھتے تھے۔
اور امام شعمی سے مروی ہے قال كان عمر و على واصحاب النبي ينهضون في الصلوة على صدور اقدامهم امام شعمی کہتے ہیں کہ حضرت عمر، حضرت علی اور اصحاب رسول اللہ پر نماز کے اندر اپنے قدموں کے بل اٹھتے تھے ۔ اور رہی وہ حدیث جس کو امام شافعی کے استدلال میں پیش کیا گیا ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ حدیث بڑھاپے کی حالت پر محمول ہے یعنی لڑھاپے کے زمانے میں آپ نے ایسا کیا ہے ہماری طرف سے عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ بیٹھنا استراحت کے لئے ہے اور نماز استراحت اور آرام کے لئے وضع نہیں کی گئی اس لئے یہ قعدہ نہ کرے۔
Prayer was not prescribed for rest. Chapter on Description of Prayer. Explanation: When one settles in prostration, he should say takbir for standing. The proof has passed earlier, i.e., the Prophet used to say takbir at every lowering and raising. The author of 'Inayah wrote that the author, as per his habit, should have said 'ma rawaina' to refer to the previously mentioned hadith, but it is possible that in the previous issue he said 'lama rawaina' as a reference, and here he indicates that with 'wa qad dhakarna'. Imam Quduri said: After finishing the second prostration, he should stand straight on the balls of his feet, not sit, and not lean on his hands, if there is no excuse, this is mustahabb. Imam al-Shafi'i said: He should make a slight pause (jalsah), then rise by supporting himself on the ground. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith: The Prophet, when he raised his head from prostration, sat down then rose. Our proof is the hadith of Abu Hurayrah: The Prophet used to rise in prayer on the balls of his feet. And from Imam al-Sha'bi is narrated: 'Umar, 'Ali, and the Companions of the Prophet used to rise in prayer on the balls of their feet. As for the hadith used by al-Shafi'i, the response is that it is interpreted for old age; the Prophet did that in old age. Our rational proof is that this sitting is for rest, and prayer was not prescribed for rest, so he should not sit.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the method of standing after prostration in prayer. The Hanafi position, as stated by Imam Quduri, is that one should stand directly on the balls of the feet without sitting and without leaning on hands. This is mustahabb (recommended) unless there is an excuse. The Shafi'i school, represented by Imam al-Shafi'i, holds that one should sit briefly (jalsah) before rising, often supporting oneself with the hands. The proof for the Shafi'i position is a hadith from Malik ibn al-Huwayrith that the Prophet sat briefly before standing. The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) the narration from Abu Hurayrah and Imam al-Sha'bi shows that the Prophet and the Companions rose directly on the feet; (2) the Shafi'i hadith is interpreted as applying to the Prophet's old age when he needed to rest, but the essence of prayer is not rest. The author also notes a textual comment by the commentator on the phrasing of the proof.

Key Terms
جلسة (jalsah): A brief sitting between prostration and standing, as claimed by Shafi'i
النهوض (al-nuhud): Rising from prostration to standing

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the recommended method of standing from prostration?
A) Sit briefly then rise with hand support
B) Stand directly on the balls of the feet without sitting
C) Rise by leaning on the hands only
D) Wait a moment in prostration then stand

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that after prostration, one should stand directly on the balls of the feet; a brief sitting (jalsah) is only permitted for an excuse, as prayer is not meant for rest.

Raising Hands in Prayer: Only at Takbirat al-ihram (Hanafi View)
Presents the Hanafi view against raising hands except at the opening takbir, with proofs and refutation of Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on raising hands (raf' al-yadayn) in prayer, cite the Hanafi proof, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the concept of abrogation (naskh).

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, raising hands during prayer is only at the opening takbir; any other raising is abrogated (mansukh).

The practice of raising hands (raf' al-yadayn) during prayer is a well-known point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that hands are raised only once at takbirat al-ihram, and provides the evidence from the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas and the practice of Ibn al-Zubayr, arguing that the hadith of Ibn 'Umar which supports the Shafi'i view is abrogated. Understanding this dispute helps clarify how Hanafi usul applies naskh (abrogation) to reconcile conflicting hadiths.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What is the exact Hanafi ruling on raising hands? Only at the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram).
2
State the Shafi'i position and their proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that hands are also raised at ruku' and after. Their proof is the hadith of Ibn 'Umar.
3
Analyse the Hanafi proof (Ibn 'Abbas hadith)
The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: 'Do not raise hands except in seven places.' Ruku' is not among them.
4
Analyse the Shafi'i proof and the Hanafi response (naskh)
The Hanafi response is that the hadith of Ibn 'Umar is abrogated (mansukh) – it was early practice but later abandoned, as reported by Ibn al-Zubayr.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In Hanafi prayer, hands are raised once per rakat; in Shafi'i, they are raised three times. This is the tangible difference in the prayer.

Ruling on raising the hands, statements of jurists and proofs. And he does not raise his hands except at the first takbir, contrary to al-Shafi'i regarding ruku' and rising from it, due to his statement: 'We do not raise the hands except in seven places: takbirat al-iftitah, takbir al-qunut, takbirat al-'idayn, and the four mentioned in Hajj.' And the hadith reported about raising is interpreted as referring to the beginning. Similarly narrated from Ibn al-Zubayr. Translation: And he does not raise his hands except at the takbirat al-ihram. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees for going into ruku' and raising the head from it. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is the hadith of Ibn 'Umar: The Prophet used to raise his hands at ruku' and when raising his head from ruku'. Our proof is the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: 'Do not raise the hands except in seven places' - the hadith from Ibn 'Abbas that the Prophet said: 'Hands are not raised except in seven places: takbirat al-ihram, takbirat al-'idayn, takbir al-qunut, takbir 'Arafah, takbir Safa and Marwah, takbirat al-jamarat, and takbir al-Islam.' The hadith of Ibn 'Umar will be interpreted as applying to the beginning of Islam, i.e., at the beginning of Islam the ruling was to raise hands, then it was abrogated. Similarly, 'Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr narrated that he saw a man praying in the Sacred Mosque raising his hands at ruku' and at raising the head from ruku', and after he finished, Ibn al-Zubayr told him: 'Do not do this, for this is something the Messenger of Allah did then abandoned it.' The commentators of Hidayah (Inayah, Fath al-Qadir, Kifayah) mention an interesting anecdote: Once in the Sacred Mosque, Imam al-Awza'i met Imam Abu Hanifah and said: 'What is the matter with the people of Iraq? They raise hands at ruku' and at rising from it?' and his own...
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the issue of raising hands (raf' al-yadayn) during prayer. The Hanafi position, attributed to Imam Abu Hanifah, is that hands are raised only at the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram). Imam al-Shafi'i holds that hands should also be raised at the time of going into ruku' and when rising from ruku'. The Shafi'i proof is the hadith of Ibn 'Umar. The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas stating that hands are raised only in seven specific places (e.g., takbirat al-ihram, 'Eid takbirs, qunut, etc.). The Hanafi response argues that the hadith of Ibn 'Umar is abrogated: it was practiced in early Islam but later abandoned, as evidenced by the narration from Ibn al-Zubayr who saw a man raising hands and told him not to, because the Prophet himself did it then left it. The text also includes a famous anecdote from the Hidayah commentators regarding a debate between Imam Abu Hanifah and Imam al-Awza'i on this very issue.

Key Terms
رفع الیدین (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands during prayer
منسوخ (mansukh): Abrogated; a ruling that was once applicable but later cancelled by a later revelation or Prophetic action

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) At the opening takbir and at ruku'
B) Only at the opening takbir
C) At the opening takbir, at ruku', and after ruku'
D) Only at ruku'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that raising hands during prayer is limited to takbirat al-ihram, as the hadiths indicating otherwise are abrogated.

Hands in Prayer: The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on Raf' al-Yadayn
Dispute on raising hands with proofs and resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on raising hands in prayer, identify the proofs used by both Hanafi and Shafi'i schools, and apply the Hanafi principle of ta'arud to reconcile conflicting proofs.

Core Idea
When two hadiths contradict, both are dropped and we seek a third explicit proof.

The act of raising hands during prayer (raf' al-yadayn) is a well-known point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. This lesson unpacks the exact Hanafi ruling, the proofs each school relies on, and the unique Hanafi method of resolving conflicting evidence — a method that prioritizes textual consistency and the practice of narrators.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed act
What is the specific act under dispute? Is it the raising of hands at the opening takbir, at ruku', or after ruku'? The Hanafi school says hands are raised only at the opening takbir; the Shafi'i school adds ruku' and after ruku'.
The dispute is not about whether to raise hands at all, but about additional instances.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi position: hands are raised only at takbir al-tahrimah. The primary proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'Do not raise hands except in seven places.' Also the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet raised hands only at the opening takbir.
The Hanafi school considers this explicit prohibition (nahy) as binding.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
The Shafi'i position: hands are raised at ruku' and after ruku' as well. Their proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'The Prophet used to raise his hands at ruku' and when raising his head from ruku'.'
This hadith is well-known and accepted in authenticity.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response: ta'arud (contradiction) and tarjih
The Hanafis argue that the two hadiths contradict each other: Ibn Abbas prohibits, Ibn Umar permits. When two equal proofs conflict, both are dropped (tasqut al-dalilayn) and a third proof is sought. Here, the third proof is the explicit command in the hadith of Ibn Abbas, which is more specific and also supported by the practice of Ibn Umar himself (as witnessed by Mujahid).
The Hanafi methodology of ta'arud is based on usul al-fiqh: if reconciliation is impossible, both are set aside and a stronger or third dalil is used.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position is that hands are raised only at the opening takbir. This is the ruling for fatwa and practice in the Hanafi school.
Later Hanafi texts consider raising hands elsewhere as makruh tanzihi, but the core ruling remains sunnah only at takbir al-tahrimah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يرفع يديه إلا في التكبيرة الأولى خلافا للشافعي في الركوع وفي الرفع منه لقوله عليه السلام: لا ترفع الأيدي إلا في سبع مواطن: تكبيرة الافتتاح، وتكبيرة القنوت، وتكبيرات العيدين، وذكر الأربع في الحج. والذي يروى من الرفع محمول على الابتداء كذا نقل عن ابن الزبير. حضرت امام اعظم: سوائے تکبیر تحریمہ کے کسی تکبیر میں ہاتھ نہ اٹھائے. امام شافعی نے کہا: تکبیر تحریمہ کے علاوہ اور دو تکبیروں میں ہاتھ اٹھائے: ایک رکوع میں جاتے وقت، دوم رکوع سے سر اٹھاتے وقت. امام شافعی کی دلیل ابن عمر کی حدیث: ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يرفع يديه عند الركوع وعند رفع الرأس من الركوع. ہماری دلیل ابن عباس کی حدیث: لا ترفع الأيدي إلا في سبع مواطن... ثم ذكر المواطن. ثم ذكر قصة الإمام أبي حنيفة مع الأوزاعي: قال الإمام أبو حنيفة: حدثني حماد عن إبراهيم عن علقمة عن عبد الله بن مسعود أن النبي كان يرفع يديه عند تكبيرة الافتتاح ثم لا يعود. قال الأوزاعي: عجبا لأبي حنيفة، أحدث بحديث الزهري عن سالم عن ابن عمر ويحدثني بحديث حماد عن إبراهيم عن علقمة عن ابن مسعود؟ فقال أبو حنيفة: أما حماد فكان أفقه من الزهري، وإبراهيم كان أفقه من سالم، ولولا سبق ابن عمر لقلت بأن علقمة أفقه منه، وأما عبد الله فعبد الله. فثبت أن حديث ابن عمر وحديث ابن مسعود متعارضان فسقطا، ورجع إلى قوله عليه السلام: لا ترفع الأيدي إلا في سبع مواطن. وعلاوة على ذلك حديث ابن عمر ساقط لأن مجاهدا قال: صليت خلف ابن عمر سنتين فلم أره يرفع يديه إلا عند افتتاح الصلاة، وقاعدة: الراوي إذا عمل بخلاف روايته سقطت روايته. (نورالانوار)
And he does not raise his hands except in the first takbir, contrary to al-Shafi'i regarding the bowing and raising from it, because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'Do not raise hands except in seven places: the opening takbir, the qunoot takbir, the Eid takbirs, and he mentioned four in Hajj.' And what is narrated of raising is interpreted as initial, similarly transmitted from Ibn al-Zubayr. Imam A'zam: Except for the takbir of tahrimah, do not raise hands in any takbir. Imam Shafi'i said: Besides the takbir of tahrimah, raise hands in two other takbirs: one when going into ruku', and second when raising the head from ruku'. Imam Shafi'i's proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'The Prophet used to raise his hands at ruku' and when raising his head from ruku'.' Our proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'Do not raise hands except in seven places...' Then he mentioned the places. Then he mentioned the story of Imam Abu Hanifa with al-Awza'i. Then it is established that the hadith of Ibn Umar and the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud contradict each other, so they both fall, and we refer to his saying: 'Do not raise hands except in seven places.' Moreover, the hadith of Ibn Umar is dropped because Mujahid said: 'I prayed behind Ibn Umar for two years and did not see him raise his hands except at the opening of prayer,' and the rule is that when a narrator acts contrary to his narration, his narration is dropped.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage addresses the dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding raising the hands (raf' al-yadayn) during prayer. The Hanafi position, as stated, is that hands are raised only at the takbir al-tahrimah (opening takbir). Imam Abu Hanifa and his school consider raising hands at ruku' and after ruku' as not established. The author first states the ruling from the matn, then presents the Shafi'i position and its proof based on the hadith of Ibn Umar. The Hanafi proof relies on the hadith of Ibn Abbas enumerating seven specific occasions for raising hands, and on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud transmitted through Imam Abu Hanifa's chain. The famous debate between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam al-Awza'i is narrated to illustrate that Hanafis prioritize the fiqh (juridical understanding) of the narrators over mere seniority in transmission. The passage then explains that the conflicting hadiths of Ibn Umar and Ibn Mas'ud are mutually contradictory and therefore both are dropped, leaving the explicit command of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Ibn Abbas as the binding evidence. Finally, it notes that the hadith of Ibn Umar is further weakened because Ibn Umar himself was not observed practicing it by Mujahid, and a narrator acting against his own narration invalidates it. This lesson demonstrates the Hanafi usul principle of preferring the more reliable and consistent narration, and the importance of 'amal (practice) in verifying hadith.

Key Terms
رفع الیدین (raf' al-yadayn): The act of raising hands during prayer, specifically the positioning of hands to the ears or shoulders.
تکبیر تحریمہ (takbir al-tahrimah): The first takbir that commences the prayer, marking the prohibition of worldly acts.
تعارض (ta'arud): Apparent contradiction between two proofs, leading to both being dropped or one being preferred via tarjih.

Key Takeaway

Posture for Sitting in Prayer and Difference for Women
Description of sitting posture with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi sunnah sitting posture for men and women in prayer and explain the proof and reasoning for the difference.

Core Idea
Men sit iftirash; women sit tajahhul for modesty; both are sunnah muakkadah.

This lesson details the correct sitting posture (qafdah) after the second sajdah, based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as reported by Aisha and Wa'il ibn Hujr. The Hanafi school distinguishes between men and women, prescribing iftirash for men and tajahhul for women for greater concealment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the sitting posture after the second sajdah in the second rak'ah. Its ruling is sunnah muakkadah.
Deviation without necessity is makruh tanzihi.
2
Locate the dalil
The proofs are the hadith of Aisha describing the Prophet's sitting and the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr.
Both are ahad hadith, but sufficient for sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The description is taken as the sunnah to follow; the Prophet's practice establishes the recommended posture.
Direct imitation of the Prophet's action.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) prescribe the same iftirash for both men and women, without differentiation.
Hanafi relies on the principle of satr for women.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi based on the hadith and the reasoning of modesty.
Women's posture is more concealing.

And when he raises his head from the second prostration in the second rak'ah, he spreads his left foot and sits on it, and erects the right foot upright, and points his fingers towards the qibla. Thus Aisha described the sitting of the Messenger of Allah in prayer, and he placed his hands on his thighs and spread his fingers and recited the tashahhud. This is narrated in the hadith of Wa'il, and because it involves directing the fingers of the hands towards the qibla. And if the person is a woman, she sits on her left buttock and brings out her feet from the right side, because it is more concealing for her.

Commentary
This passage details the sunnah posture for sitting (qafdah) in prayer, specifically after the second sajdah of the second rak'ah (the first sitting in a 4-rak'ah prayer or the final sitting). The ruling is derived from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as described by Aisha and from the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr. For men, the sunnah is iftirash: sitting on the left foot while keeping the right foot upright (nasb), with toes pointing towards the qibla. Hands are placed on the thighs with fingers spread. For women, the posture is different: she sits on her left buttock (tajahhul) and brings both feet out to the right side, as this is more modest (astar). The text provides the reasoning for the finger direction: to face the qibla. This difference between men and women is specific to the Hanafi school, based on the principle of concealment for women.

تجہل (tajahhul): Sitting on the left buttock with feet brought out to the right side, specific to women in prayer.
نصب (nasb): Erecting the right foot vertically with toes pointing towards the qibla.
تشہد (tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited while sitting in prayer.
