The Dispute Over Raising Hands in Prayer: Hanafi vs. Awza'i Guidance
Dispute between Hanafi and Awza'i over raising hands in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on raf' al-yadayn and evaluate the Hanafi response to the opposing hadith of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
When two hadiths contradict, we follow narrators with deeper fiqh and drop any narration contradicted by the narrator's own practice.

Raising hands during prayer (raf' al-yadayn) is a well-known point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. This passage delves into the original dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam al-Awza'i, focusing on how we weigh conflicting hadith evidence. Understanding this disagreement is key to appreciating the Hanafi method of tarjih based on the fiqh of narrators and the principle that a narrator's own practice can invalidate his report.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting hadiths
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (via Hammad, Ibrahim, Alqamah) states the Prophet raised hands only at takbirat al-ihram. The hadith of Ibn Umar (via Zuhri, Salim) says he raised at multiple points.
Both are fi'li hadiths (actions of the Prophet).
2
Analyze the grounds for preference
Awza'i favored Ibn Umar's hadith due to higher chain (ulu al-isnad). Imam Abu Hanifa countered by highlighting the fiqh of the narrators: Hammad > Zuhri, Ibrahim > Salim, Alqamah = Ibn Umar, and Ibn Mas'ud is unparalleled.
The Hanafi school prioritizes fiqh over chain height.
3
Apply the principle of ta'arud
Since both hadiths contradict in apparent meaning, they drop (saqit) and we refer to the general hadith 'La tarfa' al-aydiya illa fi sab'i mawatin' (do not raise hands except in seven places).
This resolves the contradiction by falling back on a broader textual evidence.
4
Examine the additional reason for dropping Ibn Umar's hadith
Mujahid observed Ibn Umar praying for two years and only saw him raise hands at the beginning. The rule is: if a narrator acts against his own narration, the narration is saqit.
This strengthens the Hanafi position.
5
State the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafis raise hands only at takbirat al-ihram; Shafi'is raise at multiple points (opening, before ruku, after ruku, after qiyam).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صفۃ الصلوة اٹھاتے وقت اپنے ہاتھ نہیں اٹھاتے حالانکہ مجھ کو زهرى عن سالم عن ابن عمر یہ حدیث پہنچی ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم ان موقعوں پر اپنے ہاتھ اٹھاتے تھے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا حدثنی حماد عن ابراهيم عن علقمة عن عبد الله بن مسعود رضی الله تعالى عنه أن النبي كان يرفع يديه عند تكبيرة الافتتاح ثم لا يعود يعنى حضور تکبیر تحریمہ کے وقت اپنے ہاتھ اٹھاتے تھے پھر اعادہ نہیں کرتے تھے ۔ امام اوزاعی نے کہا امام ابو حنیفہ پر حیرت ہے میں حدیث بیان کر رہا ہوں حدیث زہری عن سالم عن ابن عمر اور وہ حدیث بیان کر رہے ہیں حدیث حماد عن ابراهیم عن عالقمه عن ابن مسعود حاصل یہ کہ اوزاعی نے علو اسناد کا لحاظ کرتے ہوئے حدیث ابن عمر کو تر جیح دی۔ حضرت امام اعظم نے فرمایا ۔ اما حماد فكان افقه من الزهرى وابراهيم كان افقه من سالم ولولا سبق ابن عمر لقلت بان علقمة افقه منه اما عبد الله فعبد الله يعنى حمادز بری کے مقابلہ میں بڑے فقیہ ہیں اور ابراہیم سالم سے افقہ ہیں اور اگر ابن عمر گو تتقدم زمانی حاصل نہ ہوتا تو میں کہتا کہ علقمہ بڑے فقیہ میں ابن عمر کے مقابلہ میں اور رہے عبداللہ تو وہ عبداللہ ہیں یعنی ان کی تو نظیر ہی نہیں حاصل یہ کہ امام ابوحنیفہ نے فقہ روات کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے ابن مسعود کی روایت کو ترجیح دی۔ اس واقعہ سے اتنی بات ثابت ہو گئی کہ رفع یدین کے سلسلہ میں حدیث ابن عمر اور عبداللہ بن مسعود کی حدیث باہم متعارض ہیں اور ان دونوں حدیثوں میں آپ کا فعل بیان کیا گیا ہے پس تعارض کی وجہ سے دونوں ساقط ہو جائیں گی اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول "لا ترفع الايدى الافـي سبع مواطن" الحدیث کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا درآنحالیکہ یہ حدیث مشہور ہے علاوہ ازین ابن عمر کی حدیث ساقط ہے کیونکہ مجاہد نے کہا صلیت خلف ابن عمر سنتين فلم اره يرفع يديه الالافتتاح الصلاة مجاہد نے کہا کہ میں نے دو سال ابن عمر کے پیچھے نماز پڑھی ہے لیکن سوائے تکبیر تحریمہ کے کبھی ان کو ہاتھ اٹھاتے ہوئے نہیں دیکھا اور قاعدہ ہے کہ راوی جب اپنی روایت کے خلاف عمل کرے تو اس کی روایت ساقط ہو جاتی ہے۔ (نورالانوار ) جمعیل عفی عنہ
Chapter on the Description of Prayer: (He) does not raise his hands when getting up, although the hadith of Zuhri from Salim from Ibn Umar has reached me that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to raise his hands at those points. Imam Abu Hanifa said: Hammad narrated to me from Ibrahim from Alqamah from Abdullah ibn Masud (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet used to raise his hands at the opening takbir and then does not repeat. Imam Awzai said: I am amazed at Abu Hanifa; I am narrating a hadith: the hadith of Zuhri from Salim from Ibn Umar, and he is narrating the hadith of Hammad from Ibrahim from Alqamah from Ibn Masud. The result is that Awzai gave preference to the hadith of Ibn Umar by considering the higher chain (ulu al-isnad). Imam Abu Hanifa said: Indeed, Hammad was more knowledgeable in fiqh than Zuhri, and Ibrahim was more knowledgeable than Salim. If it were not for the seniority of Ibn Umar (in time),I would say that Alqamah is more knowledgeable than him. As for Abdullah, he is Abdullah (i.e., unique). Meaning that Imam Abu Hanifa preferred the narration of Ibn Masud by considering the fiqh of the narrators. From this incident, this much is proven: that regarding raising the hands, the hadith of Ibn Umar and the hadith of Abdullah ibn Masud are contradictory. Since they are contradictory, both fall (saqit) and we refer to the saying of the Prophet: "Do not raise hands except in seven places" – while this hadith is well-known. Moreover, the hadith of Ibn Umar is dropped because Mujahid said: I prayed behind Ibn Umar for two years and did not see him raise his hands except at the opening takbir. The rule is that when a narrator acts contrary to his own narration, his narration is dropped. (Nur al-Anwar) – compiled by Jamil, may he be forgiven.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the practice of raising hands (raf' al-yadayn) during prayer. The author opens by stating the Hanafi position: hands are not raised except at the initial takbir (takbirat al-ihram). The narration of Ibn Mas'ud is cited as evidence: the Prophet raised hands only at the opening takbir and did not repeat. Then the objection of Imam al-Awza'i is presented: he has a hadith from Ibn Umar (via Zuhri from Salim) that the Prophet raised hands at multiple points. Awza'i gives preference to this hadith based on the higher chain (ulu al-isnad) – the narrators are closer in time to the Prophet. Imam Abu Hanifa responds by weighing the fiqh (jurisprudential understanding) of the narrators: Hammad is more knowledgeable in fiqh than Zuhri, Ibrahim more knowledgeable than Salim, and Alqamah is at least equal to Ibn Umar, while Abdullah ibn Mas'ud is unparalleled. Thus, the narration of Ibn Mas'ud is preferred. The author then explains that due to the contradiction (ta'arud) between the two hadiths, both are dropped, and we turn to the well-known hadith "Do not raise hands except in seven places." Additionally, the hadith of Ibn Umar is further invalidated because his own practice contradicted his narration: Mujahid observed Ibn Umar praying for two years and saw him raise hands only at the beginning. The principle (qaidah) stated is that when a narrator acts contrary to his own report, that report is dropped (saqit). Thus, the Hanafi position is established and supported.

Key Terms
رفع الیدین (raf' al-yadayn): The act of raising both hands during prayer, usually up to the ears or shoulders, in conjunction with saying Allahu Akbar.
علو اسناد (ulu al-isnad): A high chain of transmission, meaning the narrators are fewer in number and closer in time to the Prophet.
ساقط (saqit): A narration that is dropped or deemed invalid due to a defect, such as contradiction with a stronger evidence or the narrator's own practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, why is the hadith of Ibn Umar regarding raising hands considered saqit (dropped)?
A) Because the chain of Ibn Umar is weak.
B) Because Ibn Umar himself did not practice what he narrated.
C) Because the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud is mutawatir.
D) Because Imam Awza'i rejected it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on raf' al-yadayn is established through careful usul analysis: conflicting hadiths are set aside, and the practice of the narrators themselves is considered decisive.

The Sitting Posture in Prayer (Qa'da) for Men and Women
Description of sitting posture in qa'da

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi recommended sitting posture for men and women during the qa'da in prayer, and explain the proofs from hadith and the rationale of modesty.

Core Idea
The sitting posture in prayer follows the Prophet's example: men sit on the left foot, women sit on the left buttock for modesty.

In this lesson, we examine the sunnah posture for the qa'da (sitting for tashahhud) as described in the Hanafi tradition. The passage details the positions for both men and women, grounding them in the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) as narrated by Aisha and Wail). Understanding these postures helps ensure that our prayer conforms to the recommended prophetic model, with special consideration for women's modesty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its time
The passage describes the posture upon raising the head from the second sajdah of the second rak'ah. This is the first sitting (qa'da) for tashahhud. The ruling applies to every sitting in prayer.
The qa'da occurs after the second sujud in the second rak'ah and in the final rak'ah.
2
Describe the posture for men
Men spread the left foot flat, sit on it, erect the right foot upright, and direct the toes towards the qiblah. Hands are placed on the thighs with fingers spread, also directed towards the qiblah.
This is called iftirash (sitting on the left foot).
3
Identify the proofs (dalil)
The passage cites the hadith of Aisha describing the Prophet's sitting, and the hadith of Wail ibn Hujr confirming it. It also mentions a rational proof (istihsan) because this posture directs the fingers towards the qiblah.
The hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut) but establish the sunnah in this matter.
4
Distinguish the posture for women and reason
Women sit on their left buttock and bring both legs out to the right side. The reason given is modesty (astar laha).
Hanafi school holds that women should adopt a more concealing posture to avoid exposure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قعدہ میں بیٹھنے کی ہیئت واذا رفع رأسه من السجدة الثانية في الركعة الثانية افترش رجاله اليسرى فجلس عليها ونصب اليمني نصبا و وجه اصابعه نحو القبلة هكذا وصفت عائشة قعود رسول الله في الصلوة ووضع يديه على فخذيه وبسط اصابعه وتشهد ويروى ذلك في حديث وائل ولان فيه توجيه اصابع يديه الى القبلة وان كانت امرأة جلست على اليتها اليسرى و اخرجت رجليها من الجانب الايمن لانه أستر لها
The manner of sitting in the qa'da: When he raises his head from the second sajdah in the second rak'ah, he spreads his left foot (lays it flat) and sits on it, and erects his right foot (keeps it upright), and directs his toes towards the qiblah. Thus Aisha described the sitting of the Messenger of Allah in prayer. And he places his hands on his thighs and spreads his fingers, and recites the tashahhud. This is also narrated in the hadith of Wail. And because it involves directing the fingers of his hands towards the qiblah. Commentary
This passage describes the recommended posture for sitting in the qa'da (the sitting for tashahhud) during prayer. The author begins with the position when rising from the second sajdah of the second rak'ah (i.e., after the second rak'ah). The man is to place his left foot flat, sit on it, and keep his right foot upright with toes pointing towards the qiblah. This is based on the description of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) of the Prophet's prayer. Additionally, the hands should be placed on the thighs with fingers spread naturally, not clasped. This is supported by the hadith of Wail ibn Hujr. A rational proof (istihsan) is also given: it allows directing the fingers towards the qiblah, which is a preferred orientation. For a woman, the posture differs: she sits on her left buttock and brings both feet out to the right side. The reason given is that this is more concealing (astar) for her, in line with the principle of modesty for women in prayer.

Key Terms
افترش (iftirash): To spread or lay flat (the left foot) and sit on it. This is the posture for men in qa'da.
نصب (nasb): To erect or keep upright (the right foot) with toes pointing forward.
توجيه اصابع (tawjih asabi'): Directing the fingers (of both hands and feet) towards the qiblah during sitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Preferred Wording of the Tashahhud (Ibn Mas'ud's Version)
Preference for Ibn Mas'ud's tashahhud based on hadith and linguistic analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi preferred wording of the tashahhud, explain the linguistic and legal reasons for its preference, and distinguish it from the version of Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
The command form and linguistic features make Ibn Mas'ud's tashahhud the preferred wording in prayer.

In the Hanafi school, the tashahhud is a wajib act of prayer. While multiple authentic wordings exist, the version taught by the Prophet to Ibn Mas'ud is considered superior. This lesson unpacks the hadith evidence and the linguistic analysis - the command 'qul', the definite article for generality, and the extra waw for renewal - that lead the Hanafi jurists to prefer this wording over that of Ibn Abbas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two tashahhud versions
Read the Arabic text and distinguish the wording of Ibn Mas'ud (starting with 'Al-tahiyyatu lillahi wa al-salawatu...') from that of Ibn Abbas (which adds 'al-mubarakatu' and 'wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuhu').
Both are authentic transmissions, but one is preferred.
2
Examine the hadith proof
Focus on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: the Prophet taught him the tashahhud 'as he taught a surah of the Quran', using a command (amr). Note that Ibn Abbas's version lacks this explicit command.
The command 'qul' (say) is a key indicator.
3
Analyze the linguistic indicators
In Ibn Mas'ud's version, the definite article 'al' in 'al-tahiyyatu' indicates generality (istighraq), encompassing all forms of greetings and praises. The extra 'waw' (and) in 'wa al-salawatu' functions to renew speech (tajdid al-kalam), adding emphasis.
These features make the wording more comprehensive.
4
Understand the practical preference
The Hanafi school holds that taking Ibn Mas'ud's version is better (awla) due to the command (amr) and linguistic superiority. Using Ibn Abbas's version is permissible but less preferred.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the actual recitation in prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و تشهد التحيات لله والصلوات والطيبات السلام علیک ایها النبی...... الى آخره، وهذا تشهد عبد الله مسعود فانه قال اخذ رسول الله بیدى و علمنى التشهد كما كان يعلمنى سورة من القرآن وقال التحيات الله الى اخره والأخذ بهذا اولى من الأخذ بتشهد ابن عباس وهو قوله التحيات المباركة الصلوات الطيبات الله سلام علیک ایها النبی و رحمة الله و بركاته سلام علينا الى اخره لان فيه الامر والاستباب والالف واللام وهما للاستغراق و زيادة الواو وهى لتجديد الكلام كما في التقسم وتاكي التعليم
And the tashahhud: 'Al-tahiyyatu lillahi wa al-salawatu wa al-tayyibatu, al-salamu 'alayka ayyuha al-nabiyyu...' to the end. And this is the tashahhud of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, for he said: The Messenger of Allah took my hand and taught me the tashahhud just as he used to teach me a surah of the Quran, and he said: 'Say: Al-tahiyyatu lillahi...' to the end. And taking this (tashahhud) is better than taking the tashahhud of Ibn Abbas, which is: 'Al-tahiyyatu al-mubarakatu al-salawatu al-tayyibatu lillahi, al-salamu 'alayka ayyuha al-nabiyyu wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuhu, al-salamu 'alayna...' to the end, because in this (Ibn Mas'ud's) there is the command (amr) and recommendation (istihbab), and the alif and lam, which are for generality (istighraq), and the extra waw, which is for renewal of speech (tajdid al-kalam), as in the oath (qasam), and an emphasis on teaching (ta'kid al-ta'lim).
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage discusses the preferred wording of the tashahhud (the testimony recited in the sitting of prayer). The author states that the tashahhud of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, which begins 'Al-tahiyyatu lillahi wa al-salawatu wa al-tayyibatu...', is the one to be taken. This is because Ibn Mas'ud reported that the Prophet taught him this tashahhud personally, just as he taught Quranic surahs, indicating its importance. The alternative tashahhud of Ibn Abbas, which includes 'al-mubarakatu' and 'wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuhu', is also transmitted but is considered less preferred. The reasoning given is linguistic and legal: in the narration of Ibn Mas'ud, the Prophet used the command form (amr: 'qul' – say), which in Hanafi usul indicates obligation (wujub) and at least recommendation (istihbab). Additionally, the article 'al' (alif-lam) in 'al-tahiyyatu' indicates generality (istighraq), encompassing all acts of praise. The extra 'waw' (and) in 'wa al-salawatu' functions to renew the speech (tajdid al-kalam), similar to its use in oaths, and it emphasizes the teaching. Therefore, the version of Ibn Mas'ud is considered the more complete and preferred wording.

Key Terms
تشہد (tashahhud): The testimony of faith (shahadah) recited in the sitting position of prayer, including the declaration of Allah's greatness, greetings to the Prophet, and the shahadah.
امر (amr): A command form (imperative) in Arabic usage. Here, the command 'qul' (say) indicates that the action is at least recommended, and in Hanafi usul, it indicates obligation unless there is a contrary indicator.
استغراق (istighraq): Generality or comprehensiveness. The definite article 'al' in 'al-tahiyyatu' encompasses all types of greetings and praises.
واو (waw): The Arabic letter 'waw' meaning 'and'. Here, it is used to renew speech (tajdid al-kalam), similar to its use in oaths.
استحباب (istihbab): Recommendation. The command (amr) here indicates both wujub (obligation) and istihbab (recommendation) depending on context. In this case, the preferred wording is recommended (mandub).
اولى (awla): Better, more appropriate. Used to indicate preference without implying exclusivity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because Ibn Abbas's version is not authentic.
D) Because the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud is shorter and easier.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prefers the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud because the Prophet taught it with a command and it has superior linguistic features, making it the most comprehensive and emphatic wording for prayer.

The Hanafi Sitting Posture (Qa'dah) in Prayer
Describes the manner of sitting and hand placement during the first tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the recommended sitting posture and hand placement during the first tashahhud according to the Hanafi school, including the pointing gesture, and identify the proofs for each element.

Core Idea
The Hanafi sitting posture is a sunnah demonstrated by the Prophet—sitting on left foot, erecting right, and pointing index finger during tashahhud.

In this lesson, we examine the recommended manner of sitting (qa'dah) during the first tashahhud in prayer. The Hanafi school specifies a particular posture based on prophetic practice and rational reasoning. We will explore the details of sitting, hand placement, and the pointing gesture, as well as the proofs cited in the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal status
The passage describes the sitting posture (qa'dah) after the second prostration of the second rak'ah. Identify that this is a recommended act (sunnah muakkadah), not obligatory.
The text does not label it as fard or wajib; the description is instructional for sunnah practice.
2
Locate the transmitted proofs (dalil naqli)
Find the hadith references: the practice of Aisha (sitting description) and Wail ibn Hujr (hand placement), and Imam Muhammad's hadith on finger pointing.
These are ahad (zanni thubut) and zanni dalalah, sufficient for sunnah but not obligation.
3
Analyze the rational proof (dalil aqli)
The text argues that directing fingers and toes towards the Qibla is preferable as it maximizes orientation of limbs towards Allah.
This rational reasoning supports the sunnah classification—it is a preferable act, not a condition of validity.
4
Detail the finger pointing (isharah)
From Imam Muhammad's hadith, the Hanafi method is to close the little and ring fingers, make a circle with thumb and middle finger, and point with the index finger. According to Imam Halwai, raise at 'la ilaha' and lower at 'illa Allah'.
This symbolizes negation and affirmation of lordship.
5
Differentiate men's and women's postures
Men sit on left foot with right foot erect; women sit on left buttock with feet to the right for modesty.
Both are sunnah, but women's posture emphasizes concealment.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایه اشرف

الله

تشریح ۔ اس عبارت میں قعدہ کی کیفیت کا بیان ہے۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ جب دوسری رکعت کے دوسرے سجدے سے اپنا سراٹھا بایاں پاؤں بچھا کر اس پر بیٹھ جائے اور دایاں گھڑا کرے۔ اور دونوں پیروں کی انگلیاں قبلہ کی طرف متوجہ کرے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ام المؤمنین حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا نے حضور کا [زمین؟] میں بیٹھنا اسی کیفیت کے ساتھ بیان کیا ہے؟ اپنے دونوں ہاتھ دونوں رانوں پر رکھے اور انگلیاں بچھا دے۔ یعنی جس حال پر ہیں چھوڑ دے باہم نہ ملائے اور ہاتھوں سے کیا پکڑے دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرت وائل بن حجر کی حدیث میں اسی کیفیت کے ساتھ روایت کیا گیا ہے اور عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ [اس لئے؟] ہاتھوں کی انگلیوں کا قبلہ رخ متوجہ کرنا حاصل ہو جاتا ہے اور جہاں تک ہر عضو کو قبلہ رخ متوجہ کرناممکن ہو اولی ہے۔ صاحب عنایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ امام محمد نے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کی ایک حدیث بیان کی ہے جس میں یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ شہادت کی انگلی اشارہ کرتے تھے لہذا ہم بھی اسی طرح کریں گے اور یہی قول ابو حنیفہ کا ہے اور ہمارا ہے۔ اور اس اشارہ کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ دائیں خضر اور بنصر کو بند کرے اور وسطی اور انگوٹھے کا حلقہ بنائے اور شہادت کی انگلی سے اشارہ کرے۔ امام حلوائی سے مروی ہے کہ تشہد لا الہ کے وقت اپنی شہادت کی انگلی کھڑی کرے اور الا اللہ کے وقت پست کر دے تا کہ انگلی کھڑی کرنا غیر اللہ سے نفی اور پست کرنا اللہ کے لئے اثبات ہو جائے۔ اور عورت کے بیٹھنے کی کیفیت یہ ہے کہ وہ اپنے بائیں سرین پر بیٹھ جائے اور دونوں پاؤں دائیں طرف نکالے کیونکہ یہ وضع زیادہ پردہ پوش ہے۔
Explanation: This passage explains the manner of sitting. So he said: When he raises his head from the second prostration of the second rak'ah, he sits on his left foot spread out, and erects the right foot. And he directs the toes of both feet towards the Qibla. The proof is that Umm al-Mu'minin Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) described the Prophet's sitting in prayer in this manner: he placed both his hands on his thighs and spread his fingers, i.e., left them as they were, not joining them, and he did not grip anything with his hands. The proof is the hadith of Wail ibn Hujr reported with this description. And rational proof is that in this way the fingers of the hands are directed towards the Qibla, and it is preferable to direct every limb towards the Qibla as much as possible. Sahib al-Inaya wrote that Imam Muhammad narrated a hadith of the Prophet that he used to point with the index finger, so we also do likewise, and this is the statement of Abu Hanifa and ours. The detail of this pointing is that he closes the little finger and ring finger of the right hand, makes a circle with the middle finger and thumb, and points with the index finger. It is narrated from Imam Halwai that at the time of saying 'la ilaha' in the tashahhud he raises his index finger, and at 'illa Allah' he lowers it, so that raising the finger indicates negation of other than Allah and lowering it indicates affirmation for Allah. And the sitting posture of a woman is that she sits on her left buttock and extends both feet to the right side because this is more concealing.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof detailing the recommended sitting posture (qa'dah) in prayer. The author first describes the position: after the second prostration of the second rak'ah, one sits on the left foot spread out, erects the right foot, and points toes towards the Qibla. The hands are placed on the thighs with fingers spread naturally, not clenched. Evidence is cited from Aisha and Wail ibn Hujr, as well as rational reasoning (directing limbs to Qibla). The commentary then discusses the pointing of the index finger during tashahhud: following a hadith narrated by Imam Muhammad, the Hanafi school recommends making a circle with thumb and middle finger and pointing with the index finger. Imam Halwai specifies that the finger is raised at 'la ilaha' and lowered at 'illa Allah' to symbolize negation and affirmation. Finally, the woman's sitting is described: on the left buttock with feet extended to the right for modesty. Throughout, these are sunnah practices, not obligatory.

Key Terms
قعدہ (qa'dah): The sitting position in prayer, specifically for tashahhud.
اشارہ (isharah): Pointing with the index finger during tashahhud.
تشہد (tashahhud): The declaration of faith recited while sitting in prayer.

Dispute over Tashahhud: Ibn Mas'ud vs. Ibn Abbas
Presents the Hanafi preference for Ibn Mas'ud's tashahhud and the Shafi'i preference for Ibn Abbas's, with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi preference for Ibn Mas'ud's tashahhud and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-arguments using linguistic principles (amr, alif-lam, waw) and hadith methodology.

Core Idea
The Hanafi tashahhud is preferred because its linguistic generality and the Prophet's emphatic teaching method outweigh the Shafi'i arguments of Quranic harmony and temporal priority.

This lesson examines a classical inter-madhhab dispute over the exact wording of the tashahhud in prayer. The Hanafi school, following Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, insists on a version that includes the letter waw and alif-lam for generality. The Shafi'i school, following Abdullah ibn Abbas, prefers a version that closely mirrors Quranic phrasing and is chronologically later. By analyzing the proofs, you will understand how Hanafi scholars prioritize linguistic and pedagogical strength over mere Quranic agreement.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact wording of Ibn Mas'ud's tashahhud as transmitted in the Hanafi school. Note the key features: 'al-tahiyyatu lillah wa al-salawatu wa al-tayyibatu', 'al-salamu 'alayka' with alif-lam, and the inclusion of waw.
This version is considered the most authentic because the Prophet taught it directly to Ibn Mas'ud by holding his hand.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State the Shafi'i position, which adopts Ibn Abbas's version: 'al-tahiyyatu al-mubarakatu al-salawatu al-tayyibatu', 'salamun 'alayka' without alif-lam, and no waw before 'al-salawatu'.
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that this version is superior for several reasons, including Quranic correspondence and later transmission.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i arguments: (1) the word 'mubarakatu' appears in the Quran (24:61); (2) 'salamun' without alif-lam matches Quranic greetings; (3) Ibn Abbas's version is later and could abrogate the earlier one.
These are based on Quranic harmony and the principle of abrogation (naskh).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi counter-arguments: (1) the command 'Qul' indicates istihbab, not wujub; (2) the alif-lam in 'al-salamu' indicates generality (istighraq); (3) the waw in 'wa al-salawatu' avoids restricting 'al-tahiyyat' to prayers alone; (4) the Prophet's hand-holding and surah-like teaching emphasize authenticity.
The Hanafis also reject the abrogation claim because the later report was not intended to abrogate the earlier.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is the actual wording recited in prayer. Hanafis recite Ibn Mas'ud's version, while Shafi'is recite Ibn Abbas's version. Both acknowledge that reciting any authentic companion version is valid, but each school prefers its own.
This difference affects the daily practice of millions of Muslims.

تشہد ابن مسعود

يم و التشهد التحيات لله والصلوات والطيبات السلام علیک ایها النبی...... الى آخره، وهذا تشهد عبد الله مسعود فانه قال اخذ رسول الله بیدى و علمنى التشهد كما كان يعلمنى سورة من القرآن وقال التحيات الله الى اخره والأخذ بهذا اولى من الأخذ بتشهد ابن عباس وهو قوله التحيات المباركة الصلوات الطيبات الله سلام علیک ایها النبی و رحمة الله و بركاته سلام علينا الى اخره لان فيه الامر وال الاستحباب والالف واللام وهما للاستغراق و زيادة الواو وهى لتجديد الكلام كما في التقسم وتاكي التعليم

ترجمہ اور تشهد التحيات الله والصلوات والطيبات السلام علیک ایها النبی ... الخ اور یہ تشہد عبد اللہ بن مسعود گا ۲ - ۱ اس لئے کہ ابن مسعودؓ نے کہا کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے میرا ہاتھ پکڑا اور مجھ کو شہد کی اس طرح تعلیم دی جس طرح قرآن کی کسی سورت کی آیت دیا کرتے تھے اور فرمایا کہ کہہ التحیات الله الى اخر اور اس تشہد کا لینا اولیٰ ہے بہ نسبت ابن عباس کے تشہد کے اور وہ یہ ہے ۴۔ التحيات المباركات الصلوات الطيبات الله سلام علیک ایها النبی ورحمة الله وبركاته سلام علينا ... الى اخرہ کیونکہ اس تشہد کے پڑھنے میں صیغہ امر وارد ہوا ہے اور امر کا کمتر درجہ استباب ہے۔ اور الف اور لام و ہ دونوں استغراق کے۔ ہیں اور واؤ کی زیادتی اور وہ تجدید کلام کے لئے ہے جیسے تم میں اور تعلیم کی تاکید ہے۔

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم

۶۵

باب صفة الصلوة

تشریح اس عبارت کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ قعد اولی میں اصح قول کی بنا پر تشہد پڑھنا واجب ہے۔ اور تشہد کی الفاظ میں صحابہ رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین نے اختلاف کیا ہے۔ چنانچہ حضرت عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کا تشہد ہے حضرت علی رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کا تشہد ہے ابن عباس رضی اللہ عنہما کا تشہد ہے اور ابن مسعود رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کا تشہد ہے۔ اور حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا کا تشہد ہے اور حضرت جابر رضی اللہ عنہ کا تشہد ہے۔ اور ان کے علاوہ دوسرے صحابہ سے بھی تشہد منقول ہے علماء احناف نے حضرت ابن مسعودرضی اللہ عنہ کے تشہد کو اختیار کیا ہے اور امام شافعی نے حضرت ابن عباس رضی اللہ عنہما کے تشہد کو اختیار کیا ہے ابن عباس رضی اللہ عنہما کا تشہد یہ ہے، التحيات المباركات الصلوات الطيبات الله سلام عليك ايها النبي ورحمة الله وبركاته سلام علينا وعلى عباد الله الصالحين اشهد ان لا اله الا الله واشهد ان محمد ارسول الله

اور ابن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ کا تشہد یہ ہے، التحيات الله والصلوات والطيبات السلام عليك ايها النبي ورحمة الله و بركاته السلام علينا و على عباد الله الصالحين اشهد ان لا اله الا الله واشهد ان محمد اعبده ورسوله

ا، مشافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا کہ ابن عباس رضی اللہ عنہا کے تشہد کو اختیار کرنا چند وجوہ سے اولی ہے،

۱) ابن عباس کے تشہد میں کلمہ مبارکات زیادہ ہے جو ابن مسعودؓ کے تشہد میں نہیں ہے۔

۲) ابن عباس کا تشہد قرآن پاک کے موافق ہے اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا تَحِيَّةً مِّنْ عِندِ اللَّهِ مُبَارَكَةً طَيِّبَةً

۳) ابن عباس نے لفظ سلام بغیر الف لام کے ذکر کیا اور قرآن پاک میں بھی اکثر تسلیمات بغیر الف لام کے مذکور ہیں چنانچہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا۔ سَلَامٌ عَلَيْكُمْ طِبْتُمُ، قَالُوا سَلَامًا قَالَ سَلَامٌ، وَسَلَامٌ عَلَيْهِ يَوْمَ وُلِد اور اشرف کلام وہ ہی شمار ہوتا ہے جو قرآن کے موافق ہو۔

۴) ابن عباس کا تشہد ابن مسعودؓ کی خبر سے مؤخر ہے کیوں کہ ابن عباس تصغیر اسن اور ابن مسعود شیوخ میں سے تھے اور یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ مؤخر مقدم کے لئے ناسخ ہوتا ہے علماء احناف نے کہا کہ ابن مسعودؓ کے تشہد کو اختیار کرنا بھی چند وجوہ سے اولیٰ ہے، لہ ابن مسعودؓ کہتے ہیں کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے میرا ہاتھ پکڑ کر مجھ کو تشہد کی تعلیم دی اور فرمایا قل التحیات اللہ اس حدیث میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول قل امر کا صیغہ ہے اور امر کا کمتر درجہ استجاب ہے۔

السلام علیک الف لام کے ساتھ مفید استغراق ہے۔

والصلوات واو کے ساتھ تجدید کلام کے لئے ہے

حضور کا ہاتھ پکڑنا اور سرت قرآن کی طرح تعلیم دینا مفید تاکید ہے

- التحیات صلوۃ اور غیر صلوۃ سب کو عام ہے لیکن جب ابن عباس کے تشہد میں الصلوات بغیر واؤ کے کہا تو یہ تخصیص ہوگئی اور اس التحیات سے مراد فقط صلوات ہوئیں اور جب والصلوات واؤ کے ساتھ کہا جیسا کہ ابن مسعودؓ کے تشہد میں ہے تو اول یعنی التحیات عام رہا اور چونکہ کلمہ عام سے ثنا کرنا ابلغ ہے اس لئے یہی اولی ہوگا۔
Tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud: ... and this is the tashahhud of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. He said: The Messenger of Allah took my hand and taught me the tashahhud just as he taught me a surah of the Quran and said: 'Say: al-tahiyyatu lillah...' Adopting this is better than adopting the tashahhud of Ibn Abbas, which is: 'al-tahiyyatu al-mubarakatu al-salawatu al-tayyibatu lillah, salamun 'alayka ayyuha al-nabiyyu wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuhu, salamun 'alayna...' because in it (Ibn Mas'ud's) there is the command, and the command indicates istihbab, and the alif and lam indicate generality, and the addition of the waw is for renewal of speech as in oaths and emphasis of teaching. Translation: And the tashahhud: al-tahiyyatu lillah... and this is the tashahhud of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud because Ibn Mas'ud said: The Messenger of Allah took my hand and taught me the tashahhud just as he taught me an ayah of the Quran and said: 'Say: al-tahiyyatu lillah...' and adopting this tashahhud is better than adopting the tashahhud of Ibn Abbas, which is: al-tahiyyatu al-mubarakatu... because in reciting this tashahhud, the command form appears, and the least degree of command is istihbab. And the alif and lam both indicate generality, and the addition of the waw is for renewal of speech, as in 'you' and emphasis of teaching. (Page 65) Ashraf al-Hidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah Juz 2, 65, Bab sifat al-salah. Explanation: The summary of this passage is that in the first sitting, according to the soundest opinion, reciting the tashahhud is wajib. The Companions differed over the wording of the tashahhud: Umar, Ali, Ibn Abbas, Ibn Mas'ud, Aisha, Jabir, and others. Hanafi scholars have chosen the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud, while Imam Shafi'i chose the tashahhud of Ibn Abbas. The tashahhud of Ibn Abbas is: al-tahiyyatu al-mubarakatu al-salawatu al-tayyibatu lillah, salamun 'alayka ayyuha al-nabiyyu wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuhu, salamun 'alayna wa 'ala 'ibadillahi al-salihin, ashhadu an la ilaha illallah wa ashhadu anna muhammadan rasulullah. And the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud is: al-tahiyyatu lillah wa al-salawatu wa al-tayyibatu, al-salamu 'alayka ayyuha al-nabiyyu wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuhu, al-salamu 'alayna wa 'ala 'ibadillahi al-salihin, ashhadu an la ilaha illallah wa ashhadu anna muhammadan 'abduhu wa rasuluh. Imam Shafi'i said that adopting the tashahhud of Ibn Abbas is better for several reasons: (1) Ibn Abbas's tashahhud contains the word 'mubarakatu' which is not in Ibn Mas'ud's. (2) Ibn Abbas's tashahhud agrees with the Quran: 'tahiyyatan min 'indillahi mubarakatan tayyibatan'. (3) Ibn Abbas mentions 'salam' without alif-lam, and in the Quran most greetings are without alif-lam, e.g., 'salamun 'alaykum', etc., and the best speech is that which agrees with the Quran. (4) Ibn Abbas's tashahhud is later than Ibn Mas'ud's report because Ibn Abbas was younger and Ibn Mas'ud was from the elders, and it is obvious that the later abrogates the earlier. Hanafi scholars said that adopting Ibn Mas'ud's tashahhud is better for several reasons: Ibn Mas'ud said: The Messenger of Allah took my hand and taught me the tashahhud and said 'Qul al-tahiyyatu lillah', and in this hadith the Prophet's saying 'Qul' is a command and the least degree of command is istihbab. 'Al-salamu 'alayka' with alif-lam indicates generality. 'Wa al-salawatu' with waw is for renewal of speech. The Prophet taking his hand and teaching like a surah of the Quran indicates emphasis. 'Al-tahiyyat' is general, including prayer and non-prayer, but when Ibn Abbas said 'al-salawatu' without waw, it restricts 'al-tahiyyat' to only prayers, but when 'wa al-salawatu' is said with waw as in Ibn Mas'ud's, then 'al-tahiyyat' remains general, and praising with a general word is more eloquent, so this is better.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the preferred wording of the tashahhud in prayer. The Hanafi school adopts the version transmitted by Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, while the Shafi'i school adopts that of Abdullah ibn Abbas. The text first establishes that reciting tashahhud in the first sitting is wajib according to the soundest opinion. It then lists various Companion versions, notably those of Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Abbas. Imam al-Shafi'i's arguments for preferring Ibn Abbas's version include: (1) the word 'mubarakatu' is present in Ibn Abbas's version and agrees with Quranic usage (Surah al-Nur 24:61); (2) the word 'salam' without alif-lam matches Quranic greetings; (3) Ibn Abbas's version is later and could abrogate the earlier one. The Hanafi response is detailed: (1) The Prophet's instruction 'Qul' is a command, which indicates istihbab (recommendation) at the least. (2) The alif-lam in 'al-salamu' indicates generality (istighraq). (3) The waw in 'wa al-salawatu' renews the speech and keeps 'al-tahiyyat' general, whereas without waw it restricts the meaning to prayers only. Praising with a general term is more eloquent. (4) The Prophet's act of holding Ibn Mas'ud's hand and teaching like a Quranic surah emphasizes the importance and authenticity of this version. The Hanafi position is thus supported by linguistic and hadith-based arguments.

Key Terms
تشہد (tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited during the sitting posture in prayer.
التحیات (al-tahiyyat): The opening word of tashahhud, meaning all greetings.
صیغہ امر (sighah al-amr): The imperative verb form, which linguistically indicates command.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis prefer Ibn Mas'ud's tashahhud over Ibn 'Abbas's?
A) Because Ibn Mas'ud was a younger companion and his report is more reliable.
B) Because Ibn Mas'ud's tashahhud includes the waw which keeps 'tahiyyat' general.
C) Because Ibn 'Abbas's tashahhud is not from the Prophet.
D) Because Hanafis do not recite tashahhud.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prefers Ibn Mas'ud's tashahhud due to the generalizing effect of the waw, the indicative nature of the command (amr), and the emphatic teaching method of the Prophet.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
9 min
The Preferred Tashahhud: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Presents the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the preferred tashahhud wording with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prefers Ibn Mas'ud's tashahhud over Ibn Abbas's and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The Hanafi tashahhud is traced through a physical handshake to Jibril; its wording emphasizes comprehensiveness of worship.

The tashahhud is a wajib part of the prayer, but its exact wording differs among madhhabs. This passage presents the Hanafi choice of Ibn Mas'ud's version and the Shafi'i choice of Ibn Abbas's, along with their respective proofs. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate hadith-based arguments and school preferences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact wording of Ibn Mas'ud's tashahhud as the Hanafi relied-upon version. Note that reciting tashahhud is wajib in the first sitting.
The Hanafi version includes 'al-tahiyyat lillah wa al-salawat wa al-tayyibat, al-salam 'alayka...' and ends with 'ashhadu anna Muhammadan 'abduhu wa rasuluh.'
2
Identify the opponent's view
State that Imam al-Shafi'i prefers Ibn Abbas's tashahhud, which includes 'al-mubarakat' and uses 'salam' without alif lam, and ends with 'rasul Allah' without 'abd'.
Ibn Abbas's version: 'al-tahiyyat al-mubarakat al-salawat al-tayyibat, al-salam 'alayka...'
3
Follow the opponent's proof
List al-Shafi'i's four arguments: extra word 'mubarakat', Quranic concordance, 'salam' without alif lam matching Qur'an, and the claim that Ibn Abbas's report is later and abrogating.
Each argument is based on a specific textual or historical observation.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Go through the Hanafi refutations: (a) extra word is not decisive; (b) Quranic agreement is irrelevant because reciting Qur'an in the sitting is makruh; (c) 'salam' appears both with and without alif lam in the Qur'an; (d) Ibn Mas'ud's report is actually later; (e) the chain of transmission is stronger and includes a physical teaching chain.
Pay attention to how each Shafi'i point is countered with a specific counter-argument.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis recite Ibn Mas'ud's tashahhud, Shafi'is recite Ibn Abbas's. The dispute does not affect the validity of prayer but reflects different preferred practices.
This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the range of accepted diversity.

باب صفة الصلوة
تشریح اس عبارت کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ قعد اولی میں اصح قول کی بنا پر تشہد پڑھنا واجب ہے۔ اور تشہد کی الفاظ میں صحابہ رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین نے اختلاف کیا ہے۔ چنانچہ حضرت عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کا تشہد ہے حضرت علی رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کا تشہد ہے ابن عباس رضی اللہ عنہما کا تشہد ہے اور ابن مسعود رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کا تشہد ہے۔ اور حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا کا تشہد ہے اور حضرت جابر رضی اللہ عنہ کا تشہد ہے۔ اور ان کے علاوہ دوسرے صحابہ سے بھی تشہد منقول ہے علماء احناف نے حضرت ابن مسعودرضی اللہ عنہ کے تشہد کو اختیار کیا ہے اور امام شافعی نے حضرت ابن عباس رضی اللہ عنہما کے تشہد کو اختیار کیا ہے ابن عباس رضی اللہ عنہما کا تشہد یہ ہے، التحيات المباركات الصلوات الطيبات الله سلام عليك ايها النبي ورحمة الله وبركاته سلام علينا وعلى عباد الله الصالحين اشهد ان لا اله الا الله واشهد ان محمد ارسول الله
اور ابن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ کا تشہد یہ ہے، التحيات الله والصلوات والطيبات السلام عليك ايها النبي ورحمة الله و بركاته السلام علينا و على عباد الله الصالحين اشهد ان لا اله الا الله واشهد ان محمد اعبده ورسوله
امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا کہ ابن عباس رضی اللہ عنہما کے تشہد کو اختیار کرنا چند وجوہ سے اولی ہے،
1. ابن عباس کے تشہد میں کلمہ مبارکات زیادہ ہے جو ابن مسعودؓ کے تشہد میں نہیں ہے۔
2. ابن عباس کا تشہد قرآن پاک کے موافق ہے اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا: تَحِيَّةً مِّنْ عِندِ اللَّهِ مُبَارَكَةً طَيِّبَةً
3. ابن عباس نے لفظ سلام بغیر الف لام کے ذکر کیا اور قرآن پاک میں بھی اکثر تسلیمات بغیر الف لام کے مذکور ہیں چنانچہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا: سَلَامٌ عَلَيْكُمْ طِبْتُمُ، قَالُوا سَلَامًا قَالَ سَلَامٌ، وَسَلَامٌ عَلَيْهِ يَوْمَ وُلِد اور اشرف کلام وہ ہی شمار ہوتا ہے جو قرآن کے موافق ہو۔
4. ابن عباس کا تشہد ابن مسعودؓ کی خبر سے مؤخر ہے کیوں کہ ابن عباس تصغیر اسن اور ابن مسعود شیوخ میں سے تھے اور یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ مؤخر مقدم کے لئے ناسخ ہوتا ہے علماء احناف نے کہا کہ ابن مسعودؓ کے تشہد کو اختیار کرنا بھی چند وجوہ سے اولیٰ ہے، 1. ابن مسعودؓ کہتے ہیں کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے میرا ہاتھ پکڑ کر مجھ کو تشہد کی تعلیم دی اور فرمایا قل التحیات اللہ اس حدیث میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول قل امر کا صیغہ ہے اور امر کا کمتر درجہ استجاب ہے۔
2. السلام علیک الف لام کے ساتھ مفید استغراق ہے۔
3. والصلوات واو کے ساتھ تجدید کلام کے لئے ہے
4. حضور کا ہاتھ پکڑنا اور سرت قرآن کی طرح تعلیم دینا مفید تاکید ہے
5. التحیات صلوۃ اور غیر صلوۃ سب کو عام ہے لیکن جب ابن عباس کے تشہد میں الصلوات بغیر واؤ کے کہا تو یہ تخصیص ہوگئی اور اس التحیات سے مراد فقط صلوات ہوئیں اور جب والصلوات واؤ کے ساتھ کہا جیسا کہ ابن مسعودؓ کے تشہد میں ہے تو اول یعنی التحیات عام رہا اور چونکہ کلمہ عام سے ثنا کرنا ابلغ ہے اس لئے یہی اولی ہوگا۔
عامۃ المحدثین نے کہا کہ ابن مسعود کا تشہد اسناد کے اعتبار سے احسن ہے۔ عام صحابہ نے بھی ابن مسعودؓ کے تشہد کو اختیار کیا ہے چنانچہ مروی ہے کہ صدیق اکبر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ نے منبر رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم پر ان میں سے تشہد کی تعلیم دی۔ اسی طرح سلمان فارسی جابر اور حضرت معاویہ رضی اللہ عنہم سے مروی ہے ابن مسعود کا تشہد لفظ عبدہ پر مشتمل ہے کیونکہ ابن مسعود کے تشہد میں ہے واشهد ان محمد اعبده ورسوله اور لفظ عبد حال پر دلالت کرتا ہے کیونکہ واقعہ معراج جس کے ذریعہ آپ کے اعلیٰ مرتبہ کو بیان کیا گیا ہے اس میں آپ کو عبد کے ساتھ ہی فرمایا چنانچہ ارشاد ہے سبحان الذی اسرى بعبده
ابن مسعود کا تشہد ضبط کے اعتبار سے بھی احسن ہے چنانچہ امام محمد سے مروی ہے، انه قال اخذ بي يوسف رحمة الله عليه بيدى وعلمنى التشهد وقال اخذ ابو حنيفة رحمه الله بيدى فعلمنى التشهد وقال ابو حنيفةً رحمة الله اخذ حماد بيدى فعلمنى التشهد وقال حماد اخذ ابراهيم بيدي فعلمني التشهد وقال ابراهيم اخذ علقمة بيدى وعلمنى التشهد وقال علقمة اخذ ابن مسعود بيدي و علمنى التشهد قال ابن مسعود اخذ رسول الله بيدي و علمني التشهد وقال رسول الله اخذ جبریل علیه السلام بیدی فعلمني التشهد یعنی امام محمد نے کہا کہ ابو یوسف نے میرا ہاتھ پکڑا اور مجھے کو شہد کی تعلیم دی اور ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ ابوحنیفہ نے میرا ہاتھ پکڑ کر مجھ کو تشہد کی تعلیم دی اور ابوحنیفہ نے کہا کہ حماد نے میرا ہاتھ پکڑ کر مجھ کو شہد کی تعلیم دی اور حماد نے کہا کہ ابراہیم نخعی نے میرا ہاتھ پکڑ کر مجھ کو تشہد کی تعلیم دی اور ابراہیم نخعی نے کہا کہ علقمہ نے میرا ہاتھ پکر کر مجھ کو تشہد کی تعلیم دی اور علقمہ نے کہا ابن مسعودؓ نے میرا ہاتھ پکڑ مجھ کو تشہد کی تعلیم اور ابن مسعودؓ نے کہا کہ رسول اللہ ا نے میرا ہاتھ پکڑ کر مجھ کو تشہد کی تعلیم دی اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے کہا کہ جبرائیل نے میرا ہاتھ پکڑ کر مجھ کو تشہد کی تعلیم دی۔
امام شافعی کی وجوہ اولویت کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی کلمہ کی زیادتی مریج ہے تو حضرت جابر رضی اللہ عنہ کا تشہد اولی ہوگا کیونکہ اس میں بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم کی زیادتی ہے اور ابن مسعودؓ کے تشہد میں واو اور الف لام اور لفظ عبدہ زائد ہے لہذا ابن مسعود کا تشہد اولی ہوگا۔ دوسری وجہ اولویت کا جواب یہ ہے کہ قرآن کے موافق ہونا مرجح نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ قعدہ میں قرآن پڑھنا مکروہ ہے پس قرآت قرآن کی موافقت کیسے مستحب ہوگی۔ تیسری وجہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ لفظ سلام جس طرح بغیر الف لام کے قرآن میں آیا ہے اسی طرح الف لام کے ساتھ بھی مذکور ہے اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا و السلام على يوم ولدت والسلام على من اتبع الهدی۔ چوتھی وجہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ تشہد کے بارے میں حدیث ابن عباس مؤخر ہے ایسا نہیں ہے بلکہ ابن مسعودؓ کی حدیث مؤخر ہے چنانچہ امام کرختی سے مروی ہے کہ ان مسعود نے کہا کہ ابتداء اسلام میں التحیات الطاهرات المباركات الزاكيات کہا کرتے تھے اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ابن مسعود کی خبر ابن عباس کی خبر سے مؤخر ہے۔
فوائد التحیات کے معنی عبادات قولیۂ صلوات، عبادات، بدنیہ الطیبات عبادات مالیہ السلام علیک یہ اس سلام کی حکایت ہے جو شب معراج میں حضور کی تین چیزوں کے ساتھ ثناء کرنے کے جواب میں فرمایا تھا۔ چنانچہ السلام التحیات کے مقابا میں ہے اور رحمت صلوات
Chapter: Description of Prayer. Explanation: The gist of this statement is that in the first sitting, according to the soundest opinion, reciting the tashahhud is obligatory (wajib). And the Companions differed regarding the wording of the tashahhud. Thus there is the tashahhud of Umar, of Ali, of Ibn Abbas, of Ibn Mas'ud, of Aisha, of Jabir, and others. The Hanafi scholars chose the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud, while Imam al-Shafi'i chose the tashahhud of Ibn Abbas. The tashahhud of Ibn Abbas is: al-tahiyyat al-mubarakat al-salawat al-tayyibat Allah salam 'alayka ayyuha al-nabiyyu wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuhu salam 'alayna wa 'ala 'ibadillah al-salihin ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah wa ashhadu anna Muhammadan rasul Allah. And the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud is: al-tahiyyat Allah wa al-salawat wa al-tayyibat al-salam 'alayka ayyuha al-nabiyyu wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuhu al-salam 'alayna wa 'ala 'ibadillah al-salihin ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah wa ashhadu anna Muhammadan 'abduhu wa rasuluh. Imam al-Shafi'i said that choosing Ibn Abbas's tashahhud is preferable for several reasons: 1) Ibn Abbas's tashahhud contains the extra word mubarakat which is not in Ibn Mas'ud's. 2) Ibn Abbas's tashahhud agrees with the Qur'an: tahiyyatan min 'indillahi mubarakatan tayyibatan. 3) Ibn Abbas mentions salam without the definite article, and in the Qur'an most salutations come without alif lam. 4) Ibn Abbas's tashahhud is later than Ibn Mas'ud's report because Ibn Abbas was younger, and a later report abrogates an earlier one. The Hanafi scholars said that choosing Ibn Mas'ud's tashahhud is preferable for several reasons: 1) Ibn Mas'ud said that the Prophet took his hand and taught him the tashahhud, saying 'Qul: al-tahiyyat lillah' – the command 'Qul' indicates recommendation. 2) al-salam with alif lam indicates comprehensiveness. 3) wa al-salawat with waw renews the speech. 4) The Prophet's taking his hand and teaching like the Qur'an indicates emphasis. 5) al-tahiyyat includes prayers and non-prayers, but when Ibn Abbas says al-salawat without waw, tahiyyat becomes specific to prayers only, whereas with waw as in Ibn Mas'ud, tahiyyat remains general and praising with a general term is more eloquent. The majority of hadith scholars said that Ibn Mas'ud's tashahhud is better in terms of chain. Most Companions also chose his tashahhud. It is narrated that Abu Bakr taught it on the Prophet's pulpit. Also from Salman, Jabir, and Mu'awiya. Ibn Mas'ud's tashahhud includes the word 'abd (servant), which indicates the state of servitude as in the verse about the Night Journey: subhan alladhi asra bi 'abdihi. It is also better in terms of preservation. Imam Muhammad narrated that Abu Yusuf took his hand and taught him the tashahhud, and Abu Yusuf said Abu Hanifa took my hand and taught me, and Abu Hanifa said Hammad took my hand and taught me, and Hammad said Ibrahim took my hand and taught me, and Ibrahim said Alqamah took my hand and taught me, and Alqamah said Ibn Mas'ud took my hand and taught me, and Ibn Mas'ud said the Prophet took my hand and taught me, and the Prophet said Jibril took my hand and taught me. The response to al-Shafi'i's reasons: If extra word is preferred, then Jabir's tashahhud (with basmala) would be better, but Ibn Mas'ud's has extra waw, alif lam, and 'abd. Agreement with Qur'an is not a preference because reciting Qur'an in the sitting is disliked. The word salam appears in the Qur'an both with and without alif lam. The claim that Ibn Abbas's hadith is later is false; rather, Ibn Mas'ud's hadith is later, as reported from al-Karkhi: Ibn Mas'ud initially used to say al-tahiyyat al-tayyibat al-mubarakat al-zakiyyat. Benefits: al-tahiyyat means verbal acts of worship, al-salawat bodily acts, al-tayyibat financial acts. Al-salam 'alayka is a narration of the greeting given to the Prophet on the Night of Mi'raj in response to his praising Allah with three things. Thus al-salam corresponds to al-tahiyyat, and rahmat to al-salawat.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the preferred wording of the tashahhud recited during the sitting (qa'dah) in prayer. The Hanafi school follows the version transmitted by Ibn Mas'ud, while the Shafi'i school follows that of Ibn Abbas. The text first establishes that reciting tashahhud is wajib (obligatory) according to the soundest opinion in the first sitting. It then lists several Companion versions but focuses on the two main ones. Imam al-Shafi'i argues his choice with four points: (1) Ibn Abbas's wording includes the word 'mubarakat' (blessed) which is an addition; (2) it matches the Qur'anic phrase in Surah an-Nur; (3) it uses 'salam' without the definite article, paralleling Qur'anic usage; and (4) Ibn Abbas's report is later, thus abrogating earlier ones. The Hanafi scholars respond with their own arguments: (1) The Prophet's command to Ibn Mas'ud using the imperative 'qul' indicates recommendation; (2) the inclusion of 'alif lam' in 'al-salam' implies comprehensiveness; (3) the conjunction 'wa' before 'al-salawat' renews the speech emphasizing the diversity of worship; (4) the Prophet's physical teaching method reinforces the importance; and (5) the general term 'al-tahiyyat' is more comprehensive and eloquent. Further supporting Ibn Mas'ud's version is the strong chain of transmission: a continuous chain from Imam Muhammad back to Jibril through a chain of teachers physically taking the student's hand. This uninterrupted transmission (sanad muttasil) gives the Hanafi version unparalleled authority. Additionally, the version includes the word 'abd' (servant) which highlights the Prophet's servitude as emphasized in the Mi'raj verse. The Hanafi response also systematically refutes each of al-Shafi'i's arguments: (a) if mere addition were preferred, Jabir's tashahhud (which includes 'bismillah') would be even more primary; (b) agreement with Qur'an is irrelevant because reciting Qur'an during the sitting is makruh; (c) 'salam' appears in the Qur'an both with and without 'alif lam'; and (d) contrary to al-Shafi'i's claim, Ibn Mas'ud's report is actually later based on the narration from Imam al-Karkhi. Finally, the passage concludes with a linguistic explanation of the terms: 'al-tahiyyat' refers to verbal acts of worship, 'al-salawat' to bodily acts, and 'al-tayyibat' to financial acts. The greeting 'al-salam' corresponds to verbal praise, 'al-rahmat' to physical worship, and 'al-barakat' to financial charity. The Hanafi ruling is that in the first sitting, the tashahhud as per Ibn Mas'ud's version is recitated (wajib), and it is this that is practiced.

Key Terms
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited during the sitting (qa'dah) in prayer.
التحیات (al-tahiyyat): Greetings of sovereignty/salutations; interpreted as verbal acts of worship.
الصلوات (al-salawat): Prayers; interpreted as bodily acts of worship.
الطيبات (al-tayyibat): Good things/pure things; interpreted as financial acts of worship (charity).
قل (qul): Imperative 'say' used by the Prophet when teaching the tashahhud.
عبده ('abduhu): His servant; emphasizes the Prophet's servitude.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a reason given by the Hanafi school for preferring Ibn Mas'ud's tashahhud?
A) It contains the extra word 'mubarakat'.
B) It matches the wording of the Qur'an.
C) It includes the word 'abd' which emphasizes servitude.
D) It uses 'salam' without the definite article.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prefers Ibn Mas'ud's tashahhud due to its stronger chain, comprehensive wording, and sound refutations of the Shafi'i arguments.

Recitation in the Last Two Rak'ahs: Preferred vs Obligatory
Intra-Hanafi dispute on last two rak'ahs recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi position on reciting Surah al-Fatihah in the last two rak'ahs and evaluate the opposing narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad.

Core Idea
Reciting Fatihah in the last two rak'ahs is mustahab, not wajib—omission requires no compensation.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: is reciting Surah al-Fatihah in the last two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard prayer obligatory (wajib) or merely recommended (mustahab)? The passage from al-Hidayah presents the preferred view and contrasts it with a weaker narration. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of sajda sahw and classifying acts within prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi mufta bihi position
Identify that the relied-upon view is that reciting Fatihah in the last two rak'ahs is mustahab (recommended), not wajib. The prayer remains valid if omitted, and no sajda sahw is required.
This is the position preferred by Sahib al-Hidayah.
2
Identify the opposing intra-Hanafi view
Note Hasan ibn Ziyad's narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that reciting Fatihah in the last two rak'ahs is wajib, and omitting it requires sajda sahw.
This is a weaker, non-mufta bihi narration.
3
Analyze the opponent's proof
Examine the qiyas (analogy): standing (qiyam) in the last rak'ahs is intended to be filled with dhikr, so leaving it empty is makruh—analogous to ruku and sujood which require dhikr.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: the obligation of recitation is specific to the first two rak'ahs; the last two do not carry the same ruling. The analogy breaks down because the rule for ruku and sujood is general, while for qiyam it is specified.
The school limits the fard of recitation to the first two rak'ahs.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Apply the practical consequence: if one omits Fatihah in the last two rak'ahs, according to the mufta bihi, the prayer is valid without sajda sahw; according to Hasan's view, sajda sahw would be wajib.
This highlights how a difference in usul affects fiqh practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صفة الصلوة
یعنی حضور یا ظہر اور عصر کی پہلی دو رکعتوں میں سورہ فاتحہ اور سورت پڑھتے تھے اور آخر کی دو رکعتوں میں سورۃ فاتحہ پڑھا کرو تھے صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ بیان افضل ہے یعنی آخر کی دورکعتوں میں سورۃ فاتحہ پڑھنا افضل اور مستحب ہے چنانچہ اگر آخر دورکعتوں میں قرآت فاتحہ اور تہی دونوں کو ترک کر دیا تو کوئی حرج نہیں اور اس پر سجدہ سہو بھی واجب نہیں ہوگا لیکن قرآت افضل یہی صحیح روایت ہے۔ حسن بن زیاد نے امام اعظم سے ایک روایت یہ بھی نقل کی ہے کہ اخربین میں سورۃ فاتحہ کا پڑھنا واجب ہے چنانچہ اگر سہوا ترک کر تو اس پر سجدہ سہولا زم ہو گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اخربین میں قیام مقصود ہے لہذا اس کو ذکر اور قرآت دونوں سے خالی رکھنا مکروہ ہے جیسہ رکوع اور سجود کو ذکر سے خالی رکھنا مکروہ ہے۔ اور قول صحیح کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قرآت صرف پہلی دو رکعتوں میں فرض ہے ان شاء اللہ اس تفصیل بعد میں آئے گی فانتظر واانى معكم من المنتظرين
Chapter of the description of prayer. That is, the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to recite Surah al-Fatihah and another surah in the first two rak'ahs of Zuhr and Asr, and in the last two rak'ahs he used to recite Surah al-Fatihah. The author of al-Hidayah says: This statement is about what is preferred, meaning reciting Surah al-Fatihah in the last two rak'ahs is preferred and mustahab. So if one abandons both recitation of Fatihah and silence in the last two rak'ahs, there is no harm and sajda sahw is not wajib. But the correct narration is that recitation is preferred. Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that reciting Surah al-Fatihah in the last two rak'ahs is wajib, so if one forgetfully omits it, sajda sahw becomes necessary. The proof is that in the last two rak'ahs, standing (qiyam) is intended, so leaving it empty of both dhikr and recitation is makruh, just as leaving ruku and sujood empty of dhikr is makruh. And the proof of the correct saying is that recitation is only fard in the first two rak'ahs, and by Allah's will, this detail will come later. So wait, and I am with you among those who wait.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage, taken from the commentary of al-Hidayah, addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding recitation in the last two rak'ahs of fard prayers. The base text states that the Prophet would recite Fatihah and a surah in the first two rak'ahs but only Fatihah in the last two. The commentator explains that this indicates the preferred (afdal) practice: reciting Fatihah in the last two rak'ahs is mustahab (recommended), not obligatory. If one omits both recitation and silence, the prayer remains valid and no sajda sahw is required. However, a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad attributes to Imam Abu Hanifa the view that reciting Fatihah in the last two rak'ahs is wajib, necessitating sajda sahw if omitted. The proof for Hasan's view is that qiyam in these rak'ahs is intended to be filled with dhikr, so leaving it empty is makruh, analogous to ruku and sujood. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position, however, is that recitation in the last two rak'ahs is not wajib, as the obligation of recitation is limited to the first two rak'ahs. This dispute shows the range of opinions within the Hanafi school and the importance of distinguishing between fard, wajib, and mustahab.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahab): Recommended but not obligatory; omission is not sinful and does not require compensation.
سجدہ سہو (sajda as-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for an omission or addition in prayer.
اخربین (ākhirīn): The last two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the last two rak'ahs of Zuhr prayer, if one omits reciting Surah al-Fatihah entirely, what is the ruling according to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) Hanafi position?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but sajda sahw is wajib.
C) The prayer is valid and no sajda sahw is required.
D) The prayer is valid only if one recites a different surah.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, reciting Surah al-Fatihah in the last two rak'ahs of a fard prayer is mustahab, not wajib; omission does not require sajda sahw.

Sitting in the Final Tashahhud: Iftirash vs Tawarruk
Inter-madhhab dispute on final tashahhud sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers iftirash mustahab in the final tashahhud and evaluate the Maliki argument for tawarruk using hadith criticism and the principle of 'ashaq.

Core Idea
Iftirash is preferred; the hadith for tawarruk is weak or for old age.

This lesson focuses on a point of difference between the Hanafi and Maliki schools regarding the posture in the final tashahhud. The Hanafi school, as elaborated in al-Hidayah, holds that sitting in iftirash (as in the first tashahhud) is mustahab. Imam Malik, however, considers tawarruk to be sunnah. We will examine the evidence each school presents and the Hanafi response, which combines hadith criticism (jarh) and interpretive ta'wil.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that the final tashahhud should be performed in the same manner as the first: iftirash (sitting on the left foot with the right foot erect). This is considered mustahab (preferred), not wajib.
2
Identify the Maliki position
Imam Malik maintains that tawarruk (sitting on the buttocks with both feet protruding to the right) is sunnah in both tashahhuds.
Tawarruk is also associated with women's sitting posture.
3
Examine the Maliki proof
The Maliki school relies on a hadith that the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) sat mutawarrikan. This hadith is transmitted through 'Abd al-Hamid ibn Ja'far.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds in two ways. First, Imam al-Tahawi declared this hadith weak (da'if) due to the narrator 'Abd al-Hamid ibn Ja'far. Second, even if accepted, it is interpreted as applying specifically to the Prophet's old age when tawarruk was easier.
This exemplifies the Hanafi method of dealing with opposing hadith: either challenge its authenticity (thubut) or reconcile by ta'wil.
5
Apply the Hanafi principle of 'ashaq
The Hanafi school adds a rational argument: iftirash is more strenuous (ashaq) on the body, and in acts of worship, when multiple valid options exist, the more strenuous is considered more virtuous. This reinforces the preference for iftirash.
The principle is 'أَشَقُّهَا أَفْضَلُهَا' (the most strenuous is the most virtuous).

The final sitting is like the first sitting. And he sat in the final (sitting) as he sat in the first, due to the hadith we narrated from Wa'il and 'Aisha, and because it is more strenuous on the body, so it is more virtuous than tawarruk, which Malik inclines to. And the hadith that is narrated that he (peace be upon him) sat mutawarrikan, al-Tahawi declared it weak, and it is interpreted as applicable to the state of old age. Translation: And in the final sitting, he sits in the same manner as he sat in the first sitting, due to the hadith we narrated, i.e., the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr and 'Aisha, and because this posture is more strenuous on the body, so it is more virtuous compared to tawarruk, towards which Imam Malik inclines. And the hadith narrated about tawarruk, that the Prophet (peace be upon him) sat mutawarrikan, Imam al-Tahawi declared it weak, or it is interpreted as applicable to the state of old age. Explanation: He said that in the final sitting, one sits in the same posture as in the first sitting. Imam Malik said that sitting mutawarrikan in both sittings is sunnah. Tawarruk is to sit on the buttocks and extend both feet to the right, as women sit. Imam Malik argues from the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) sat mutawarrikan. Our proof is the hadith we narrated from Wa'il ibn Hujr and 'Aisha (may Allah be pleased with them). Some details of this sitting are in the hadith of Wa'il, and the posture—spreading the left foot and erecting the right—is in the hadith of 'Aisha. Another proof is that sitting in this manner is more strenuous on the body, and in worship, what is more strenuous is more virtuous. Therefore, we say that sitting in this posture is better. As for the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) sat mutawarrikan, Imam al-Tahawi declared it weak because it is narrated through 'Abd al-Hamid ibn Ja'far, and 'Abd al-Hamid is weak according to hadith scholars. The author of al-Hidayah said: If this hadith is accepted as authentic, the response is that this tawarruk sitting is interpreted as applicable to the state of old age, i.e., when the blessed age advanced, he adopted tawarruk.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage addresses an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafis and Malikis regarding the preferred manner of sitting in the final tashahhud. The Hanafi position, based on the Hidayah, is that one should sit in the final tashahhud in the same manner as in the first (iftirash): sitting on the left foot with the right foot erect. The proof is the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr and 'Aisha (may Allah be pleased with them) describing the Prophet's practice, and the principle that the more strenuous posture is more virtuous in worship. Imam Malik, however, holds that tawarruk (sitting on the buttocks with feet extended to the right) is sunnah in both sittings. The Maliki proof is a hadith that the Prophet sat mutawarrikan. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, this hadith is weak (da'if) according to Imam al-Tahawi due to a weak narrator ('Abd al-Hamid ibn Ja'far); second, even if accepted, it can be interpreted as applying to the Prophet's old age when tawarruk was easier. Therefore, the Hanafi school maintains that iftirash is the preferred practice.

Key Terms
تورك (tawarruk): Sitting on the buttocks with both feet protruding to the right side, as women sit.
افتراش (iftirash): Sitting on the left foot with the right foot erect, as in the first tashahhud.
اشق (ashaq): More strenuous; a criterion for preferring one act of worship over another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on sitting in the final tashahhud?
A) It is wajib to sit mutawarrikan.
B) It is mustahab to sit as in the first tashahhud (iftirash).
C) It is fard to sit iftirash.
D) It is makruh to sit iftirash.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prefers iftirash in both tashahhuds, regarding tawarruk as a weak or exceptional practice.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Tashahhud and Salawat: Wajib vs Fard Dispute with Shafi'i
Proving that tashahhud is wajib and salawat is sunnah in Hanafi school, refuting Shafi'i view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tashahhud and salawat, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the fard/wajib distinction and hadith interpretation.

Core Idea
Tashahhud is wajib, not fard — the difference determines whether prayer is invalid or requires compensation.

This lesson examines an inter-madhhab dispute on whether tashahhud and salawat are fard, wajib, or sunnah. The Hanafi school distinguishes between fard (decisive evidence) and wajib (probable evidence), while the Shafi'i school treats them as synonymous. The dispute hinges on the interpretation of a key hadith from Ibn Mas'ud. Understanding this nuance helps you appreciate the precision of Hanafi legal theory and its practical consequences in prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling on tashahhud and salawat according to the Hanafi school as stated in the text: tashahhud is wajib, salawat is sunnah.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i considers both tashahhud and salawat fard. Understand that for him, fard and wajib are the same.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the three arguments from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: (1) the Prophet used the word 'fard' for tashahhud, (2) the imperative 'qulu' indicates obligation, (3) the conditional phrase makes prayer completion dependent on tashahhud.
The text details these as the three istidlal methods.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi rebuttals: (1) 'fard' here means 'taqdir' (decree), not legal obligation; (2) the imperative is for instruction, not obligation; (3) the condition is actually the final sitting, not tashahhud alone, as all agree.
The third response is cut off in the source but we have its essence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider the practical consequence: if tashahhud is omitted, Hanafis require sajda sahw and the prayer is valid; Shafi'is consider the prayer invalid. For salawat, Hanafis require nothing; Shafi'is consider the prayer invalid.
This shows how the fard/wajib distinction affects real practice.

The legal status of tashahhud, statements of jurists and proofs. And he recites tashahhud, and it is wajib according to us, and he sends blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him), and it is not a fard according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i regarding both, because of his (peace be upon him) statement: 'When you have said this or done this, your prayer is complete. If you wish to stand, stand, and if you wish to sit, sit.' And sending blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him) is wajib outside prayer, either once as al-Karkhi said, or every time the Prophet is mentioned as al-Tahawi chose. So the burden of the command is removed from us, and the 'fard' narrated regarding tashahhud means 'taqdir' (decree). Translation: And he recites tashahhud, and it is wajib according to us, and he sends blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him), and it is not a fard according to us. And Imam al-Shafi'i differed regarding both, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When you have said this or done this, your prayer is complete. If you wish to stand, stand, and if you wish to sit, sit.' And sending blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him) is wajib outside prayer, either once as Imam al-Karkhi said, or every time the Prophet is mentioned as Imam al-Tahawi chose. So the great burden of the command is removed from us, and the 'fard' narrated regarding tashahhud means 'taqdir' (decree). Explanation: Reciting tashahhud in the final sitting is wajib according to us, and reciting salawat is not fard but rather sunnah. And according to Imam al-Shafi'i, both reciting tashahhud and sending blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him) are fard. Regarding the fardiyyah of reciting tashahhud, Imam al-Shafi'i argues from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: 'We used to say before tashahhud was made fard: Peace be upon Allah, peace be upon Jibril and Mika'il.' Then the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Say: al-tahiyyatu lillah...' and at the end he said: 'When you have said this or done this, your prayer is complete.' Three proofs are derived from this hadith: First, the Prophet said 'before tashahhud was made fard' attributing fard to tashahhud, so it is established that tashahhud is fard. Second, he said 'Say: al-tahiyyatu lillah', and 'qulu' is an imperative form, and the imperative indicates obligation, so reciting al-tahiyyat is wajib, and according to al-Shafi'i, wajib and fard are the same, so it is fard. Third, the Prophet made the completion of prayer conditional upon this, so without tashahhud the prayer is not complete, and that which is essential for completion is fard. Our response is: In 'before tashahhud was made fard', the word 'fard' is used in its linguistic meaning, i.e., taqdir (decree), as Allah says 'nisfa ma faradtum' meaning 'what you have decreed'. So the meaning is that before tashahhud was decreed, we used to say such and such. Thus, applying the term 'fard' does not necessitate legal obligation. The response to the second proof is that the imperative here is for instruction (ta'lim) and teaching (talqin), so obligation is not established. The response to the third proof is that in the hadith, the completion of prayer is conditional upon one of two things: reciting tashahhud or the final sitting. And there is consensus that the completion of prayer is dependent on the final sitting, because if one leaves the final sitting, the prayer is not valid. So when the prayer is complete...
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is concerning the status of tashahhud and salawat (sending blessings on the Prophet) in prayer. The Hanafi position, as stated in the Hidayah, is that tashahhud is wajib (obligatory but not fard), and salawat is sunnah (recommended, not obligatory). Imam al-Shafi'i holds that both are fard (obligatory with decisive evidence). The Shafi'i proof is based on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, where the Prophet used the term 'fard' regarding tashahhud, issued an imperative ('qulu'), and made the completion of prayer conditional upon it. The Hanafi response refutes each argument: (1) 'fard' in the hadith means 'taqdir' (decree) in the linguistic sense, not legal obligation; (2) the imperative is for instruction, not obligation; (3) the completion of prayer is actually contingent upon the final sitting, not tashahhud alone, as all scholars agree. This passage illustrates the Hanafi methodology of distinguishing between fard and wajib, and the importance of contextual interpretation of hadith.

Key Terms
تشہد (tashahhud): The testimony of faith (al-tahiyyatu lillah...) recited in the final sitting of prayer.
فرض (fard): Obligatory act established by decisive evidence (Quran or mutawatir Sunnah).
واجب (wajib): Obligatory act established by probable evidence (e.g., ahad hadith); omission requires compensation but does not invalidate.
مسنون (sunnah): Recommended act; omission is not sinful and does not require compensation.
تقدیر (taqdir): Decree or determination; in this context, the linguistic meaning of 'fard' as something decreed by Allah, not legal obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of reciting tashahhud in the final sitting?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Mustahab

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between fard and wajib, making tashahhud wajib (requiring sajda sahw if omitted) and salawat sunnah, based on the interpretation of the hadith and consensus on the final sitting.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Hanafi Refutation of Shafi'i Claim that Salawat is Fard in Prayer
Dispute on obligation of salawat in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that salawat in prayer is not fard, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the principle of nafi al-kamal.

Core Idea
The Quranic command is fulfilled outside prayer; in prayer, salawat perfects but is not required.

One of the classic disputes between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools concerns whether sending blessings upon the Prophet (salawat) during prayer is obligatory. Both schools rely on textual proofs, but they interpret the same sources differently. This lesson walks you through the Hanafi refutation of the Shafi'i position, focusing on the key hadith and the principle of nafi al-kamal (negation of perfection). You will learn how the Hanafis maintain that salawat in prayer is a sunnah, not a fard, without contradicting the Quranic command.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proofs
State the Shafi'i claim that salawat is fard in prayer. Identify the two proofs: the Quranic imperative 'صلوا عليه' and the hadith 'لا صلاة لمن لم يصل عليه في صلاته'.
The Shafi'i argument relies on the apparent meaning of command and the literal interpretation of 'لا صلاة' as invalidation.
2
Analyze the Hanafi critique of the Quranic proof
Examine how the Hanafis argue that the command is fulfilled outside prayer. Note the Hanafi positions from al-Karkhi (once in a lifetime) and al-Tahawi (whenever the Prophet is mentioned). This satisfies the command, so it need not be repeated in prayer.
This step shows how Hanafis use the principle that a command does not imply repetition.
3
Analyze the Hanafi critique of the hadith proof
Understand the Hanafi interpretation of 'لا صلاة' as nafi al-kamal (negation of perfection) rather than nafi al-sihhah (negation of validity). Cite the parallel hadith about the neighbor of the mosque as evidence.
The key evidence for this interpretation is that the Prophet omitted salawat when teaching the obligatory acts to the bedouin.
4
Compare the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Contrast the practical outcome: for Hanafis, omitting salawat leaves the prayer valid but incomplete; for Shafi'is, it invalidates the prayer.
The difference matters for fatwa and daily practice.
