حدیث سے استدلال کیا ہے اس طور پر ابن مسعود گو تشہد کی تعلیم دینے کے بعد حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا اذا قلت هذا لو فعلت هذا فقد تمت صلو تک یعنی حضور نے نما پورا ہونا قرأت تشہد اور قعدہ اخیر و ان دونوں میں سے ایک پر معلق کیا ہے پس جس شخص نے صلاۃ علی النبی پر معلق کیا اس نے نفس کو حدیث ابن مسعود کی مخالفت کی۔ اور امام شافعی کا یہ کہنا کہ نماز سے باہر درود بھیجنا واجب نہیں ہمیں یہ بات تسلیم نہیں کیونکہ امام کرختی نے ذکر کیا کہ زندگی میں ایک حضور پیے پر نماز سے باہر درود بھیجنا واجب ہے اس لئے کہ صلوا امر کا صیغہ ہے اور امر تکرار کا تقاضا نہیں کرتا۔ اور امام طحاوی نے فرمایا کہ جب بھی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ذکر کرے یا آپ کا ذکر سنے تو درود بھیجنا واجب ہے لیکن بار بار درود بھیجنا اس لئے واجب نہیں کہ امر تکرار کا تقاضا کی ہے بلکہ اس لئے کہ درود کا وجوب سبب متکرر کے ساتھ متعلق ہے اور وہ سبب متکرر ہونے ہے پس تکرار ذکر سے درود مکرر ہو گیا۔ جیسا کہ اوقات کے تکرار سے نماز کا وجوب مکرر ہو جاتا ہے بہر حال جب نماز سے باہر درود بھیجنا واجب ہو گیا تو صلوا علیہ صیغہ امر پر عمل ہو گیا اور نماز کے اندر درود کے واجب ہونے کو ثابت کرنے کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں رہی۔ امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ حدیث لا صلوۃ لمن لم يصل الخ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حدیث نفی کمال پر محمول ہے یعنی بغیر درود کے نماز کامل نہیں ہوتی جیسا کہ لاصلوۃ لجار المسجد الا فی المسجد میں نفی کمال پر محمول ہے اور اس پر قرینہ یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جب اعرابی کو فرائض نماز کی تعلیم دی ۔ تو اس وقت آپ نے صلوۃ علی النبی کا ذکر نہیں کیا اگر صلوۃ علی النبی فرض ہوتا تو آپا اس کو ضرور ذکر فرماتے۔
Imam al-Shafi'i argued for the obligation of noble salawat based on the saying of Allah Most High: 'O you who believe, send blessings upon him.' In this way, 'send blessings' is a command form, and a command necessitates obligation, and outside prayer sending salawat is not obligatory, so it is established that inside prayer sending salawat is obligatory. The second proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no prayer for the one who does not send blessings upon me in his prayer.' That is, whoever does not send my salawat in his prayer, his prayer is not valid. And it is apparent that the non-validity of prayer occurs due to abandoning an obligatory act, not due to abandoning a sunnah. So it is established that sending salawat is obligatory. As for the non-obligation of salawat upon the Prophet, our scholars argued from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) in this manner: After teaching the tashahhud, the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When you say this, you have completed your prayer.' That is, the Prophet made the completion of prayer conditional upon reciting the tashahhud and the final sitting, on one of these two. So whoever made it conditional upon salawat upon the Prophet has opposed the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud. And as for Imam al-Shafi'i's saying that sending salawat outside prayer is not obligatory, we do not accept this, because Imam al-Karkhi mentioned that sending salawat upon the Prophet once in a lifetime outside prayer is obligatory, because 'send blessings' is a command form and a command does not require repetition. And Imam al-Tahawi said: Whenever he mentions the Prophet (peace be upon him) or hears His mention, sending salawat is obligatory, but repeated sending salawat is not obligatory because the command does not require repetition, but rather because the obligation of salawat is connected to repeated cause and that cause is repeated, so due to repetition of mention, salawat becomes repeated. Just as due to repetition of times, the obligation of prayer becomes repeated. In any case, when sending salawat outside prayer became obligatory, the command 'send blessings upon him' has been acted upon, and there remains no need to prove its obligation inside prayer. The answer to the hadith presented by Imam al-Shafi'i 'There is no prayer for the one who does not send blessings...' is that the hadith is interpreted as negation of perfection, meaning without salawat the prayer is not perfect, just as in 'there is no prayer for the neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque' it is interpreted as negation of perfection. And the evidence for this is that when the Prophet taught the bedouin the obligatory acts of prayer, he did not mention salawat upon the Prophet at that time. If salawat upon the Prophet were obligatory, he would definitely have mentioned it.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning whether sending salawat (blessings) upon the Prophet in prayer is obligatory (fard) or not. Imam al-Shafi'i argues for its obligation using two proofs: the Quranic command 'صلوا علیه' (send blessings upon him) which he interprets as a command implying obligation, and the hadith 'لا صلاة لمن لم يصل علی في صلاته' (no prayer for one who does not send blessings upon me in his prayer) which he takes as invalidating prayer if omitted. The Hanafi response refutes both. First, they argue that the Quranic command is fulfilled by sending salawat outside prayer, as it is obligatory once in a lifetime (according to al-Karkhi) or whenever the Prophet is mentioned (according to al-Tahawi). Thus the command is already satisfied, and there is no need to make it obligatory within prayer. Second, they interpret the hadith as a negation of perfection (nafi al-kamal) rather than validity, citing the analogy of 'لا صلاة لجار المسجد إلا في المسجد' (no prayer for the neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque), which means the prayer is not perfect outside the mosque, not that it is invalid. They further support this by noting that when the Prophet taught a bedouin the obligatory elements of prayer, he did not mention salawat, indicating it is not fard. The Hanafi position is that salawat in prayer is sunnah, not fard. The dispute shows the Hanafi reliance on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, where the Prophet made completion of prayer conditional upon tashahhud and final sitting, not salawat.

Key Terms
صلوۃ علی النبی (salawat 'ala al-nabi): Sending blessings upon the Prophet Muhammad
نفی کمال (nafi al-kamal): Negation of perfection; the statement indicates something is not perfect rather than invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, how is the Shafi'i hadith 'لا صلاة لمن لم يصل عليه في صلاته' interpreted?
A) It refers to the invalidity of prayer
B) It refers to the perfection of prayer
C) It is abrogated
D) It applies only to the imam

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that sending salawat in prayer is sunnah, not fard, because the Quranic command is fulfilled outside prayer and the hadith of negation is interpreted as a lack of perfection, not validity.

The Recommended Wording for Salawat in Prayer
Ruling on the specific wording for salawat in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred Hanafi wording for salawat in prayer and explain its basis in the hadith.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school prescribes a specific wording for salawat in prayer, taught by Imam Abu Hanifa and confirmed by prophetic hadith.

Sending salutations upon the Prophet (saw) is a key part of the final tashahhud in prayer. This lesson examines the specific wording recommended by Imam Abu Hanifa and its foundation in the Sunnah. Understanding this ensures our worship aligns with the prophetic model.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Determine what act is being discussed and its legal status. The act is sending salawat (blessings) upon the Prophet in the final tashahhud. According to the Hanafi school, it is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
2
Locate the Daleel
Find the proof cited by Imam Abu Hanifa. The passage mentions the hadith of Ka'b ibn 'Ujrah and the narration from 'Ali, Ibn 'Abbas, and Jabir (ra) who directly asked the Prophet how to send salawat.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves the recommended wording. The Prophet explicitly taught the Companions a specific phrasing, which indicates that this wording is the sunnah. The imperative form ("Say: Allahumma salli...") shows desirability.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf (if any)
Check if there is any disagreement within or outside the Hanafi school. The passage states all Hanafis agree on this wording. The Shafi'i school similarly uses a version of this wording, showing broad acceptance.
5
Apply the Ruling in Practice
In your own prayer, recite the wording: 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad wa 'ala aali Muhammad kama sallayta 'ala Ibraheem wa 'ala aali Ibraheem innaka Hameedun Majeed.' This fulfills the sunnah.

Source Text

فوائد رہی یہ بات کہ آپ پریس کیفیت کے ساتھ درود بھیجے تو اس بارے میں عیسی بن ابان نے کتاب الجھے علی اہل المدینہ میں ذکر کیا کہ امام سے صلوۃ النبی کے بارے میں دریافت کیا گیا تو فرمایا کہ یہ کہئے اللهم صلى على محمد وعلى آل محمد كما صليت على ابراهيم وعلى آل ابراهیم انک حمید مجید صاحب کفایہ نے لکھا کہ یہ درود کعب بن عجرہ کی حدیث کے موافق ہے۔ حضرت علی ابن عباس اور جابر رضی اللہ عنہم نے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے کہا کہ ہم کو آپ پر سلام بھیجنے کا طریقہ تو معلوم ہے لیکن درود کس طرح بھیجیں پس آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا یوں کہو اللهم صلى على محمد واعلى ال محمد و بارک علی محمد وعلى آل محمد وارحم محمد اوال محمد کما صلیت و بارکت و ترحمت على ابراهيم وعلى آل ابراهیم فی العالمین ایک طور که حمید مجید۔
Benefits: This matter that you send salawat upon him in such a manner, regarding this 'Isa ibn Aban mentioned in the book 'al-Hujjah 'ala Ahl al-Madinah' that Imam (Abu Hanifa) was asked about salawat upon the Prophet, and he said: Say: 'O Allah, send blessings upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad as You sent blessings upon Ibrahim and upon the family of Ibrahim; indeed You are Praiseworthy, Glorious.' The author of al-Kifayah wrote that this salawat is in accordance with the hadith of Ka'b ibn 'Ujrah. 'Ali, Ibn 'Abbas, and Jabir (may Allah be pleased with them) said to the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'We know how to send salam upon you, but how should we send salawat?' So the Prophet said: 'Say: O Allah, send blessings upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad, and bless Muhammad and the family of Muhammad, and have mercy on Muhammad and the family of Muhammad, as You sent blessings, blessed, and had mercy upon Ibrahim and the family of Ibrahim in the worlds. Indeed You are Praiseworthy, Glorious.'
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on the preferred wording for sending salawat upon the Prophet in prayer. It begins with a benefit: the specific wording that Imam Abu Hanifa taught, which matches the hadith of Ka'b bin 'Ujrah. This wording includes sending blessings upon Muhammad and his family, modeled after the blessings upon Ibrahim and his family. The passage then recounts a narration from Ali, Ibn Abbas, and Jabir (may Allah be pleased with them) who asked the Prophet how to send salawat, and he taught them a similar but slightly expanded wording: 'O Allah, send blessings upon Muhammad and the family of Muhammad, and bless Muhammad and the family of Muhammad, and have mercy on Muhammad and the family of Muhammad, as You sent blessings, blessed, and had mercy upon Ibrahim and the family of Ibrahim in the worlds. Indeed You are Praiseworthy, Glorious.' This demonstrates that the recommended wording is based on prophetic instruction and has been transmitted in multiple authentic narrations. The Hanafi school adopts this wording as sunnah in the final tashahhud.

Key Terms
صلوۃ علی النبی (salawat 'ala al-nabi): The specific formula of sending blessings upon the Prophet

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends reciting the specific wording of salawat taught by the Prophet in the final tashahhud, as transmitted by Imam Abu Hanifa and confirmed by multiple Companions.

Ruling on Supplication in the Final Sitting of Prayer
Ruling on supplication with evidence from hadith and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on supplication in the final sitting of prayer and identify which conditions make it valid or invalid.

Core Idea
Supplication in prayer must be in Arabic and resemble Quranic or prophetic phrases; non-Arabic is makruh tahrimi.

After reciting tashahhud and salawat in the final sitting, it is recommended to make supplication. However, not every supplication is permissible. The Hanafi school sets specific conditions: the words must be in Arabic, resemble divine or prophetic speech, and avoid everyday conversation. This lesson unpacks the evidence and practical implications from the Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is making supplication (dua) in the final sitting after tashahhud and salawat. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
This is a recommended act, not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Then choose the purest and most pleasing supplication to you.' This indicates the permissibility and recommendation of supplication.
The hadith is ahad (single narration), thus zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'choose' (ikhtar) is understood by Hanafi usul as indicating recommendation (nadb), not obligation. The Prophet's approval of various supplications shows that any good supplication is permissible.
This is a clear proof for the sunnah status.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools allow supplication in languages other than Arabic if one cannot speak Arabic. The Hanafi school considers it makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) because it deviates from the prescribed form of prayer.
The practical difference: a non-Arabic speaker may sin unintentionally according to Hanafis.
5
Apply the conditions
The supplication must (1) be in Arabic, (2) resemble words of the Quran or prophetic supplications, and (3) avoid words that resemble the everyday speech of people, as this may corrupt the prayer.
Examples: 'O Allah, forgive me' is allowed; 'O Allah, marry me to so-and-so' is not.

بالمأثور المحفوظ وما لا يستخيل سواله من العباد لقوله اللهم زوجنى فلانة يشبه كلامهم وما يستحيل كقوله اللهم اغفر لي ليس من كلامهم وقوله اللهم ارزقني من قبيل الأول لاستعمالها فيما بين العباد يقال رزق الامير الجيش
He said: And he supplicates with words resembling the words of the Quran and the transmitted supplications, because of the hadith we narrated from Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to him: 'Then choose the purest and most pleasing supplication to you.' And he begins with salutation upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) so that it is closer to acceptance. [Translation:] The author said: He supplicates with words resembling the words of Quran and transmitted supplications due to the hadith we narrated, i.e., the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet said: 'Then choose the supplication that is most pure and pleasing to you.' And he begins with salawat upon the Prophet to be closer to acceptance. Explanation of the issue: In the final sitting, after salawat upon the Prophet, he supplicates in the Arabic language, because supplicating in prayer in a language other than Arabic is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi). Then it is clear that the words of supplication should resemble the words of the Holy Quran, for example the saying of Allah Most High: 'Say: My Lord, forgive me and my parents and whoever enters my house believing, and the believing men and women on the Day when the account is established.' Or they should resemble the supplications transmitted from the Prophet, such as the narration from Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said to the Messenger of Allah: 'Teach me, O Messenger of Allah, a supplication with which I supplicate in my prayer.' He said: 'Say: O Allah, I have wronged myself greatly, and none forgives sins except You, so forgive me with forgiveness from You; indeed You are the Oft-Forgiving, the Most Merciful.' 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) used to supplicate with these words: 'O Allah, I ask You for all good, what I know and what I do not know, and I seek refuge in You from all evil, what I know and what I do not know.' The proof for this is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, i.e., 'When he is at the end of the prayer, he supplicates for himself whatever he wishes.' Then at the end of this hadith, the Prophet said to Ibn Mas'ud: 'Then choose the most pleasing and purest supplication to you.' 'Its most pleasing and purest' with masculine pronoun agrees with the narration of some, but in some copies of Hidayah it is 'the most pleasing and purest' with feminine pronoun, but that is not correct, and if it is considered correct with feminine pronoun, it is interpreted as referring to supplications or words. The author of Hidayah said: He first sends blessings upon the Prophet, then supplicates, so that it is closer to acceptance. The proof is that supplication for the Prophet will definitely be accepted, and it is distant from the Generous One that He would accept some supplication and not accept some; rather He will accept the entire supplication. He refrains from supplications that resemble the speech of people! And he does not supplicate with what resembles the speech of people, as a precaution against corruption. Therefore, he uses the transmitted and preserved supplications and what is not inconceivable to ask from created beings. For example, his saying 'O Allah, marry me to so-and-so' resembles their speech, and what is inconceivable like 'O Allah, forgive me' is not their speech. His saying 'O Allah, provide for me' is of the former type because it is used among people; one says 'the commander provided for the army.'
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on supplication (dua) in the final sitting of prayer. The author states that after reciting tashahhud and salawat, it is recommended to make supplication in Arabic using words that resemble Quranic verses or those transmitted from the Prophet. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud in which the Prophet told him to choose the most pure and pleasing supplication. The commentary explains that supplication in prayer must be in Arabic; using any other language is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) because it deviates from the established form. The preferred supplications are those mentioned in the Quran, such as 'Rabbi ighfir li...' (My Lord, forgive me) and those taught by the Prophet, like the supplication of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq and the comprehensive dua of Ibn Mas'ud. The author emphasizes starting with salawat upon the Prophet to increase the likelihood of acceptance, based on the reasoning that supplication for the Prophet is always accepted, so including it makes the entire dua more likely to be accepted. Additionally, one must avoid supplications that resemble the everyday speech of people, as this may corrupt the prayer. Examples of forbidden phrases include asking for marriage or worldly favors in a manner common among people, while phrases like 'O Allah, forgive me' are acceptable because they are not spoken among people. The ruling distinguishes between what is inconceivable to ask from creatures (like forgiveness) and what is conceivable (like wealth, which people ask from each other), deeming the latter as resembling human speech and thus disliked in prayer.

Key Terms
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): An act that is forbidden to the extent of being sinful but without decisive evidence; close to haram.
ماثور (ma'thur): Supplications that are transmitted from the Prophet or the righteous predecessors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on supplicating in a language other than Arabic in prayer?
A) Permissible if one does not know Arabic
B) Sunnah
C) Makruh tahrimi
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
Supplication in the final sitting is a sunnah act that must be in Arabic and avoid everyday speech; non-Arabic is makruh tahrimi.

Performing the Concluding Salam (Taslim) in Prayer: Manner and Intention
Ruling on saying salam to right and left with proper intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the manner of the concluding salam and explain whom the worshipper should intend.

Core Idea
The salam is wajib to both sides; intention is required, but women are not intended in our time.

This passage from Al-Hidayah details the performance of the concluding salam in prayer. It establishes the sunnah manner based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and addresses the important issue of intention (niyyah) in the salam. The author also clarifies a later Hanafi position regarding women in congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the concluding salam (taslim) in prayer. According to the Hanafi school, it is wajib (obligatory) and must be performed by turning the head to the right and left while saying 'As-salamu alaykum wa rahmatullah'.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) describing the Prophet's (peace be upon him) practice: he would turn his face until the whiteness of his cheek was seen on each side. This establishes the manner of salam.
This hadith is ahad (single transmission), so its thubut is zanni, but Hanafis accept it for establishing a wajib.
3
Understand the intention (niyyah) in salam
In the first salam, the worshipper intends those on his right: the congregation (men and women) and the guardian angels. Similarly for the left salam. The principle is that actions are judged by intentions.
The intention is what distinguishes the salam as an address to those present, not just a word.
4
Note the later Hanafi position on women and absentees
In the time of the author (and in our time), women do not typically attend congregational prayer, so the mufta bihi (relied-upon opinion) is not to intend women. Similarly, one should not intend those who have no share in the prayer (e.g., people not praying). This is because the salam is an address to those present.
This is an intra-Hanafi refinement; the earlier view included women, but later scholars preferred exclusion due to absence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يسلم عن يمينه فيقول السلام عليكم ورحمة الله وعن يسارة مثل ذلك لماروى ابن مسعود ان الله عليه السلام كان يسلم عن يمينه حتى يرى بياض خده الايمن وعن يساره حق یری بیاض خده الابر ونوى بالتسليم الأولى من على يمينه من الرجال والنساء والحفظة كذلك فى الثانية لان الاعمال بالب ولا ينوى النساء في زماننا ولا من لا شركة له في صلاته هو الصحيح لان الخطاب حظ الحاضر ترجمہ پھر اپنی دائیں طرف سلام پھیرے پھر کہے السلام علیکم ورحمتہ اللہ اور اپنی بائیں طرف اس کے مثل کیونکہ ابن مسعود نے روایت کی کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم اپنی دائیں طرف سلام پھیرتے تھے حتی کہ آپ کے دائیں رخسار کی سفیدی دیکھی جاتی تھی۔ اور بائیں جانب یہاں کہ آپ کے بائیں رخسار کی سفیدی دیکھی جاتی تھی اور پہلے سلام سے ان کی نیت کرے جو اس کے دائیں جانب ہوں خواہ مرد ہوں یا عورتیں اور ملائکہ حفظہ اور اسی طرح دوسرے سلام میں کیونکہ اعمال کا مدار نیتوں پر ہے اور ہمارے زمانے میں (امام) عورتوں کی نسبت نہ کرنا نہ ایسے شخص کی نیت کرے جس کو اس کی نماز میں شرکت نہیں۔ یہی قول صحیح ہے کیونکہ خطاب حاضرین کا حصہ ہے۔
Then he gives salam to his right, saying 'As-salamu alaykum wa rahmatullah', and to his left similarly, because Ibn Mas'ud narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would give salam to his right until the whiteness of his right cheek was seen, and to his left until the whiteness of his left cheek was seen. And he intends by the first salam those on his right, whether men or women and the guardian angels, and similarly in the second, because actions are by intentions. And in our time, he does not intend women, nor does he intend one who has no share in his prayer. This is the correct opinion, because the address is the portion of those present.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on how to perform the concluding salam in prayer. The author states that after tashahhud, the worshipper turns his head to the right and says 'As-salamu alaykum wa rahmatullah', then to the left and says the same. This is based on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud reporting the Prophet's practice, indicating that the salam is said while turning the face enough to show the whiteness of the cheek. The intention in the salam is important: in the first salam, one should intend those on the right, including the congregation (men and women) and the guardian angels. Similarly for the second salam. However, the commentary notes that in our time (i.e., the time of the author), women are not intended because they do not attend congregational prayer, and one should not intend those who have no share in his prayer (e.g., people not praying). This is the correct position because the address of salam is for those present. The principle is that actions are judged by intentions.

Key Terms
التسليم (al-taslim): The concluding salutation of the prayer, saying 'As-salamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' to the right and left.
نية (niyyah): Intention in the salam to direct the address to those present on that side.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The salam must be said to both sides with intention; the mufta bihi is to intend only those present in congregation (men and angels), excluding women in our time unless they are present.

Du'a Resembling Human Speech After Tashahhud
Ruling on du'a resembling human speech in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible and invalidating du'a after tashahhud based on the Hanafi criterion of resemblance to kalam an-nas, and apply the rule that after tashahhud even actual kalam an-nas does not invalidate.

Core Idea
After tashahhud, du'a resembling human speech does not invalidate prayer; before tashahhud it does.

This passage from a Hanafi commentary clarifies a critical nuance: while du'a that resembles ordinary conversation is generally prohibited during prayer, the timing matters. The author explains that after the tashahhud and salawat, the prayer is considered complete, so any speech-like du'a does not break it. You will learn the criterion for 'resemblance to human speech' and the practical implications for your salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between du'a resembling human speech before tashahhud and after tashahhud. Before tashahhud, it invalidates the prayer; after tashahhud, it does not.
This is the central distinction.
2
Analyze the criterion for kalam an-nas
The du'a resembles human speech if the request could be made to a human (e.g., marriage, provision). If it is impossible to ask from humans (e.g., forgiveness), it does not resemble kalam an-nas.
The proof given: such phrases are commonly used among people.
3
Apply the talil (legal reasoning)
After tashahhud, actual human speech does not invalidate the prayer because the prayer is considered complete and the speaker has exited it by choice. By greater reason, speech resembling human speech also does not invalidate.
This is a qiyas awlawi (a fortiori) argument.
4
Note the authority
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and Imam Abu Hanifa all agree that after tashahhud such du'a does not invalidate.
The text cites 'Inayah' for this ruling.
5
Derive the practical rule
Use ma'thurat (transmitted) du'as to avoid any resemblance. If one inadvertently uses a du'a that resembles kalam an-nas after tashahhud, the prayer remains valid.
However, before tashahhud, such du'a would invalidate the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صفۃ الصلوة
۷۲
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایه
ترجمہ اور ایسے الفاظ کے ساتھ دعا نہ کرے جو لوگوں کے کلام سے مشابہ ہوں۔ فساد نماز سے بچنے کی وجہ سے اور اسی وجہ سے ماثورہ دعاؤں کو جو محفوظ ہیں پڑھے اور جس چیز کا مانگنا بندوں سے محال نہ ہو جیسے اس کا قول اللهم زوجني فلانة كلام الناس کے ہے اور جس چیز کا مانگنا محال ہو جیسے اس کا قول اللهم اغفر لی تو یہ کلام الناس سے نہیں ہے۔ اور مصلی کا کہنا اللهم ارزقنی قسم اول ہے کیونکہ یہ کلام لوگوں میں باہم مستعمل ہے ( چنانچہ ) کہا جاتا ہے رزق الا میر انیش امیر نے لشکر کو رزق دیا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ صلوۃ علی النبی کے بعد ایسے الفاظ کے ساتھ دعا نہ کرے جو لوگوں کے کلام سے مشابہ ہوں تا کہ نماز کار

لوگوں میں باہم مستعمل ہے چنانچہ کہا جاتا ہے رزق الا میر انجیش امیر نے لشکر کو رزق دیا۔
Chapter on Description of Prayer. 72. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Bidaya. Translation: And do not make du'a with words that resemble the speech of people, due to avoiding corruption of prayer, and for that reason recite the preserved du'as. And what it is not impossible to ask from servants, like his saying: O Allah, marry me to so-and-so, is of the speech of people. And what it is impossible to ask, like his saying: O Allah, forgive me, is not of the speech of people. And the prayer's saying: O Allah, provide for me, is of the first type because this speech is mutually used among people. (Thus) it is said: The amir provided sustenance to the army. Explanation: The issue is that after salutation upon the Prophet, do not make du'a with words resembling people's speech so that the prayer's connection to the speech of people is protected from corruption. For that reason it is said that the one praying should recite the transmitted du'as. Du'a resembling human speech corrupts prayer. It should be clear that if after tashahhud one makes du'a with words resembling human speech, the entire prayer will not become corrupt because after tashahhud if actual human speech occurs, prayer does not become corrupt. So if it is speech resembling human speech, a fortiori the prayer will not become corrupt. This ruling is apparent according to the Sahibayn, and similarly according to Imam Abu Hanifa it will not become corrupt because human speech from the praying person is exiting the prayer by choice, so his prayer will be complete, and that du'a which is made with words resembling human speech after tashahhud will be outside the prayer, not that it corrupts the prayer. (Inayah) The meaning of resembling human speech: Now, regarding which du'a resembles human speech and which does not, it is said that what it is not impossible to ask from servants, like saying: O Allah, marry me to so-and-so, resembles human speech. And what it is impossible to ask from servants, like saying: O Allah, forgive me, does not resemble human speech. The one praying saying: O Allah, provide for me is of the first type, i.e., resembles human speech. This is correct. The proof is that it is commonly used among people, thus it is said: The amir provided sustenance to the army.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on the chapter of prayer discusses the ruling on making du'a after the tashahhud and salutation upon the Prophet. The author, a Hanafi scholar, states that one should not make du'a with words that resemble the ordinary speech of people (kalam an-nas), because such du'a could invalidate the prayer. The reason is that speech resembling human conversation breaks the sanctity of prayer. To be safe, one should use the transmitted du'as (ma'thurat) that are preserved from the Prophet. The commentator then clarifies the criterion: If the request is something that can be asked from a human being (like marriage), it resembles human speech; if it is impossible to ask from humans (like forgiveness), it does not. He gives the example of asking for sustenance (rizq), which is commonly asked from people, so it falls under the prohibited category. However, a crucial distinction is made: This prohibition applies before the tashahhud. After the tashahhud, if one utters actual human speech, the prayer is still valid according to the majority (Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn), because the prayer is considered complete and the speech is an exit from prayer. By greater reason, speech resembling human speech after tashahhud does not invalidate the prayer. This is based on the principle that exiting the prayer by choice completes it, and any speech after that is outside the prayer. The passage thus provides a nuanced ruling combining caution and leniency.

Key Terms
کلام الناس (kalam an-nas): Ordinary human speech or conversation, as opposed to religious formulas.
ماثورہ دعاؤں (ma'thurat du'a): Transmitted supplications from the Prophet, preserved in the Sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because it is asking for worldly sustenance from Allah.
B) No, because after tashahhud even actual human speech does not invalidate.
C) Yes, because it resembles the speech of people.
D) No, because asking for sustenance is a form of dhikr.

Key Takeaway
After tashahhud, du'a that resembles human speech does not invalidate the Hanafi prayer, though it is recommended to use transmitted supplications.

Salam at the End of Prayer: Number and Intention
Rulings on the final salam and whom to intend

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of final salams, explain the proof from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, and apply the rules of intention in salam, including exceptions in later times.

Core Idea
The Hanafi prayer ends with two salams to the sides, intending only those present in prayer.

In this lesson, we examine the final salam of the prayer: how many, when, and for whom we intend. The Hanafi school establishes two salams based on the practice of the Prophet as reported by Ibn Mas'ud. We also explore the reasoning behind whom to intend and the exceptions in later practice, including the intra-Hanafi difference between Sahib al-Hidayah and Hakim Shahid.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on salams
The prayer ends with two salams: first to the right, then to the left, saying 'Assalamu alaikum wa rahmatullah' each time. This is considered wajib; omission requires sajdah as-sahw.
Hanafis view the salam as a wajib component, not a rukn.
2
Identify the primary dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: the Prophet made salam to his right until his right cheek was visible, and to his left until his left cheek was visible.
This hadith is transmitted by multiple companions, giving it strength.
3
Respond to the Maliki objection
Imam Malik holds that one salam to the front suffices, citing Aisha and Sahl ibn Sa'd. The Hanafi response is that the senior companion's narration is preferred, and the second salam may not have been heard by those in the back rows due to lower voice.
This illustrates the Hanafi method of tarjih (preference) between conflicting narrations.
4
Determine the intention for each salam
With the first salam, intend those on your right (men, women, and guardian angels). With the second, intend those on your left. This is because actions are by intentions and the salam is an address to those present.
Intending angels is based on their presence recording deeds.
5
Apply the principle in later times
In later eras, women do not attend congregation, so they are not intended. Also, do not intend those who are not participating in the prayer (e.g., non-praying individuals). Hakim Shahid disagreed, but the correct view (mufta bihi) is to restrict intention to present participants.
The salam is an address (khitab), and address is only for those present.

مصنف نے کہا کہ پہلا سلام پھیر تے وقت ان لوگوں کی نیت کرے جو اس کے دائیں جانب ہیں خواہ مرد ہوں خواہ عورتیں اور ملائکہ حفظہ کی نیت کرے اور اسی طرح بائیں طرف سلام پھیرتے وقت ان کی نیت کرے جو اس کی بائیں طرف ہیں۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اعمال کا مدار نیت پر ہے جیسا کہ حدیث میں ہے صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ ہمارے زمانے میں عورتوں کی نیت نہ کرے کیونکہ اس زمانہ میں عورتوں کا جماعت میں حاضر ہونا با جماع متاخرین متروک ہے۔ اور جو مسلمان نماز میں شریک نہیں ان کی بھی نیت نہ کرے یہی صحیح قول ہے اور حاکم شہید نے کہا کہ تمام مردوں اور عورتوں کی نیت کرے خواہ نماز میں شریک ہوں یا شریک نہ ہوں تا کہ سلام تشہد یعنی السلام علينا وعلی عباداللہ الصالحین کے موافق ہو جائے اور قول صحیح کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سلام تحیہ خطاب ہے اور خطاب حاضرین کا حصہ ہے اس لئے جو لوگ نماز میں شریک نہیں ان کو یہ سلام شامل نہیں ہوگا۔ اس کے برعکس سلام تشہد کہ وہ تحیتہ عامہ ہے اللہ کے تمام نیک بندوں کو خواہ حاضر ہوں خواہ غائب ہوں چنانچہ حضور پیر نے فرمایا اذا قال المصلى السلام علينا وعلی عباد الله الصالحين اصاب كل عبدا صالح من اهل السماء و الارض یعنی نمازی جب السلام علينا وعلى عباد الله الصالحین کہتا ہے تو وہ اور اہل ارض میں سے اللہ کے ہر نیک بندے کو پہنچتا ہے۔
Salam to the right and left; whose intention in salam. Then he makes salam to his right saying 'Assalamu alaikum wa rahmatullah' and to his left similarly, because it is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet used to make salam to his right until the whiteness of his right cheek was visible, and to his left until the whiteness of his left cheek was visible. And with the first salam he intends those on his right, men and women and the guardian angels; similarly in the second, because actions are by intentions. And in our time, he does not intend women, nor anyone who does not participate in his prayer; this is the correct view, because the address is the portion of those present. Translation: Then he makes salam to his right saying 'Assalamu alaikum wa rahmatullah' and to his left similarly, because Ibn Mas'ud narrated that the Prophet used to make salam to his right until the whiteness of his right cheek was visible, and to his left until the whiteness of his left cheek was visible. And with the first salam he intends those on his right, whether men or women, and the guardian angels; similarly in the second, because actions are by intentions. And in our time, he does not intend women nor anyone who does not participate in his prayer; this is the correct view, because the address is the portion of those present.
Volume 2 Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume 2
73
Chapter on Description of Prayer
Explanation: The gist of this passage is that after tashahhud, salutation upon the Prophet, and du'a, he makes salam on both sides, first right then left similarly. And the wording of salam is 'Assalamu alaikum wa rahmatullah'. This is the madhhab of the majority of scholars and senior companions like Umar, Ali, and Abdullah ibn Sa'd. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet used to make salam to his right until the whiteness of his right cheek was visible, and to his left until the whiteness of his left cheek was visible. As for Imam Malik who said there is only one salam to the front, and he cited the narration of Aisha and Sahl ibn Sa'd as-Sa'idi that the Prophet did that, our response is that adopting the statement of senior companions is preferable over Imam Malik's statement. As for Aisha and Sahl narrating one salam, the answer is that Aisha was in the women's row and Sahl in the children's row; it is possible they did not hear the second salam because the Prophet's second salam was with a lower voice than the first. So with this possibility, the hadith of Aisha and Sahl is not admissible as proof. The author said that when making the first salam, he intends those on his right, whether men or women, and the guardian angels; similarly when making the left salam, he intends those on his left. The proof is that actions are by intention as in the hadith. Sahib al-Hidayah says that in our time, he does not intend women because in our time women's presence in congregation is abandoned by the later scholars. And he does not intend any Muslim who does not participate in his prayer; this is the correct view. Hakim Shahid said that he should intend all men and women, whether participating in prayer or not, so that the salam corresponds to the tashahhud greeting 'Assalamu alaina wa ala ibadillah as-salihin'. And the proof for the correct view is that the salam is a greeting of address, and the address is the portion of those present, so those not present in prayer are not included in this greeting. In contrast, the salam of tashahhud is a general greeting to all righteous servants of Allah, whether present or absent, as the Pir said: When the praying person says 'Assalamu alaina wa ala ibadillah as-salihin', it reaches every righteous servant of Allah from the people of heaven and earth.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah commentary addresses the final salam in prayer. It establishes that the prayer concludes with two salams: turning to the right and to the left, saying 'Assalamu alaikum wa rahmatullah'. The primary proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud describing the Prophet's practice. The commentator then addresses the opinion of Imam Malik, who held that only one salam to the front is sufficient. The Hanafi response is that the narrations from senior companions (Ibn Mas'ud) are preferred, and the narrations of Aisha and Sahl (who reported one salam) are explained by the possibility that they did not hear the second salam due to its lower volume. Thus, two salams are established. Regarding intention, the author rules that with the first salam one intends those on his right (including men, women, and angels), and similarly for the left. However, in current times (according to the text), women are not intended because their attendance in congregation has been abandoned. Additionally, one should not intend those who are not participating in the prayer (e.g., those not praying). This is based on the principle that the salam is an address, and an address is directed only to those present. There is a difference with Hakim Shahid, who held that all believers should be intended to include the general greeting of tashahhud, but the text prefers restricting to present participants.

Key Terms
سلام (salam): The final salutation ending the prayer, recited as 'Assalamu alaikum wa rahmatullah'.
حفظہ (hafazah): Guardian angels, believed to be present recording deeds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis perform two salams at the end of prayer?
A) Because it is a fard according to the Quran.
B) Based on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud describing the Prophet's practice.
C) Because Imam Malik also taught two salams.
D) To ensure the prayer is valid if one salam is missed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi prayer ends with two wajib salams to the sides, and the intention in salam is directed only to those present in the prayer (including angels), not to all believers.

The Follower's Intention for the Imam in Salam
Intra-Hanafi dispute on intention in salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on whether the follower intends the imam in both salams when directly behind, and explain the reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
When the follower is directly behind, the imam has a share from both sides – Muhammad includes him in both salams; Abu Yusuf gives preference to the right.

This passage addresses a subtle point in congregational prayer: whom does the follower intend when making salam? While it is necessary (la budda) to intend the imam, the exact application differs when the imam is directly ahead. The Hanafi school presents two views, reflecting different analyses of the imam's 'share' in the salams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the text is about the follower's intention in the final salam. The ruling is that intending the imam is necessary (wajib) for the validity of the salam.
The phrase 'la budda' indicates necessity, not mere recommendation.
2
Distinguish the imam's position
Note the two scenarios: imam on the right/left vs. directly in front (bihidha'ihi). The rule differs based on position.
When on a side, the follower intends the imam only in the corresponding side's salam.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's position
When directly in front, Abu Yusuf says the follower intends the imam only in the first salam (to the right), citing preference (tarjih) for the right side.
ABU YUSUF: The imam's share is primarily on the right.
4
Analyze Muhammad's position
Muhammad (and a narration from Abu Hanifa) holds that the follower intends the imam in both salams, because the imam has a share (hazz) from both sides.
MUHAMMAD/ABU HANIFA: The imam is equally related to both salams.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Yusuf's view, the second salam is addressed only to others (angels, Muslims to the left); under Muhammad's view, both salams include the imam.
This affects whether the follower's second salam is valid if he omitted the imam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقتدی سلام میں امام کی نیت بھی کرے گا یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء
ولابد للمقتدى من نية امامه، فان كان الامام من الجانب الايمن او الايسر نواه فيهم وان كان بحذائه نواه في الأولى عند ابي يوسف ترجيحا لجانب الايمن وعند محمد وهو رواية عن ابي حنيفة نواه فيهما لانه ذو حظ من الجانبين ترجمہ اور مقتدی کے لئے امام کی نیت کرنا بھی ضروری ہے پس اگر دائیں طرف ہو یا بائیں طرف تو ان میں اس کی نیت کرے اور اگر
Whether the follower should also intend the imam in salam? Statements of jurists. And it is necessary for the follower to intend his imam. So if the imam is on the right side or left side, he intends him among them. And if he is facing him (directly in front), he intends him in the first (salam) according to Abu Yusuf, preferring the right side. And according to Muhammad, and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa, he intends him in both (salams) because he has a share from both sides. Translation: And it is necessary for the follower to also intend the imam. So if the imam is on the right or left side, he intends him among them. And if he is facing him directly, he intends him in the first according to Abu Yusuf, preferring the right side. And according to Muhammad, and a narration from Abu Hanifa, he intends him in both because he has a share from both sides.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This short passage discusses the muqtadi's intention for the imam during the final salam. The text states that it is necessary (la budda) for the follower to intend the imam when making salam. If the imam is located to the right or left of the follower, the follower should include the imam in the intention of the corresponding salam (right or left). If the imam is directly in front (in line), there is an intra-Hanafi difference: According to Abu Yusuf, the follower intends the imam only in the first salam (to the right), giving preference to the right side. According to Muhammad (and a narration from Abu Hanifa), the follower intends the imam in both salams because the imam has a share from both sides (i.e., he is simultaneously on the right and left relative to the follower? Or because both salams address him). This difference stems from whether the imam's position relative to the follower is considered as being on one side or both. The text does not give a preference, but it highlights the ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
بحذائه (bihidha'ihi): Directly facing or in line with the imam (i.e., neither to the right nor left).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad (and a narration from Abu Hanifa), if the follower is directly facing the imam, in how many salams should he intend the imam?
A) In none of the salams.
B) Only in the first salam.
C) Only in the second salam.
D) In both salams.

Key Takeaway
When the follower is directly behind the imam, the preferred Hanafi view is to intend the imam in both salams because the imam has a share from both sides.

The Manner of Taslīm (Salutation) in Prayer
Describes the wording and method of taslīm with proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of taslīms in prayer, cite the proof from the hadith of Ibn Masʿūd, and explain the rebuttal to the Maliki position.

Core Idea
Two salutations (taslīm) end the prayer: right then left, based on the Prophet's example.

The taslīm is the final act of the prayer, marking its completion. This passage clarifies the precise method: two salutations, first to the right then to the left, with the specific words 'al-salāmu ʿalaykum wa raḥmatu llāh'. The author presents the proof from the Prophet's practice and addresses a disagreement with Imam Mālik, showing how the Hanafi school establishes its position through strong companion testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the taslīm (salutation) at the end of prayer. The Hanafi ruling is that two taslīms are performed: first to the right, then to the left.
The wording is specified as 'al-salāmu ʿalaykum wa raḥmatu llāh'.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Masʿūd, which describes the Prophet's practice of turning his head until the whiteness of his cheek was visible on each side.
This action (fiʿl) is the primary evidence.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the opposing view
Imam Mālik argued for one taslīm based on narrations from ʿĀʾishah and Sahl. The Hanafi response explains that those narrators might not have heard the second taslīm due to lower voice and their distance in the rows.
This response preserves the stronger proof of the senior companions.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis perform two taslīms; Mālikis perform one (to the front). This affects how one prays in congregation and individually.
Knowing this helps avoid confusion when following different imams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صفۃ الصلوة نمازی تشریح اس عبارت کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ تشہد صلوۃ علی النبی اور دعاء کے بعد دونوں طرف سلام پھیرے پہلے دائیں طرف پھر بائیں کے مشابہ طرف اور سلام کے الفاظ یہ ہیں السلام علیکم ورحمۃ اللہ یعنی تم پر سلام اور اللہ کی رحمت ہو جمہور علما ، اور کبار صحابہ حضرت عمران بات حضرت علی اور حضرت عبد اللہ بن سعد رضی اللہ عنہم کا یہی مذہب ہے دلیل حضرت ابن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ کی حدیث ہے ان النبی صلی اللہ عليه وسلم كان يسلم عن يميته حتى يرى بياض خده الأيمن وعن يسازه حتى يرى بياض خده الايسر حضرت جز [؟] جو امام مالک نے کہا کہ صرف سامنے کی جانب ایک سلام ہے اور استدلال میں پیش کیا کہ حضرت عائشہ اور سہل بن سعد الساعدی رضی اللہ عنہا نے روایت کی ان النبي صلى الله عيله وسلم فعل كذلک یعنی حضور اقدس صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایسا ہی کیا ہے یعنی نماز سے نکلنے کے لئے ایک اہم کیا۔ ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ کبار صحابہ کے قول ک اختیار کرتا اولی ہے یہ نسبت امام مالک کے قول کے۔ اور رہا حضرت عائشہ اور بھی میل [؟] بن سعد الساعدی کا ایک سلام روایت کرنا تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا عورتوں کی صف میں رہتی تھیں اور سہل بچوں کی صف میں، پس ممکن ہے کہ ان دونوں نے دوسرا اسلام نہ سنا ہو۔ درانحالیکہ مروی ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا دوسر اسلام بہ نسبت اول کے پست اواز سے ہوتا تھا پس اس احتمال کے ہوتے ہوئے حدیث عائشہ اور سہیل قابل استدلال نہیں ہوگی۔
Section on the description of prayer. The summary of this expression is: after tashahhud, salat upon the Prophet and supplication, one turns the salutation to both sides, first to the right then to the left side, and the words of the salutation are: al-salāmu ʿalaykum wa raḥmatu llāh, meaning 'peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah'. This is the school of the majority of scholars and the senior companions such as ʿUmar, ʿAlī, and ʿAbdullāh ibn Saʿd, may Allah be pleased with them. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Masʿūd, may Allah be pleased with him: 'The Prophet, peace be upon him, used to say the salutation to his right until the whiteness of his right cheek was seen, and to his left until the whiteness of his left cheek was seen.' As for what Imām Mālik said that there is only one salutation to the front, and he presented as evidence that ʿĀʾishah and Sahl ibn Saʿd as-Sāʿidī narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, did that, meaning he did only one salutation to exit the prayer. Our response is that adopting the statement of the senior companions is more appropriate compared to the statement of Imām Mālik. As for ʿĀʾishah and Sahl ibn Saʿd as-Sāʿidī's narration of one salutation, the answer is that ʿĀʾishah used to be in the women's row and Sahl was in the children's row, so it is possible that both did not hear the second salutation. Moreover, it is narrated that the second salutation of the Prophet was with a lower voice than the first. Given this possibility, the hadith of ʿĀʾishah and Sahl cannot be used as evidence.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage begins a new section on the description of prayer (Bāb Ṣifat al-Ṣalāh). It establishes the ruling that the taslīm at the end of prayer is performed twice: first to the right, then to the left. The wording is 'al-salāmu ʿalaykum wa raḥmatu llāh'. The author cites the hadith of Ibn Masʿūd as proof that the Prophet used to turn his head so that the whiteness of his cheek became visible. The author then addresses a dispute with Imam Mālik, who held that only one taslīm to the front is sufficient. The Hanafī response is that the practice of the senior companions is preferred, and the narrations of ʿĀʾishah and Sahl might be explained by the fact that they were in rows where they could not clearly observe the second salutation, which was said with a lower voice. Therefore, their narration is not decisive against the clear hadith of Ibn Masʿūd.

Key Terms
تشہد (tashahhud): The recitation of the testimony of faith (al-tahiyyāt) in the sitting position of prayer.
سلام (salām): The salutation at the end of prayer, performed by turning the head right and left.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafī school, how many salutations (taslīm) are performed at the end of prayer?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school mandates two taslīms in prayer, proven by the explicit practice of the Prophet as reported by Ibn Masʿūd.

Intention in Taslīm for Imām, Follower, and Lone Worshipper
Explains whom to intend when saying taslīm in different roles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state whom to intend in the taslīm for each role (imam, follower, munfarid) and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the follower directly behind the imam.

Core Idea
The taslīm greeting is addressed to those present; intention determines its validity, and Hanafis differ on the follower's intention when directly behind the imam.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the required intention (niyyah) when saying the taslīm at the end of prayer. The ruling differs based on whether one is leading, following, or praying alone. The author also presents an intra-madhhab debate between Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad on whether a follower directly behind the imam should intend him in one or both salutations. Understanding these details ensures the taslīm fulfills its purpose as a greeting to the congregation and angels.

Guided Path
1
Identify the roles and their general intention requirements
List the three roles: imam, follower (muqtadī), and lone worshipper (munfarid). For each, note whom they must intend when turning the taslīm to the right and left. The imam intends the congregation and recording angels; the follower intends the imam and angels; the lone worshipper intends only the angels.
The text also mentions an exception for women in later times – they are not intended because their presence in congregation is abandoned.
2
Examine the proof for intention in taslīm
The general principle from the hadith 'innamā al-aʿmālu bi-n-niyyāt' is cited. Also, the taslīm is a greeting (taḥiyya) addressed to those present, so those not present in prayer are not included. Contrast this with the tashahhud greeting which is general.
The proof distinguishes between the taslīm of the prayer and the tashahhud formulation.
3
Analyze the special case of the follower directly behind the imam (muḥādhī)
When the follower is directly facing the imam (i.e., directly behind), there is a disagreement among the Hanafi imams. Abu Yusuf holds that the follower intends the imam only in the right salutation, preferring the right side. Imam Muhammad and a narration from Abu Hanifa hold that the follower intends the imam in both salutations because the imam has a share from both sides.
Muhammad also argues that when combination is possible, preference (tarjīḥ) is not needed.
4
Understand the ruling for the lone worshipper (munfarid)
The munfarid intends only the recording angels, as there is no human congregation. The text states this clearly and notes that the proof is obvious.
The imam does not intend a specific number of angels, as their number is not known; this resembles belief in all prophets without specifying their count.
5
Determine the practical application
The text does not declare one view as mufta bihi, but both opinions are transmitted in the Zahir al-Riwayah. In practice, a follower may follow either opinion, though caution would suggest intending the imam in both salutations.
This is an area where taqlīd to either of the two great Hanafi scholars is acceptable.

The author said: When turning the first salutation, he should intend those who are on his right side, whether men or women, and intend the recording angels. Likewise, when turning the salutation to the left, he should intend those who are on his left side. The proof is that actions are judged by intentions, as mentioned in the hadith. The author of al-Hidayah says: In our time, he should not intend women because the presence of women in congregation has been abandoned by later scholars. Also, he should not intend those Muslims who are not participating in the prayer; this is the correct statement. Al-Hākim al-Shahīd said that he should intend all men and women, whether they are participating in prayer or not, so that the salutation matches the tashahhud salutation (i.e., 'al-salāmu ʿalaynā wa ʿalā ʿibādillāhi aṣ-ṣāliḥīn'). The proof for the correct statement is that the salutation is a greeting addressed to those present, so those not participating are not included. In contrast, the tashahhud salutation is a general greeting to all righteous servants of Allah, whether present or absent, as the Prophet said: 'When the worshipper says "al-salāmu ʿalaynā wa ʿalā ʿibādillāhi aṣ-ṣāliḥīn", it reaches every righteous servant in the heavens and the earth.' The follower must intend the imam in the salutation. If the imam is on the right or left side, he intends him in that salutation. If the imam is directly facing him (muqābil), then according to Abu Yusuf, he intends the imam in the first salutation (to the right), preferring the right side. According to Muhammad, and it is also a narration from Abu Hanifa, he intends him in both salutations because the imam has a share from both sides. Explanation: The issue is that when saying the salutation, the follower must intend his imam. If the imam is on the right, he intends him in that salutation; if on the left, in that one. If the follower is directly behind the imam (muḥādhī), then Abu Yusuf's view is that he intends the imam in the right salutation, while Muhammad's view is that he intends him in both salutations; this is one narration from Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf gave preference to the right side because the right side is preferred in Sharia. Muhammad's proof is that the one directly facing has a share from both sides, so it is better to intend him in both salutations. Also, when conflicting, if combination is possible, one should not resort to preference; therefore, Muhammad said to intend in both. The lone worshipper: He intends only the recording angels because he has no one with him except them. Explanation: The issue and proof are clear. The imam intends both the angels and the followers in both salutations; this is the correct position. He should not intend a specific number of angels because reports about their number differ; it resembles belief in the prophets, peace be upon them.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage details whom the person praying should intend with his salutations. The general rule is that the taslīm is a greeting addressed to the congregation and the recording angels. For the imam, he should intend both the angels and the followers present. The intention should not be for those not present in the prayer, as the salutation is a greeting to the attendees. There is a difference of opinion when the follower is directly behind the imam: Abu Yusuf says intend the imam only in the right salutation (preferring the right), while Imam Muhammad and a narration from Abu Hanifa say intend him in both salutations, because the imam is in front and thus has a share in both directions. The lone worshipper (munfarid) intends only the angels, as he has no human congregation. The imam should not intend a specific number of angels, as their count is not precisely known. This is similar to believing in all prophets without specifying their number.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Intention in the heart; here, whom the worshipper intends to greet with the taslīm.
مقتدی (muqtadī): A follower praying behind an imam in congregation.
منفرد (munfarid): A person praying alone, not in congregation.
محاذی (muḥādhī): One who is directly opposite or facing; here, the follower directly behind the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) In both salutations

Key Takeaway
The intention in taslīm varies by role, and when the follower is directly behind the imam, Hanafis differ on whether to intend him in one or both salutations.

The Ruling of Taslīm: Wājib Not Fard
Establishes taslīm as wājib and refutes Shafiʿī view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taslīm, explain the evidence and reasoning, and evaluate the Shafiʿī counter-argument.

Core Idea
Taslīm is wājib, not fard, because the proof is zanni—and choice contradicts compulsion.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, al-Marghinani establishes the Hanafi position that the closing salutation (taslīm) of prayer is wājib (obligatory) but not fard (compulsory). He contrasts this with Imam al-Shāfiʿī's view that taslīm is fard, and provides the Hanafi response based on the hadith of Ibn Masʿūd. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping the Hanafi epistemology of fard vs. wājib.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the central legal claim: taslīm is wājib, not fard.
The passage opens with 'ثم اصابة لفظة السلام واجبة عندنا وليس بفرض'.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
Recognize that Imam al-Shāfiʿī holds taslīm as fard based on the hadith 'tahrīmuhā al-takbīr wa tahlīluhā al-taslīm'.
The text mentions 'خلاف للشافعي هو يتمسك بقوله عليه السلام تحريمها التكبير وتحليلها التسليم'.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Ibn Masʿūd, which shows choice (takhayyur). Choice is incompatible with fard. Moreover, the evidence is ahad (zanni), which can only establish wujūb, not fard.
The response relies on usul: 'والتخيير ينافى الفريضة والوجوب' and 'بمثله لا يثبت الفرض'.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if taslīm is omitted intentionally, Hanafis consider the prayer valid but sinful; Shafiʿīs consider it invalid.
This difference affects fatwa and daily practice.
5
Note the tarjih
The Hanafī position is muftā bihi in the Hanafī school, as per al-Marghinani.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is mentioned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اصابة لفظة السلام واجبة عندنا وليس بفرض خال للشافعي هو يتمسك بقوله علیه السلام تحريمها التكبير وتحليلها التسليمولنا ماروينا من حديث مسعود والتخيير ينافى الفريضة والوجوب الا انا اثبتنا الوجوب بما رواه احتياطا و بمثله لا يثبت الفرد والله اعلم
Then, the utterance of the word 'salām' is wājib (obligatory) according to us, and it is not fard (compulsory). Contrary to al-Shāfiʿī, who adheres to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Its tahrīm is the takbīr, and its tahlīl is the taslīm.' Our evidence is what we have narrated from the hadith of Ibn Masʿūd. Choice (takhayyur) is incompatible with fardīyyah (compulsory nature) and wujūb (obligation). However, we have established wujūb based on what he (Ibn Masʿūd) narrated, as a precaution. With such evidence, fard is not established. And Allāh knows best.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal classification of the taslīm at the end of prayer. The Hanafī school holds that uttering the word 'salām' is wājib (obligatory) but not fard (compulsory). Imam al-Shāfiʿī differs, considering it fard based on the hadith 'The tahrīm of prayer is the takbīr, and its tahlīl is the taslīm.' The Hanafīs respond by citing the hadith of Ibn Masʿūd, which shows that the Prophet sometimes performed taslīm in a way that allows for choice (e.g., one or two salutations? Actually, the hadith of Ibn Masʿūd shows two salutations, but the point is that the evidence for fard is not conclusive). The presence of choice in the manner of taslīm contradicts the idea of it being fard (which requires a strict, unchangeable command). The Hanafīs establish wujūb from the narration as a precautionary measure, but such evidence (a single hadith with zanni thubut) cannot establish fard (which requires definitive proof).

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): Obligatory but at a level below fard; omission requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw) but does not invalidate the prayer.
فرض (fard): Compulsory; omission invalidates the act.
تحلیل (tahlīl): The act that makes the prayer permissible to end; here, the taslīm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafīs consider taslīm as wājib rather than fard?
A) Because the proof is from the Quran
B) Because the proof is from a mutawatir hadith
C) Because the evidence is zanni (probable) and not qatʿī (definitive)
D) Because there is no proof at all

Key Takeaway
Taslīm is wājib in the Hanafī school because the evidence is of probable transmission and meaning, and the presence of choice in its manner precludes it from being fard.

Intention in Salam: Muqtadi and Munfarid
Intra-Hanafi dispute on muqtadi's intention plus ruling for munfarid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state whom the muqtadi and munfarid must intend in salam and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the muqtadi when directly behind the imam.

Core Idea
In salam, intention follows presence: muqtadi intends the imam, munfarid intends angels; dispute when directly behind.

The intention (niyyah) in the salam at the end of prayer is not merely a ritual utterance; it must be directed to the appropriate recipient. For the muqtadi (follower), the intention is toward the imam; for the munfarid (one praying alone), toward the guardian angels. This lesson examines these rulings and the internal Hanafi disagreement when the muqtadi is directly opposite the imam (muhadhi).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Distinguish between the muqtadi (follower in congregation) and the munfarid (praying alone). Each has a different entity to intend in salam.
Also consider the intermediate case: muqtadi not directly behind.
2
Apply the general rule for muqtadi
If the imam is on the right, intend him in the right salam; if on the left, intend in the left salam. This is the basic, undisputed rule.
This applies unless the follower is directly behind (muhadhi).
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute for muhadhi
When the muqtadi is directly behind the imam, two opinions exist: Abu Yusuf – intend only in the right salam (giving priority to tayammun); Muhammad and a narration of Abu Hanifa – intend in both salams (the imam is entitled to both sides).
The mufta bihi is the latter: intend in both.
4
State the rule for the munfarid
The munfarid intends only the guardian angels (hafazah). The reason is that no one else is present with him.
This is a clear, undisputed ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صفۃ الصلوة
۷۴
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ و الله
امام مقتدی کے مقابل ہوتو ابو یوسف کے نزدیک مقتدی پہلے سلام میں امام کی نیت کرے دائیں جانب کو ترجیح دینے کی وجہ سے اور انہیں کے نزدیک اور یہی روایت ہے ابو حنیفہ سے کہ مقتدی دونوں سلام میں امام کی نیت کرے۔ کیونکہ امام دونوں جانب سے حصہ والا ہے۔ مطہ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ سلام پھیر تے وقت مقتدی کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ اپنے امام کی نیت کرے امام اگر دائیں طرف ہے تو انس طرف سلام میں نیت کرے اور بائیں طرف ہے تو اس طرف کے سلام میں امام کی نیت کرے۔ اور اگر مقتدی ٹھیک امام کے پیچھے اصل محاذی ہو تو اس صورت میں امام ابو یوسف کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ مقتدی دائیں طرف کے سلام میں امام کی نیت کرے اور امام محمد کا ذبر وہ ہے کہ دونوں طرف کے سلام میں امام کی نیت کرے یہی ایک روایت امام ابو حنیفہ سے ہے ایام ابو یوسف نے دائیں جانب کو ترنجی را نیک کیونکہ شریعت میں تیا من ہی معتبر ہے اور امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ محاذی ( مقابل ) دونوں طرف سے حصہ پانے والا ہوتا ہے اس اس دونوں طرف کے سلام میں امام کی نیت کر لی جائے تو بہتر ہے دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ تعارض کے وقت اگر جمع کرنا ممکن ہوتو ترجیح کی رائے رجوع نہیں کیا جاتا اس لئے بھی امام محمد نے کہا کہ دونوں طرف کے سلام میں نیت کرے۔

ترجمہ اور منفر د ملائکہ حفظہ کی نیت کرے فقط کیونکہ منفرد کے ساتھ سوائے حفظہ کے کوئی نہیں ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ اور دلیل واضح ہے۔
Chapter on the Description of Prayer. And Allah. When the imam is opposite the follower, according to Abu Yusuf the follower should intend the imam in the first salam because he gives preference to the right side, and according to him and this is also narrated from Abu Hanifa that the follower intends the imam in both salams because the imam is entitled to both sides. The explanation of the issue is: When turning for salam, it is necessary for the follower to intend his imam. If the imam is on the right, he intends the imam in the salam to that side; if on the left, he intends in the salam to that side. If the follower is directly behind the imam (muhadhi), then according to Imam Abu Yusuf the follower intends the imam in the salam to the right, and according to Imam Muhammad and one narration from Abu Hanifa, he intends the imam in both salams. Abu Yusuf gave preference to the right because in Shariah the right side is considered valid. Imam Muhammad's proof is that the one directly opposite (muhadhi) is entitled to both sides, so it is better to intend the imam in both salams. Second, when there is conflict and reconciliation is possible, one does not resort to preference, so Imam Muhammad said to intend in both. What should the munfarid intend in salam? And the munfarid intends the guardian angels only, because he has no one with him except them. Translation: And the munfarid intends the guardian angels only, because the munfarid has no one with him except the angels. Explanation: The issue and proof are clear.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the niyyah (intention) of the muqtadi (follower) when performing the salam in congregational prayer. The text begins by discussing the situation where the muqtadi is directly opposite (muhadhi) the imam. There are two positions: Abu Yusuf holds that the muqtadi should intend the imam only in the first salam (to the right), giving preference to the right side because the Shariah honors the right (tayammun). Imam Muhammad, and in one narration Abu Hanifa, hold that the muqtadi should intend the imam in both salams because the imam, being directly in front, is entitled to both sides. The text also includes a general ruling: if the imam is on the muqtadi's right, he intends him in the right salam; if on the left, in the left salam. Then the passage addresses the munfarid (one praying alone): he intends only the guardian angels (hafazah) in his salam, as no one else is present. The proof is explicit: 'because he has no one with him except them.' The commentary clarifies that these rulings are well-established.

Key Terms
مقتدی (muqtadi): The person following the imam in congregational prayer.
منفرد (munfarid): One who prays alone, not in congregation.
حفظہ (hafazah): The guardian angels (kiram al-katibin) who record deeds.
سلام (salam): The greeting said at the end of prayer: assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, whom should the munfarid (one praying alone) intend when saying salam?
A) The imam only
B) The guardian angels (hafazah) only
C) Both the imam and the guardian angels
D) The congregation on the right

Key Takeaway
The muqtadi must intend the imam in salam, with ikhtilaf when directly behind; the munfarid intends only the guardian angels.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

The Legal Status of Salam: Fard or Wajib?
Ruling on imam's intention in salam and inter-madhhab dispute on salam being fard or wajib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that salam is wajib not fard, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and the principle of khabar wahid.

Core Idea
Salam is wajib in prayer, not fard: choice in the hadith negates fard, but caution (ihtiyat) from khabar wahid establishes wujub.

This passage addresses a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: the legal status of the final salam in prayer. The Hanafi school views it as wajib (obligatory but not a pillar), while the Shafi'i school considers it fard (essential pillar). The evidence revolves around two hadiths and the nature of khabar wahid. Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi methodology of balancing textual evidence and caution.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: salam is wajib, not fard. Note that this means omission requires sajdah al-sahw but does not invalidate the prayer.
The ruling is based on the principle that khabar wahid establishes wujub but not fard.
2
Identify the Shafi'i proof
Find the hadith cited by Imam al-Shafi'i: 'tahrīmuha al-takbīr wa tahlīluhā al-taslīm'. Understand how they argue that just as takbīr is fard, salam is fard.
This is a dalīl naqlī, but its interpretation differs.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Examine the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud where the Prophet gives choice after tashahhud. Explain how 'choice' negates both fard and wujub.
The hadith is used to negate fard, not to negate all obligation.
4
Explain the Hanafi resolution
The Hanafis harmonize the two hadiths: the choice shows salam is not fard, but out of caution (ihtiyat) they accept the other hadith as establishing wujub. Since that hadith is khabar wahid, it can only establish wujub, not fard.
This demonstrates the Hanafi usul that khabar wahid gives zanni evidence, sufficient for wujub but not for fard.
5
Determine the practical consequence
State the thamarah al-khilaf: if salam is omitted intentionally, the Hanafi school says the prayer is valid but requires sajdah al-sahw; the Shafi'i school says the prayer is invalid.
This difference has real-world implications for worshippers.
