And the Imam intends in both salams; this is correct, and he does not intend a specific number of angels because the reports about their numbers differ, so it resembles faith in the prophets, peace be upon them. Then the uttering of the word 'salam' is wajib according to us, not fard. Imam al-Shafi'i differs, adhering to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Its tahrīm is the takbīr, and its tahlīl is the taslīm.' And our proof is what we narrated from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, and giving choice contradicts fard and wujub. However, we established wujub out of caution due to what he narrated, and through similar evidence fard is not established. And Allah knows best. Translation: And the Imam intends in both salams; this is correct, and he does not intend a specific number of angels because the reports about their numbers differ, so this matter resembles faith in the prophets, peace be upon them. Then according to us, uttering the word 'salam' is wajib, and there is no difference in that except Imam al-Shafi'i, who adheres to the saying of the Prophet: 'Its tahrīm is the takbīr, and its tahlīl is the taslīm.' Our proof is what we narrated from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, and granting choice is contrary to fard and wujub. But we established wujub out of caution due to the hadith he narrated, and from a similar hadith fard is not established. And Allah knows best. Explanation: The Imam intends in both his salams the guardian angels and the congregation. This is the correct saying. Some said that the Imam does not intend. It is not correct, and some said that intending in one salam is sufficient. The author of Al-Hidayah said that he should not intend a specific number of angels, but absolutely intend the angels, because the reports about the number of guardian angels vary. Thus, it is reported from Ibn Abbas (RA) that he said: 'With every believer are five guardian angels: one on his right writes good deeds, one on his left writes evil deeds, one in front prompts him to good, one behind wards off calamities, and one at his forelock writes what he sends blessings upon the Prophet and conveys it to the Messenger of Allah (SAW).' He willed; one narration says 'with every believer are sixty angels', another says 'one hundred and sixty'. Since the number is not fixed, he should intend them without specifying. This matter resembles faith in the prophets, where we must believe in all without specifying numbers. It is wajib to exit prayer with the word salam: It should be clear that according to us uttering the word 'salam' is wajib, not fard. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, saying salam is a rukn and fard. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is the Prophet's saying: 'Its tahrīm is the takbīr, and its tahlīl is the taslīm.' The reasoning is that just as entering prayer is not valid without takbīr, exiting prayer is not valid without salam, and it has passed that takbīr tahrīmah is fard, so saying salam must also be fard. Our proof is that when the Prophet (SAW) taught tashahhud to Ibn Mas'ud (RA), he said: 'When you say this or do this, your prayer is complete. If you wish, you may stand, and if you wish, you may sit.' From this hadith, the argument is that the Prophet declared the prayer complete with salam and gave him choice between standing and sitting. Giving choice contradicts something being fard or wajib. So it is established that after tashahhud, salam etc. are not fard. But if someone objects that giving choice also contradicts wujub, so salam should not be wajib either, yet Hanafis believe it is wajib. The answer: We established wujub out of caution due to the hadith narrated by Imam al-Shafi'i, i.e., the hadith 'tahrīmuha al-takbīr', and this hadith is khabar wahid, and from khabar wahid wujub can be established but not fard. And Allah knows best. Jamil Ahmad 'Afā 'anhu.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a combination of a ruling and an inter-madhhab dispute. It begins by stating the correct ruling for the imam: he should intend in both salams (right and left) for the guardian angels and the congregation. He should not intend a specific number of angels because the reports vary (five, sixty, one hundred sixty). This is analogous to believing in all prophets without specifying numbers. Then the text addresses the legal status of the salam itself. According to the Hanafi school, uttering the words of salam (assalamu alaykum) is wajib (obligatory), not fard (essential). Imam al-Shafi'i holds that it is fard and a rukn. The Shafi'i proof is the hadith: 'The tahrīm (prohibition of worldly actions in prayer) is the takbīr, and the tahlīl (permitting them to leave) is the taslīm.' The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud where the Prophet said that after saying the tashahhud, the prayer is complete, and the worshipper has the choice to stand or sit. Giving choice negates both fard and wujub. However, Hanafis still consider salam wajib out of caution (ihtiyatan) because of the hadith cited by al-Shafi'i. Since that hadith is khabar wahid (single-narrator report), it can establish wujub but not fard. Thus, the Hanafi position is that salam is wajib, not fard.

Key Terms
سلام (salam): The final greeting of prayer, 'assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah'.
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A hadith narrated by one or a few narrators, not reaching the level of tawatur.
حفظہ (hafazah): The guardian angels (kiram al-katibin) who record deeds.
تحریمہ (tahrīmah): The opening takbīr that makes worldly actions prohibited during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal status of saying salam (assalamu alaykum) at the end of prayer?
A) Fard (essential pillar)
B) Wajib (obligatory but not a pillar)
C) Sunnah (recommended)
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
Salam is wajib in Hanafi prayer: its omission requires sajdah al-sahw but does not invalidate the prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Intention for Guardian Angels and the Wajib Status of Salam
Explains intention for guardian angels and the wajib status of salam in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on intending guardian angels without specifying a number and explain why the salam (taslim) in prayer is wajib rather than fard, using the proofs from Ibn Mas'ud and the 'tahrimuha' hadith.

Core Idea
When evidence is indeterminate, intend absolutely; when evidence conflicts, weaker proof (khabar wahid) establishes obligation, not integral necessity.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents two distinct but pedagogically linked rulings. First, the manner of intending the guardian angels during prayer illustrates a broader principle: when transmitted reports are indefinite, one must not specify in intention. Second, the much-debated status of the concluding salutation (taslim) becomes a classic inter-madhhab dispute, demonstrating how the Hanafi school uses usul al-fiqh to reconcile conflicting hadith and classify obligations. This lesson will guide you through both rulings and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage begins with the intention for guardian angels and then transitions to the status of salam. Recognize these as separate but both rooted in textual evidence.
2
Analyze the angel intention ruling
The author instructs not to intend a specific number of guardian angels because narrations vary (5, 60, 160). Instead, intend them absolutely. This is analogous to believing in all prophets without enumerating them.
Principle: when the transmitted data is indeterminate, avoid specification.
3
Examine the salam dispute
The core disagreement: Hanafis say salam is wajib; Shafi'is say it is fard (rukn). Both sides cite hadith.
4
Understand the Hanafi proof and response
The Hanafi proof is the hadith where the Prophet (pbuh) told Ibn Mas'ud that after tashahhud the prayer is complete and gave a choice to stand or sit. This negates fardiyyah. However, Hanafis still hold salam as wajib out of caution, based on the Shafi'i's hadith 'tahrimuha al-takbir', which is khabar wahid and can only establish wujub, not fard.
Key usul: khabar wahid provides zanni evidence, sufficient for wujub but not for fard (which requires qat'i).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: if salam is forgotten, Hanafis say prayer is valid with sajdah sahv; Shafi'is say prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
This highlights the importance of distinguishing rukn from wajib.

یعنی تحريمها التكبير الحدیث اور یہ حدیث خبر واحد ہے اور خبر واحد سے وجوب تو ثابت ہو جاتا ہے مگر فرضیت ثابت نہیں ہوتی ۔ واللہ اعلم جمیل احمد عفی عنہ۔
Chapter on the description of prayer. 'And some said that intention within one Islam is sufficient. The author of Hidayah said: Do not intend a specific number among the angels, rather intend the angels absolutely, because the reports and hadiths about the number of guardian angels vary. So, Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) narrated: He said: With every believer there are five guardian angels: one on his right writes the good deeds, another on his left writes the evil deeds, another in front of him prompts him to good, another behind him wards off troubles from him, and another at his forelock writes what is sent as blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) and conveys it to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). Ibn Abbas said: With every believer there are five guardian angels. In one narration: 'With every believer sixty angels' and in another: 'one hundred and sixty'. So when the number of guardian angels is not fixed, one should intend them without specification. And this matter has become similar to believing in the prophets (peace be upon them) – i.e., it is necessary to believe in all prophets without a fixed number. Exiting prayer with the word of salam is wajib: It is clear that according to us, uttering the word al-salam is wajib, not fard. And according to Imam Shafi'i, saying the word salam is a rukn and fard. Imam Shafi'i's proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Its beginning is takbir and its ending is taslim.' The way of reasoning is that just as entering prayer is not valid without takbir, similarly exiting prayer is not valid without salam. And it has passed previously that takbir tahrimah is fard, so likewise saying salam for leaving prayer would be fard. Our proof is that when the Prophet (peace be upon him) taught tashahhud to Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him), he said to him: 'When you say this or do this, your prayer is complete. Then if you wish to stand, stand, and if you wish to sit, sit.' The inference from this hadith is that the truthful Prophet (peace be upon him) made the completion of prayer conditional upon salam and gave him a choice between sitting and standing. And giving a choice negates something being fard or wajib. So it is proven that after the measure of tashahhud, nothing like salam is fard. But if someone objects that giving a choice also negates obligation, so saying salam should not even be wajib, while Hanafi scholars hold the obligation of salam. The answer: We have proven obligation cautiously due to the hadith that Imam Shafi'i narrated, i.e., 'Takbir is its beginning...' and this hadith is khabar wahid. And from khabar wahid, obligation (wujub) is proven, but fardiyyah is not proven. And Allah knows best. Jamil Ahmad, may he be forgiven.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage covers two related but distinct rulings. First, regarding the intention for the guardian angels (hafazah) during prayer: because narrations differ on their exact number, one should not specify a count in one's intention but should simply intend the angels in general. This is analogous to believing in all prophets without enumerating them. Second, and more centrally, the passage addresses the nature of the salam (salutation) that concludes prayer. It confirms the Hanafi position that saying 'al-salamu alaykum' is wajib (obligatory) but not fard (integral). The Shafi'is argue it is fard based on the hadith 'tahrimuha al-takbir wa tahliluha al-taslim' (its prohibition is the takbir and its release is the taslim). The Hanafis counter with a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) told Ibn Mas'ud that after completing the tashahhud the prayer is complete, and he gave him the choice to stand or sit. This choice indicates that the salam is neither fard nor originally wajib; however, due to the other hadith (which is a khabar wahid), the Hanafis elevate it to the level of wajib (obligatory but not as strong as fard). The distinction between fard and wajib in the Hanafi school is that fard is proven by definitive evidence (qat'i) while wajib is proven by speculative evidence (zanni). Thus, the salam is wajib, and deliberately omitting it necessitates a sajdah sahv or repetition according to some views. The passage also includes a brief discussion on the angels, but the main legal point is the status of salam.

Key Terms
ملائکہ حفظہ (mala'ikah hafazah): Guardian angels assigned to every believer to record deeds and provide protection.
واجب (wajib): A religious obligation proven by speculative evidence (zanni); omission without excuse is sinful but the act remains valid if omitted forgetfully (compensated by sajdah sahv).
فرض (fard): An integral (rukn) of prayer proven by definitive evidence; its omission invalidates the prayer.
تسلیم (taslim): The concluding salutation of prayer, saying 'al-salamu alaykum' to exit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on the salam (taslim) in prayer?
A) It is fard (integral) – omitting it invalidates the prayer.
B) It is wajib (obligatory) – omitting it requires sajdah sahv but does not invalidate.
C) It is sunnah – omitting it is not sinful.
D) It is mustahabb – recommended but not required.

Key Takeaway
Salam is wajib in the Hanafi school; its forgetful omission is compensated by sajdah sahv, but it does not invalidate the prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Loud and Silent Recitation for Imam and Munfarid
Expansion on rulings of jahr and ikhfa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on jahr and ikhfa for the imam and munfarid and identify the proofs from the Sunnah and Quran.

Core Idea
For the imam, jahr in Fajr and first two rak'ahs of Maghrib/Isha is wajib; for the munfarid, it is a choice, but jahr is better.

The rulings on recitation in prayer are detailed in a separate chapter because of their importance. This lesson clarifies when the imam must recite aloud and when silently, and what flexibility the individual praying alone has. The proofs from the consistent practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the Quranic verse on moderation are discussed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling for the imam
Read the passage to find the specific prayers where the imam must recite aloud (jahr) and where he must recite silently (ikhfa). Note that this is wajib.
The imam's obligation is established by the Sunnah and consensus.
2
Identify the ruling for the munfarid
Find the passage that states the munfarid has a choice between jahr and ikhfa, and understand why jahr is considered better.
The munfarid is like an imam for himself.
3
Locate the primary proof from Sunnah
Examine the hadith of Abu Hurairah (may Allah be pleased with him) which states that the Prophet's practice in jahr and ikhfa is the norm.
The hadith is found in Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Understand the Quranic evidence
Read about the revelation of verse 17:110, which instructed the Prophet to avoid both extremes in recitation, leading to the established pattern of jahr at night and ikhfa during the day.
This verse abrogated the earlier practice of jahr in all prayers.

Section on recitation. Translation: This section is on the rulings of recitation. Commentary: When the author (may Allah have mercy on him) finished describing the description of prayer, its quality, its pillars, obligations, and its sunnahs, because the rulings of recitation are many, he mentioned them in a separate section. 'And he recites aloud in Fajr and the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha if he is an imam, and he recites silently in the remaining rak'ahs according to the transmitted practice. And if he is praying alone, he has a choice: if he wishes he may recite aloud and make himself hear, because he is an imam in his own right; and if he wishes he may recite silently because there is no one behind him to hear. And the better is to recite aloud so that his performance resembles the form of the congregation.' Commentary: The author said that if the worshipper is an imam, it is wajib to recite aloud in the two rak'ahs of Fajr and the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha, and in the remaining rak'ahs, i.e., the third of Maghrib and the last two of Isha, it is wajib to recite silently. This is what has been transmitted from the Prophet and the Followers. Then, in the prayers where recitation is loud, jahr is wajib; in silent prayers, ikhfa is wajib. And the obligation is established by the Sunnah. So, Abu Hurairah (may Allah be pleased with him) narrated that he said: 'In every prayer, recitation is performed. So wherever the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) made us hear, we made you hear; and wherever he concealed from us, we concealed from you.' The gist is that in the prayers where the Prophet performed jahr and made us hear, we performed jahr and made you hear; and in the prayers where he performed ikhfa (and we did not hear correctly?), we also performed ikhfa. So it is known that jahr in loud prayers and ikhfa in silent prayers is established by the Sunnah. And ijma' is also evidence, because from the blessed era of the Prophet (peace be upon him) until today, there is consensus on jahr in loud prayers and ikhfa in silent prayers, except for Zuhr and Asr? And rational evidence is that recitation is one of the pillars of prayer, so just as all pillars are required to be manifest, the manifestation of recitation would also be required. This is why in early Islam, the Prophet used to recite aloud in all prayers. And the polytheists would sometimes cause him harm by hearing the Qur'an and talk obscenely. So Allah revealed: 'And do not recite your prayer too loudly nor too silently, but seek between that a way.' So the Prophet did not recite aloud in all prayers nor silently in all prayers, but chose the middle way, i.e., recite aloud in the night prayers and silently in the day prayers. After that, he began to perform Zuhr and Asr silently? because the disbelievers were likely to cause trouble during those times. And since the disbelievers were busy eating at Maghrib time and were in the sleep of heedlessness at Isha and Fajr, he performed jahr at those times. And in Jumu'ah and the two 'Eids, he performed jahr because these prayers were established in Madinah? And he says 'our completed' meaning sound?
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the rulings of qira'ah (recitation) in prayer. It begins by quoting the matn from Hidayah: the imam must recite aloud (jahr) in Fajr prayer and in the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha. In the remaining rak'ahs (third of Maghrib, last two of Isha, and Zuhr/Asr), he must recite silently (ikhfa). A munfarid (individual praying alone) has the choice, but the better option is to recite aloud to emulate the congregation. The commentary then explains that this ruling is wajib (obligatory) for the imam, not just sunnah. The evidence is from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as reported by Abu Hurairah: the Prophet would recite aloud in some prayers and silently in others, and the Companions followed. This practice is also supported by ijma' (consensus) and a rational argument: since recitation is a rukn, it should be made manifest like other acts, but this was later restricted by the Quranic verse commanding moderation (Surah al-Isra 17:110), which led to loud recitation at night (Fajr, Maghrib, Isha) and silent during the day (Zuhr, Asr). The passage explains the reason: early on, the Prophet recited aloud in all prayers, but the polytheists harassed him, so he was instructed to vary his recitation, eventually settling on the known pattern. The ruling applies only to obligatory prayers; for nafl prayers, the munfarid has more flexibility.

Key Terms
جہر (jahr): Loud recitation that makes the voice audible to others nearby.
اخفاء (ikhfa): Silent recitation where one moves the lips and tongue, making it audible only to oneself (not to others).
منفرد (munfarid): A person praying alone, not in congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which prayers is it wajib for the imam to recite aloud (jahr)?
A) All prayers except Zuhr and Asr.
B) Fajr only.
C) Fajr and the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha.
D) Maghrib and Isha only.

Key Takeaway
The imam must recite aloud in Fajr and first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha; the munfarid has a choice but jahr is better.

The Obligation of Loud and Silent Recitation for the Imam
Ruling with proof on imam's recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jahr and ikhfa for the imam in Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha, and explain the proofs from hadith.

Core Idea
The imam's loud recitation is wajib in Fajr and first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha; silent is wajib otherwise.

The passage establishes the foundational ruling for recitation in congregational prayers. It clarifies that the imam's loud or silent recitation is not optional but a required element (wajib) based on the Prophet's practice and explicit command. Understanding this distinction is crucial for anyone leading prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayers for jahr
From the text, identify which prayers and rak'ahs require the imam to recite aloud.
Fajr (both rak'ahs) and first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha.
2
Identify the prayers for ikhfa
Determine where silent recitation is required.
The remaining rak'ahs (third of Maghrib, last two of Isha, and all of Zuhr/Asr).
3
Understand the ruling for munfarid
Analyze the text to see the ruling for a person praying alone.
He has a choice, but the preferred option is to recite aloud.
4

Identify the two hadiths cited and explain how they support the ruling.
The command 'sallu' indicates wujub; the practice of the Prophet specifies the details.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجهر بالقراءة في الفجر والركعتين الأوليين من المغرب والعشاء إن كان إماماً ويخفي في الأخيرين باتفاق. وهو المتوارث من الصحابة والتابعين. وإن كان منفرداً فهو مخير إن شاء جهر وأسمع نفسه لأنه إمام في حق نفسه وإن شاء أخفى لأنه ليس خلفه من يسمعه. والأفضل الجهر ليكون الأداء على هيئة الجماعة. قال عليه السلام: «صلوا كما رأيتموني أصلي». وروى أبو هريرة رضي الله عنه: «في كل صلاة يقرأ، فما أسمعنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أسمعناكم، وما أخفى عنا أخفينا عنكم».
He recites aloud in Fajr and the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha if he is an imam, and he recites silently in the remaining [rak'ahs] by agreement. This is inherited from the Companions and Successors. And if he is praying alone, he has a choice: if he wishes he may recite aloud and make himself hear, because he is an imam with respect to himself, and if he wishes he may recite silently because there is no one behind him to hear him. The better is to recite aloud so that his prayer resembles that of the congregation. He (peace be upon him) said: 'Pray as you have seen me pray.' Abu Huraira reported: 'In every prayer there is recitation. What the Messenger of Allah made us hear, we make you hear; and what he concealed from us, we conceal from you.'

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the recitation of the imam and the individual. The author first states the ruling: the imam must recite aloud in Fajr (both rak'ahs) and in the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha, and silently in the remaining rak'ahs. This is the established practice transmitted from the Companions. Then for the one praying alone (munfarid), he has an option: he may recite aloud (making himself hear) because he is his own imam, or silently. However, the preferred (afdal) is to recite aloud so his prayer resembles the congregational form. The proofs include the general command to pray as the Prophet did, and the specific hadith of Abu Huraira indicating that the Prophet's practice is the standard.

Key Terms
الجهر (al-jahr): Loud recitation that can be heard by others or by oneself if alone.
الإخفاء (al-ikhfa'): Silent recitation such that only the reciter hears himself or less.
منفرد (munfarid): A person praying alone, not as an imam or follower.

Silent Recitation in Zuhr and Asr and the 'Arafah Dispute
States the ruling of silent recitation for imam in Zuhr and Asr, and the dispute with Imam Malik regarding 'Arafah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that silent recitation in Zuhr and Asr is wajib even at 'Arafah, and evaluate the Maliki counterargument.

Core Idea
The daytime prayer is mute — Hadith overrides analogy; silent recitation in Zuhr and Asr is absolute.

This lesson addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: whether the imam must recite silently or aloud in Zuhr and Asr when praying at 'Arafah during Hajj. The Hanafi school adheres to the general rule of silent recitation for daytime prayers, while Imam Malik makes an exception for 'Arafah by analogy to Jumu'ah. We will examine the proofs and understand why the Hanafi position is considered stronger.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the imam must recite silently (ikhfa') in Zuhr and Asr, even at 'Arafah. This is based on the hadith 'Daytime prayer is mute.'
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Imam Malik holds that jahr (audible recitation) is wajib at 'Arafah, drawing an analogy to Jumu'ah due to the large congregation.
3
Follow the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school counters that the hadith is explicit and general; 'Arafah does not create an exception. The analogy is weak because Jumu'ah has its own specific textual basis.
4
Determine the practical consequence
In practice, a Hanafi imam recites silently at 'Arafah; a Maliki imam recites aloud. This difference affects the validity according to each school's conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويخفيها الإمام في الظهر والعصر وإن كان بعرفة لقوله عليه السلام «صلاة النهار عجماء» أي ليست قراءة مسموعة. وفي عرفة خلاف لمالك والحجة عليه ما رويناه: صلاة النهار عجماء. وأما حديث ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما قال: «الإقراءة في هاتين الصلاتين» فغير صحيح. ودليل قراءته صلى الله عليه وسلم في الظهر والعصر ما روي عن خباب بن الأرت قال: «عرفنا قراءة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في الظهر والعصر باضطراب لحيته». وعن أبي قتادة: «كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يسمعنا الآية والآيتين في الظهر أحيانا». وعن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه: «في كل صلاة يقرأ فما أسمعنا أسمعناكم وما أخفى عنا أخفينا عنكم».
And the imam recites silently in Zuhr and Asr even if he is at 'Arafah, because of his (peace be upon him) statement: 'The daytime prayer is mute', meaning there is no audible recitation. Regarding 'Arafah there is a difference from Malik, and the proof against him is what we have narrated: 'The daytime prayer is mute.' As for the hadith of Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: 'There is no recitation in these two prayers', it is not authentic. And evidence for his (peace be upon him) recitation in Zuhr and Asr is what is narrated from Khabbab ibn al-Aratt: 'We recognized the recitation of the Messenger of Allah in Zuhr and Asr by the movement of his beard.' And from Abu Qatada: 'The Messenger of Allah would sometimes make us hear a verse or two in Zuhr.' And from Abu Huraira: 'In every prayer there is recitation; what he made us hear we make you hear, and what he concealed from us we conceal from you.'
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute regarding silent recitation in Zuhr and Asr. The Hanafi position is that the imam must recite silently in Zuhr and Asr, even if he is at 'Arafah during Hajj. The proof is the hadith 'Daytime prayer is mute' (mute meaning no audible recitation) and the general principle from Abu Huraira's hadith. Imam Malik held that at 'Arafah, the imam should recite aloud in Zuhr and Asr because of the large gathering, analogous to Jumu'ah. However, the Hanafi response is that the hadith of 'daytime prayer is mute' is general and includes 'Arafah. They also cite the practice of the Prophet as witnessed by Khabbab and Abu Qatada: he recited silently (only audible sometimes for a verse or two). Hence, silent recitation is the absolute rule for Zuhr and Asr. The hadith of Ibn Abbas denying recitation altogether is not authentic.

Key Terms
عجماء (‘ajma’): Mute; used to describe daytime prayers meaning no audible recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He recites aloud because of the large congregation
B) He recites silently as usual
C) He recites aloud only in the first two rak'ahs
D) He recites silently only if he is not at 'Arafah

Key Takeaway
Silent recitation in Zuhr and Asr is wajib based on the hadith 'daytime prayer is mute'; the Prophet's practice confirms it, and 'Arafah does not change the ruling.

Ikhfa in Dhuhr and Asr: The Hanafi–Maliki Dispute on 'Arafah
Ruling on silent recitation with inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ikhfa in Dhuhr and Asr at 'Arafah and evaluate the Maliki counter-proof.

Core Idea
The daytime prayer is dumb – no exception at 'Arafah.

This passage addresses a specific point of dispute: whether the imam should recite silently in Dhuhr and Asr when at 'Arafah during Hajj. The Hanafi school holds the ruling is unconditional; Imam Malik differs. We will examine the proof and the response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: ikhfa (silent recitation) is wajib in Dhuhr and Asr, even at 'Arafah.
The ruling is unconditional.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik holds that at 'Arafah the imam should recite audibly (jahr) due to the large gathering.
Maliki position is an exception to the general rule.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Malik argues by qiyas: large gathering at 'Arafah is analogous to Jumu'ah, where jahr is required.
Analogy based on the commonality of large congregation.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal is that the Prophet's hadith 'Salat al-nahar jam'a' is explicit and general; it cannot be overridden by qiyas. Additionally, the Prophet himself prayed at 'Arafah with ikhfa.
The text states 'al-hujjah 'alayhi ma rawaynahu'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafi imam recites silently at 'Arafah; Maliki imam recites audibly. Followers must be aware of the difference.
The prayer is valid in both schools, but the ruling differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويخفيها الامام في الظهر والعصر وان كان بعرفة لقوله عليه السلام صلوة النهار عجماء اى ليست فيها قراءة مسموعة وفى عرفة خلاف لمالك والحجة عليه مارويناه صلاة النهار عجماء
The imam conceals (his recitation) in Dhuhr and Asr, even if he is at 'Arafah, because of his saying peace be upon him: 'The prayer of the day is dumb' i.e. there is no audible recitation in it. Commentary
This passage states a ruling: the imam must perform silent recitation (ikhfa) in Dhuhr and Asr prayers unconditionally, even if the prayer is performed at 'Arafah during Hajj. The primary dalil is the Prophet's statement 'Salat al-nahar jam'a' (the daytime prayer is mute/buzzing), meaning no audible recitation is part of it. Imam Malik held that at 'Arafah, because of the large gathering, it should be audible, analogous to Jumu'ah. However, the Hanafi response is that the hadith is general and overrides any analogy. The Hanafi position is that ikhfa is wajib in Dhuhr and Asr for the imam and the individual.

Key Terms
إخفاء (ikhfā'): Concealing the recitation such that it is not audible to others; silent recitation.
جهر (jahr): Audible recitation, allowing others to hear.
عرفات ('Arafāt): The plain near Makkah where part of Hajj is performed; the text discusses Dhuhr and Asr combined at 'Arafah (the standing).

Core Idea
Jahr in Jumu'ah and 'Eid is wajib due to widely transmitted practice, not mere sunnah.

In this lesson, we examine the obligation of audible recitation (jahr) for the imam in Friday and 'Eid prayers. The Hanafi school holds that jahr is wajib, not merely sunnah, based on the widely transmitted (mustafid) reports of the Prophet's ﷺ practice. This distinction has practical implications for the validity of the prayer.

Guided Path

The act is jahr (audible recitation) for the imam in Jumu'ah and 'Eid. The ruling is wajib.
2

3
Understand why it is wajib not fard
Because the evidence is from sunnah, not Quran, and mustafid gives certainty of practice but not of thubut like mutawatir.
In Hanafi usul, mustafid is binding in practice.
4

All schools agree on the ruling, though some may consider it sunnah rather than wajib.

Jahr and Ikhfa in Nafl Prayers by Day and Night
Ruling on recitation in voluntary prayers during day and night

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation in nafl prayers during day and night and explain the qiyas that derives it from the fard prayers of the munfarid.

Core Idea
Daytime nafl requires ikhfa; night nafl gives a choice—nafl completes fard and follows its rule.

This passage extends the established ruling for fard prayers to voluntary (nafl) prayers. The key insight is that nafl is a completion (mukammil) of fard, so it follows the same pattern of jahr and ikhfa as the corresponding fard for a person praying alone. You will see how the Hanafi school uses qiyas jali (clear analogy) to derive this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for fard (the asl)
Recall that for a munfarid (individual) performing fard prayer, the rule is: day fard (Zuhr, Asr) require ikhfa; night fard (Maghrib, Isha) allow either jahr or ikhfa. This is established via dalil from sunnah.
This asl is the anchor of the qiyas.
2
Recognize the connection between nafl and fard (the illa)
The passage states that nafl is a 'mukammil' (completion) of fard. This means voluntary prayers compensate for any shortcomings in the obligatory ones, making them subordinate.
The illa is 'being a completion'—a clear attribute.
3
Apply qiyas to derive the nafl ruling
Since the illa is present in both fard and nafl, the ruling on jahr/ikhfa transfers to nafl: day nafl requires ikhfa; night nafl gives a choice.
This is qiyas jaliy because the illa is explicit and the cases share the same cause.
4
Confirm the practical outcome
Thus, a person performing nafl prayer alone at noon must recite silently, while at night he may choose. If he recites audibly by day in a nafl, it is considered makruh or contrary to the preferred practice.
Some later scholars held variant views, but the relied-upon position is as above.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التطوع بالنهار يخافت وفى الليل بيا. اعتبارا بالفرض في حق المنفرد وهذا لانه مكمل له فيكون تبعات
And in voluntary (prayer) during the day he conceals, and at night he has the choice, considering the obligatory (prayer) in the case of the individual, and this is because it (voluntary) completes it (obligatory), so it follows it.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage extends the ruling of jahr/ikhfa from obligatory prayers to voluntary (nafl) prayers by analogy (qiyas). Since nafl prayers complete and perfect the obligatory prayers, they are subordinate to them. Therefore, for a person praying nafl alone during the day, ikhfa is required (like Dhuhr and Asr for a munfarid). At night, the person has a choice between jahr and ikhfa (like Maghrib and Isha for a munfarid). The underlying principle is that nafl follows the ruling of its corresponding obligatory prayer regarding jahr and ikhfa.

Key Terms
تطوع (taṭawwu'): Voluntary/nafl prayer, as opposed to fard.
مكمل (mukammil): That which completes or perfects something else; nafl completes the deficiencies of fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Jahr is required
B) Ikhfa is required
C) He has a choice
D) It is invalid without recitation

Key Takeaway
Daytime nafl prayers require ikhfa (silent recitation) because they complete the fard prayers, which also require ikhfa during the day; nighttime nafl allows a choice.

Jahr in Jumu'ah and 'Eid Prayers
States ruling on jahr in Jumu'ah/Eid with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that jahr is wajib for the imam in Jumu'ah and 'Eid prayers and identify the hadith evidence that supports this ruling.

Core Idea
The imam must recite aloud in Jumu'ah and 'Eid; the Prophet's continuous practice proves obligation.

This lesson examines the ruling that the imam recites aloud (jahr) in Jumu'ah and the two 'Eid prayers. The Hidayah states this as wajib, supported by widely transmitted hadith reports. We will explore the evidence and understand why this is the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the imam's recitation in the congregational prayers of Jumu'ah and 'Eid. The ruling is that he must recite aloud (jahr), and this is considered wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school.
This is not fard but wajib because the proof is from ahad hadith.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites 'mutawatir transmission' and specific hadith: the Prophet used to recite 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la' and 'Hal ataka hadith al-ghashiyah' in Jumu'ah and 'Eid. Also the hadith from Abu Waqid al-Laythi.
The term 'nagl mustafidh' indicates widespread transmission, giving zanni thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's continuous practice (mudawamah) on these occasions indicates obligation. In Hanafi usul, a consistent action of the Prophet implies wujub unless there is evidence for mere recommendation.
The proof is from fi'l (action) and taqrir (approval).
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school considers jahr in these prayers as sunnah, not wajib. However, the Hanafi position is mufta bihi due to the strength of the evidence.
The practical difference: if imam omits jahr intentionally, sajdah al-sahw is wajib in Hanafi.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایت فی
امام جمعہ اور عیدین میں جہر اقرآت کرے، دن اور رات کے نوافل میں جہر کا حکم
ويجهر في الجمعة والعيدين لورود النقل المستفيض بالجهر وفى التطوع بالنهار يخافت وفى الليل يخير اعتبارا بالفرض في حق المنفرد وهذا لانه مكمل له فيكون تبعات
ترجمہ اور امام جمعہ اور عیدین میں جہر کرے گا۔ کیونکہ جہر کے ساتھ نقل مشہور وارد ہے اور دن کی نفل میں اخفاء کرے اور رات میں اختیار ہے منفرد کے حق میں فرض پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے۔ اور یہ اس لئے کہ نفل فرض کو مکمل کرنے والا ہے تو نفل فرض کے تابع ہوا اور اس کی تشریح مسئلہ جمعہ اور عیدین کی نماز میں بھی امام پر جہر واجب ہے۔ دلیل احادیث مشہورہ ہیں چنانچہ بخاری کے علاوہ محمد ہیں۔
جماعت نے روایت کیا ہے انه صلی الله علیه وسلم كان يقرأ فى العيدين ويوم الجمعة سبح اسم ربك الاعلى
اتاک حدیث الغاشیۃ اور مسلم کی روایت ہے عن ابى واقد الليثى سألني عمر ما كان يقرأ به رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في الأضحى والفطر فقال كان يقرأ بـ (ق) والقرآن المجيد واقتربت الساعة یعنی ابو واقد سے مروی ہے کہ عمر نے سوال کیا کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم عید الاضحی اور عید الفطر کی نماز میں کیا پڑھتے تھے فرمایا سورہ ق اور سورہ اقتربت الساعت روایات سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ آپ جمعہ اور عیدین میں جہر فرماتے تھے۔ دلیل صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ دن کے نفل میں اخفاء واجب ہے اور رات کے نفل میں اختیار ہے جہر کرے یا اخفاء کرے اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ نفل پڑھنے والے کو قیاس کیا گیا ہے مفترض منفرد پر یعنی تنہا فرض نماز ادا کرنے والے پر یعنی جیسے فرض میں منفرد کا حکم ہے کہ دن فرائض میں وجوباً اخفاء کرے گا اور رات کی نمازوں میں اس کو اختیار ہے جی چاہے جہر کرے اور جی چاہے اخفاء کرے اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ نفل فرض کی تکمیل کرنے والا ہوتا ہے لہذا نفل فرض کے تابع ہوگا۔ اور رات کے فرضوں میں منفرد کو اختیار ہے کہ جہر کرے یا اخفاء کرے اسی طرح رات کے نفلوں میں بھی اختیار ہے۔ اور چونکہ دن کے فرضوں میں اخفاء متعین ہے لہذا دن کے نفلوں میں بھی متعین ہوگا۔
Chapter on Description of Prayer. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary on Hidaya. The imam recites aloud in Jumu'ah and the two 'Eids due to the mutawatir transmission of jahr. And in supererogatory prayers during the day he recites silently, and at night he has a choice, analogizing to the obligatory prayer for the one praying alone, because the supererogatory completes the obligatory and thus follows it. Translation: And the imam will recite aloud in Jumu'ah and the two 'Eids because a well-known transmission about jahr has come. And in day nafl he recites silently, and at night there is choice, by analogy on the fard for the individual. And this is because nafl completes fard, so nafl follows fard. Explanation: The issue: In Jumu'ah and 'Eid prayers, jahr is wajib upon the imam. The evidence is famous hadith. For example, besides Bukhari, a group has narrated that he (peace be upon him) used to recite in the two 'Eids and on Friday 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la' and 'Hal ataka hadith al-ghashiyah'. And Muslim has narrated from Abu Waqid al-Laythi that 'Umar asked him what the Prophet recited in al-Adha and al-Fitr, and he said he used to recite 'Qaf wal-qur'an al-majid' and 'Iqtarabat al-sa'ah'. These narrations show that he used to recite aloud in Jumu'ah and the two 'Eids. The author of Hidayah said that in day nafl ikhfa is wajib, and in night nafl there is choice: he may recite aloud or silently. The evidence is that the person praying nafl is analogized to the individual performing fard alone, i.e., just as in fard the individual's ruling is that he recites silently in day prayers as an obligation, and in night prayers he has the choice to recite aloud or silently, and the reason is that nafl completes fard, so nafl follows fard. And in night fard the individual has the choice to recite aloud or silently; similarly in night nafl there is choice. And since in day fard ikhfa is determined, therefore in day nafl it is also determined.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the recitation (qira'ah) in different prayers. It opens by stating that the imam must recite aloud (jahr) in Jumu'ah and the two 'Eid prayers. The proof given is 'mutawatir transmission' – meaning a large number of hadith that are widely transmitted, particularly the hadith that the Prophet used to recite Surah al-A'la and Surah al-Ghashiyah in these prayers. The author then addresses supererogatory prayers (nawafil). During the day, the person must recite silently (ikhfa); at night, he has the choice (takhayyur) to recite aloud or silently. The reasoning (ta'lil) is qiyas on the individual (munfarid) praying fard. For fard, a solitary person must recite silently in day prayers but has the choice at night. Since nafl is a completion (mukammil) of fard, it follows the same pattern. The commentary expands on the hadith sources and explains that the qiyas is sound because nafl is subordinate to fard. This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
جہر (jahr): Loud audible recitation in prayer (qira'ah jahriyyah)
نقل مستفیض (naql mustafidh): A widely transmitted report that is below mutawatir but above ahad

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling for the imam's recitation in Jumu'ah prayer?
A) He may choose between jahr and ikhfa.
B) He must recite aloud (jahr), and it is wajib.
C) He must recite silently (ikhfa), and it is sunnah.
D) He must recite subvocally.

Key Takeaway
The imam must recite aloud in Jumu'ah and 'Eid prayers; this is wajib due to the Prophet's consistent practice, and omission requires sajdah al-sahw.

Salah — Prayer

Recitation in Nawafil: Day vs Night
States rulings on recitation in nawafil (day vs night) with qiyas reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qiyas to determine that day nafl requires ikhfa (silent) and night nafl allows choice, and derive the ruling via qiyas on fard munfarid.

Core Idea
Nafl follows fard: silent recitation in day nafl is wajib, night nafl offers choice.

This lesson delves into the rulings for recitation in supererogatory prayers (nawafil). The Hidayah states that during the day, one must recite silently (ikhfa), while at night there is a choice between loud and silent. The reasoning is based on analogy (qiyas) to the solitary fard prayer, as nafl is considered a completion of fard.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling for day and night nafl
The Hidayah states: in day nafl, the worshipper must recite silently (ikhfa); in night nafl, he has the choice to recite aloud or silently. This applies to the individual praying alone (munfarid).
The ruling is for the person praying nafl alone; if in congregation, the imam's rulings apply.
2
Identify the asl (original case) in the qiyas
The asl is the fard prayer performed alone (munfarid) during the day or night. For fard, the ruling is: day fard requires ikhfa (silent), night fard allows choice between jahr and ikhfa. This is established by the Sunnah.
The asl's hukm is known from the Prophet's practice.
3
Identify the far' (new case) and the illa (effective cause)
The far' is the nafl prayer during the day or night. The illa is that nafl is a completion (mukammil) of fard, so it follows the rulings of fard in matters that are not specifically legislated differently.
The illa is extracted by tahqiq al-manat: the completion relationship is the common attribute.
4
Derive the hukm for the far'
Since the asl (fard munfarid) requires ikhfa in day and choice at night, and the illa (completion) applies, the far' (nafl) takes the same ruling: day nafl ikhfa wajib, night nafl choice.
This is a clear qiyas jaliy (evident analogy) with no objections.

باب صفۃ الصلوة
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایت فی

Qada of Jahri Prayer After Sunrise: Ruling on Jahr or Ikhfa When Alone
Intra-Hanafi dispute on jahr/ikhfa in qada after sunrise for a munfarid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation in qada of jahri prayers after sunrise and evaluate the intra-madhhab dispute between the preferred view and that of Sarakhsi and Fakhr al-Islam.

Core Idea
When making up a jahri prayer alone after sunrise, ikhfa is wajib — jahr is only for congregation or within time.

In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario: a missed jahri prayer (Fajr, Maghrib, or Isha) made up after sunrise. Is there a choice between jahr and ikhfa? The author of Al-Hidayah addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute, presenting the correct view that ikhfa is obligatory for the individual. We will analyze the evidence and reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
The passage addresses two scenarios: leading in jama'ah (jahr wajib) and praying alone (ikhfa wajib). Focus on the alone scenario.
Memorize the two conditions for jahr: congregation (wajib) or within time (optional).
2
Analyze the evidence (dalil)
The Prophet's action at Lailat al-Ta'ris shows jahr in congregation; the lack of evidence for jahr when alone implies ikhfa is the default.
Hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in practice.
3
Understand the ta'lil (effective cause)
Jahr is restricted to two situations: with jama'ah (wajib) or within time (optional). After sunrise, neither condition applies, so ikhfa becomes wajib.
This is a qiyas-based argument: the absence of both conditions necessitates ikhfa.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imams Sarakhsi and Fakhr al-Islam argued that jahr is afdal because qada follows ada, where choice exists for the munfarid. The author refutes this by emphasizing the specific conditions of jahr.
The dispute is about the applicability of the general principle (qada mirrors ada) vs. specific conditions.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah prefers the view that ikhfa is wajib, and this is the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah).
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جہری نماز کی قضا میں بھی جہراً قرآت ہوگی
نہیں یا
ومن فاتته العشاء فصلاها بعد طلوع الشمس ان ام فيها جهر كما فعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حين قضى الفجر من ليلة التعريس بجماعة وان كان وحده خافت حتما ولا يتخير هو الصحيح لان الجهر يختص إما بالجماعة على حتما أو بالوقت في حق المنفرد على وجه التخيير ولم يوجد احدهما
ترجمہ اور جس مرد کی عشاء فوت ہو گئی۔ پھر طلوع آفتاب کے بعد اس کو قضاء کیا تو اگر فضا میں امامت کی تو جبر کرے جیسے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے کیا تھا جب کہ لیلۃ التعریس کی صبح کو فجر کی نماز کو جماعت کے ساتھ قضا فرمایا تھا اور اگر تنہا ہو تو وجوباً اخفاء کرے اور اس کو اختیار نہیں۔ یہی صحیح ہے کیونکہ جہر کرنا مختص ہے یا تو با جماعت ہو (کہ اس وقت جہر) واجب ہے یا وقت کے اندر ہو تو منفرد کے حق میں بطور اختیار ہے اور یہاں دونوں میں سے کوئی نہیں پایا گیا۔
تشریح مسئلہ اگر کسی شخص کی عشاء یا مغرب اور فجر کی نماز فوت ہو گئی پھر اس کو آفتاب طلوع ہونے کے بعد قضا کیا تو اس کی دوصورتیں ہیں، تو با جماعت قضاء کرے گا یا تنہا اگر جماعت کے ساتھ قضاء کی ہے تو جہر کرے اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ لیلۃ التعریس کے موقع پر جب آپ نے فجر کی نماز کو با جماعت قضاء کیا تو آپ نے جہر فرمایا تھا۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے قضاء نماز میں قرآت بالجبر فرمائی مختصر واقعہ یہ ہے کہ سفر جہاد سے واپسی میں صحابہ کی درخواست پر آپ مع اُسکر اترے اور حضرت بلال نے جاگنے کی ذمہ داری لی مگر سو گئے اور اس وقت جاگے کہ ان پر دھوپ آئی پس حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے وہاں سے کوچ کا حکم دیا اور آگے بڑھ کر جب آفتاب ایک نیزہ بلند ہوا تو اتر کر وضو کیا اور مؤذن کو اذان کا حکم دیا پھر دو رکعتیں پڑھیں یعنی سنت فجر، پھر نماز کی اقامت کہی گئی پھر نماز فجر پڑھی جیسے روز پڑھا کرتے تھے اور ظاہر ہے کہ آپ فجر کی نماز میں بالجبر قرآت کرتے تھے پس ثابت ہوا کہ آپ نے لیلۃ التعریس کے موقعہ پر فجر کی نماز کو قرآت بالجبر کے ساتھ قضاء کیا۔
تنہا جہری نماز کی قضا کرتے وقت اخفاء واجب ہے اور اگر مذکورہ قضا نماز تنہا پڑھنے تو اخفاء واجب ہے اور اس کو جہر اور اخفاء کے درمیان اختیار نہیں ہے۔ یہی قول صحیح ہے بعض الائمہ السرخسی اور فخر الاسلام وغیرہ نے کہا کہ جہر افضل ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ قضاء ادا کے موافق ہوتی ہے اور رات کی نمازوں میں ادا منفرد کے حق میں اختیار ہے کہ جہر کرے یا اخفاء کرے اور جہر افضل ہے پس ایسے ہی قضا میں ہوگا۔ قول صحیح کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جہر کرنا دو صورتوں میں مختص ہے ایک یہ کہ نماز با جماعت ہو دوم یہ کہ نماز وقت کے اندر ہو پہلی صورت میں جہر واجب ہے اور دوسری صورت میں منفرد کے حق میں بطور اختیار کے ہے۔ حاصل یہ ہے کہ جہر اور اخفاء شرعی توقیف پر موقوف ہے اور ہم نے شریعت میں جہر دو طریقوں سے پایا ایک تو جہر واجب یہ اس وقت ہے کہ جماعت سے جہری نماز پڑھے خواہ ادا ہو یا قضاء ہو اور دوم جہر اختیاری یہ اس وقت ہے جب کہ منفرد وقت کے اندر جہری نماز پڑھے۔ اور یہاں جب کہ منفرد طلوع آفتاب کے بعد جہری نماز پڑھتا ہے تو دونوں باتوں میں سے کوئی بات نہیں پائی گئی یعنی نہ جماعت ہے اور نہ وقت اس لئے اس صورت میں نہ جہر واجب ہوگا اور نہ جہر مخیر بلکہ اخفاء واجب ہوگا۔ جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
And in qada of jahri prayers, jahr is also done? Or not? And whoever misses Isha and prays it after sunrise, if he leads in jama'ah, he recites aloud as the Prophet did when he made up Fajr on the night of al-Ta'ris in congregation. And if he is alone, he must recite silently and has no choice. This is the correct view because jahr is specific either to congregation (where it is obligatory) or to time for the individual by way of choice, and neither is found here. Translation and explanation of the issue: If a person misses Isha, Maghrib, or Fajr, then makes it up after sunrise, there are two scenarios: with congregation or alone. If with congregation, he recites aloud, as the Prophet did on the night of al-Ta'ris when he made up Fajr in congregation. The story: On return from jihad, at the request of the Companions, the Prophet camped with his army. Bilal took responsibility to wake them but slept. They woke up when the sun had risen. The Prophet ordered departure, moved forward, and when the sun was a spear's height, he dismounted, performed wudu, ordered the adhan, prayed two rak'ats (sunnah of Fajr), then the iqamah was said, and he prayed Fajr as usual. It is known that he recited aloud in Fajr, so he made up Fajr with jahr. When making up a jahri prayer alone, ikhfa is wajib and there is no choice. This is the correct view. Some imams like Sarakhsi and Fakhr al-Islam said jahr is afdal, arguing that qada corresponds to ada, and in night ada the individual has choice, and jahr is better, so similarly in qada. The correct view's evidence: jahr is specific to two scenarios: (1) prayer with jama'ah (where it is obligatory), and (2) prayer within its time for the individual (by way of choice). Here, when an individual prays a jahri prayer after sunrise, neither congregation nor within time is present, so jahr is neither obligatory nor optional; rather ikhfa is wajib.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario: making up a missed jahri prayer (Maghrib, Isha, or Fajr) after sunrise. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the ruling of recitation. The text first presents the correct (sahih) view: if you lead the qada in congregation, you must recite aloud (jahr), based on the Prophet's action at the incident of Lailat al-Ta'ris (the night spent on the way). If you pray alone, you must recite silently (ikhfa) and have no choice. The reason (ta'lil) is that jahr in shari'ah is found in only two situations: (1) when praying in congregation – then jahr is wajib; (2) when praying within the prayer's prescribed time as a munfarid – then jahr is optional (better but not mandatory). After sunrise, neither condition is met: there is no congregation (if alone) and it is not within the original time. Hence, jahr is not valid; wajib is ikhfa. The passage then discusses an alternative view attributed to some Hanafi scholars (Sarakhsi, Fakhr al-Islam) that jahr is afdal (better) because qada follows the ruling of ada (original performance). In ada, a munfarid at night has the choice and jahr is better, so it should be the same in qada. The author rebuts this by emphasizing the specific conditions of jahr. The correct view (mufta bihi) is the one stated first: wajib of ikhfa when alone.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory prayer outside its prescribed time
لیلۃ التعریس (lailat al-ta'ris): The night when the Prophet and Companions camped and overslept Fajr, making it up after sunrise

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in Hanafi fiqh, what is the ruling for a person making up Isha alone after sunrise?
A) He must recite aloud (jahr) because it is a jahri prayer
B) He may choose between jahr and ikhfa
C) He must recite silently (ikhfa)
D) He must recite subvocally but can also recite aloud

Key Takeaway
When making up a jahri prayer alone after sunrise, ikhfa is wajib because the conditions for jahr (jama'ah or within time) are absent.

Compensating Missing Recitation in 'Isha: Abu Hanifa & Muhammad vs. Abu Yusuf
Ruling on compensating omission of Fatiha or surah in first two rak'ats of 'Isha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two scenarios of missing recitation in 'Isha and state the Hanafi mufta bihi position regarding compensation.

Core Idea
Fatiha cannot be compensated later if omitted; surah can be, because order of recitation is sacred.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about what happens when a worshipper omits either the Fatiha or a surah in the first two rak'ats of 'Isha. The disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad on one side and Imam Abu Yusuf on the other turns on the possibility of preserving the prescribed order of recitation. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the mufta bihi ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Recognize that the passage discusses two distinct omissions: (a) surah recited without Fatiha, and (b) Fatiha recited without surah.
These are mutually exclusive cases.
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
For case (a), they rule no compensation. For case (b), they require the worshipper to recite both Fatiha and a surah in the last two rak'ats aloud.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
State Abu Yusuf's objection
Abu Yusuf holds that neither omission should be compensated, because an obligatory act missed in its proper time cannot be made up later.
His reasoning is based on the general principle of qada' (making up missed obligations).
4
Understand the rational distinction (tartib)
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that Fatiha is legislated to be followed immediately by a surah. If Fatiha were compensated later, it would come after the surah, violating the prescribed order. Surah, however, can be added after Fatiha in proper sequence.
The order (tartib) is the key illa (effective cause).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as supported by the author of the sharh.
This is the ruling to apply in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عشاء کی پہلی دورکعت میں سورت ملائی فاتحہ نہیں پڑھی یا فاتحہ پڑھی اور سورت ساتھ نہیں ملائی تو اس کے لئے کیا حکم ہے
ومن قرأ في العشاء فى الاوليين السورة ولم يقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب لم يعد فى الاخريين وان قرأ الفاتحة ولم يزد عليها قرأ في الاخريين الفاتحة والسورة وجهر و هذا عند ابي حنيفة و محمد و قال ابو يوسف لا يقضى واحدة منهما لان الواجب اذا فات عن وقته لا يقضى الابدليل ولهما وهو الفرق بين الوجهين ان قراءة الفاتحة شرعت على وجه يترتب عليها السورة فلو قضاها فى الاخريين يترتب الفاتحة على السورة وهذا خلاف الموضوع بخلاف ما اذا ترك السورة لانه امكن قضاؤها على الوجه المشروع ثم ذكر ههنا مايدل على الوجوب وفي الاصل بلفظة الاستحباب لانها ان كانت مؤخرة فغير موصولة بالفاتحة فلم يمكن مراعاة موضوعها من كل وجه
What is the ruling for one who recited the surah in the first two rak'ats of 'Isha but did not recite Fatiha? Or one who recited Fatiha but did not add a surah? And whoever recites in 'Isha in the first two rak'ats the surah and does not recite the Fatiha, he does not repeat it in the last two rak'ats. And if he recites the Fatiha and does not add anything to it, he recites the Fatiha and surah in the last two rak'ats and recites aloud. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: he does not make up either of them, because when an obligatory act is missed in its time, it is not made up later as a substitute. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is the distinction between the two cases: the recitation of Fatiha is legislated in such a way that the surah follows it. If he makes it up in the later rak'ats, the Fatiha would follow the surah, contrary to the prescribed order. This is unlike the case where he omitted the surah, because it is possible to make it up in the prescribed manner. Then the author mentions here something that indicates wujub, whereas in the original text it is phrased as istihbab (recommendation), because if it (the Fatiha) is delayed, it is not connected to the surah, so it is not possible to observe its prescribed order completely.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding compensating missing recitation in 'Isha prayer. The scenario: a person in the first two rak'ats of 'Isha either (a) recited a surah without Fatiha, or (b) recited Fatiha without a surah. According to Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, in case (a) the missing Fatiha is not repeated in the last two rak'ats, because reciting Fatiha after the surah would violate the proper order (Fatiha should precede surah). In case (b), both Fatiha and a surah are recited again in the last two rak'ats with jahr (aloud), because the surah can be properly added after Fatiha. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees and says neither omission should be made up, because once the obligatory act (like Fatiha in the first two) is missed in its proper time (the first two rak'ats), it cannot be compensated later; the missed recitation is not like the case where no recitation was done. The text explains that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad distinguish the two cases based on the shar'i order: Fatiha is meant to be followed immediately by surah, so delaying Fatiha to a later rak'ah would invert the order (surah then Fatiha), which is invalid. However, if only the surah is missed, it can be made up in the later rak'ats by reciting Fatiha and surah in correct order. The text also notes that in the original (al-Asl) the wording indicates recommendation (istihbab) rather than obligation (wujub), but here the author (of the sharh) uses wording that suggests wujub, meaning it is considered necessary to compensate for the surah omission. The practical consequence: the student should follow the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (mufta bihi) which requires repeating Fatiha and surah if only surah was missed, but not repeating if Fatiha was missed.

Key Terms
فاتحة الكتاب (Fatiha al-Kitab): Surah al-Fatiha, obligatory in every rak'ah of prayer according to the Hanafi school (wajib)
استحباب (istihbab): Recommendation; an act that is commendable but not obligatory

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, what should one do if they recited a surah but omitted Fatiha in the first two rak'ats of 'Isha?
A) Recite only Fatiha in the last two rak'ats
B) Recite Fatiha and surah in the last two rak'ats
C) Do not repeat anything in the last two rak'ats
D) Repeat the entire prayer

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position: if surah is omitted in the first two rak'ats, compensate by reciting Fatiha and surah in the last two; if Fatiha is omitted, do not compensate.

The Ruling on Recitation in Qada of Jahri Prayers (Munfarid after Time)
States ruling on jahr vs ikhfa for qada of fajr/maghrib/isha after sunrise

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on recitation for a munfarid praying qada of a jahri prayer after sunrise and identify the two conditions that permit jahr.

Core Idea
After sunrise, a munfarid must recite quietly in qada of jahri prayers — jahr is only for congregation or within time.

This lesson clarifies the recitation ruling when making up missed Fajr, Maghrib, or Isha prayers after their time. The passage distinguishes between praying in congregation and praying alone, and establishes that the munfarid has no choice: ikhfa is obligatory. This is based on the principle that jahr is prescribed only in specific circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is qada of a jahri prayer (Fajr, Maghrib, Isha) after sunrise. Two scenarios: in congregation or alone.
2
State the ruling
If in congregation, jahr is wajib. If alone (munfarid), ikhfa is wajib and he has no choice.
This is the correct view (qawl sahih) in the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the evidence
The hadith of Laylat al-Aris shows the Prophet prayed Fajr qada in congregation with jahr.
This proves jahr is prescribed for congregation in qada.
4
Understand the reasoning
Jahr is confined to two situations: (1) congregation (obligatory jahr) and (2) munfarid within time (optional jahr). Neither condition exists here, so ikhfa is wajib.
The ruling is based on tawqif (legal prescription), not pure analogy.
5
Note the intra-ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars (al-Sarakhsi, Fakhr al-Islam) held jahr is superior because qada follows ada. But the correct view is that ikhfa is wajib.
This will be explored in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح مسئلہ اگر کسی شخص کی عشاء یا مغرب اور فجر کی نماز فوت ہو گئی پھر اس کو آفتاب طلوع ہونے کے بعد قضا کیا تو اس کی دوصورتیں ہیں ، توبا جماعت قضاء کرے گیا یا تنہا اگر جماعت کے ساتھ قضاء کی ہے تو جہر کرے اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ لیلتہ العریس کے موقع پر جب آپ نے فجر کی نماز کو با جماعت قضاء کیا تو آپ نے جہر فر مایا تھا۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے قضاء نماز میں قرآت بالجبر فرمائی مختصر واقعہ یہ ہے کہ سفر جہاد سے واپسی میں صحابہ کی درخواست پر آپ مع اشکر اترے اور حضرت بلال نے جاگنے کی ذمہ داری لی مگر سو گئے اور اس وقت جاگے کہ ان پر دھوپ آئی پس حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے وہاں سے کوچ کا حکم دیا اور آگے بڑھ کر جب آفتاب ایک نیزہ بلند ہوا تو اتر کر وضو کیا اور موذن کو اذان کا حکم دیا پھر دور کعتیں پڑھیں یعنی سنت فجر، پھر نماز کی اقامت کہی گئی پھر نماز فجر پڑھی جیسے روز پڑھا کرتے تھے اور ظاہر ہے کہ آپ فجر کی نماز میں بالجبر قرآت کرتے تھے پس ثابت ہوا کہ آپ نے لیلتہ العریس کے موقعہ پر فجر کی نماز کو قرآت بالجبر کے ساتھ قضاء کیا۔
تنہا جری نماز کی قضا کرتے وقت اخفاء واجب ہے اور اگر مذکورہ قضا نماز تہا پڑھنے تو اختفاء واجب ہے اور اس کو جہر اور اخفاء کے در میان اختیار نہیں ہے۔ یہی قول صحیح ہے میں الائمہ السرخسی اور فخر الاسلام وغیرہ نے کہا کہ جبر افضل ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ قضاء ادا کے موافق ہوتی ہے اور رات کی نمازوں میں ادا منفرد کے حق میں اختیار ہے کہ جہر کرے یا اختفاء کرے اور جہر افضل ہے پس ایسے ہی قضا میں ہوگا۔ قول صحیح کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جہ جہر کرنا دو صورتوں میں مختص ہے ایک یہ کہ نماز با جماعت ہو دوم یہ کہ نماز وقت کے اندر ہو پہلی صورت میں جہر واجب ہے اور دوسری صورت میں منفرد کے حق میں بطور اختیار کے ہے۔ حاصل یہ ہے کہ جہر اور اخفاء شرعی توقیف پر موقوف ہے اور ہم نے شریعت میں جہر دو طریقوں سے پایا ایک تو جہر واجب یہ اس وقت ہے کہ جماعت سے جہری نماز پڑھے خواہ ادا ہو یا قضاء ہو اور دوم جہر خیر یہ اس وقت ہے جب کہ منفر دوقت کے اندر جہری نماز پڑھے۔ اور یہاں جب کہ منفرد طلوع آفتاب کے بعد جہری نماز پڑھتا ہے تو دونوں باتوں میں سے کوئی بات نہیں پائی گئی یعنی نہ جماعت ہے اور نہ وقت اس لئے اس صورت میں نہ جہر واجب ہوگا اور نہ جب مخیر بلکہ اخفاء واجب ہوگا۔ جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
Explanation of the issue: If a person missed Isha, Maghrib, or Fajr prayer and then offered qada after sunrise, there are two scenarios: either he prayed qada in congregation or alone. If he prayed qada in congregation, he should recite aloud (jahr). The proof is that on the occasion of Laylat al-Aris, when the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed Fajr in congregation as qada, he recited aloud. The brief incident: On returning from a military expedition, at the request of the Companions, the Prophet dismounted with his army. Bilal took responsibility to wake them but fell asleep, and they woke only when the sun was upon them. The Prophet ordered them to move on. When the sun had risen a spear's length, he dismounted, performed wudu, ordered the muezzin to give adhan, prayed two rak'ahs (sunnah of Fajr), then iqama was said, and he prayed Fajr as he usually did. It is well-known that he used to recite aloud in Fajr prayer. Thus it is proven that on Laylat al-Aris he prayed Fajr qada with audible recitation.
When praying alone (munfarid), ikhfa (quiet recitation) is obligatory. If the aforementioned qada prayer is prayed alone, ikhfa is obligatory, and he has no choice between jahr and ikhfa. This is the correct view (qawl sahih). Some imams like al-Sarakhsi and Fakhr al-Islam said that jahr is superior (afdal). Their proof: Qada corresponds to ada (performance in time). In night prayers, the munfarid within the time has a choice: he may recite aloud or quietly, and aloud is superior. So similarly in qada. The proof of the correct view: Jahr is confined to two situations: (1) prayer in congregation, (2) prayer within its time. In the first, jahr is obligatory; in the second, the munfarid has a choice. In essence, jahr and ikhfa depend on legal prescription (tawqif). We find in Shariah two types of jahr: (i) obligatory jahr – when one prays a jahri prayer in congregation, whether ada or qada; (ii) optional jahr – when a munfarid prays a jahri prayer within its time. Here, when a munfarid prays a jahri prayer after sunrise, neither condition exists: neither congregation nor the prescribed time. Therefore, in this case, jahr is not obligatory, nor does he have a choice; rather ikhfa is obligatory. Written by Jamil Ahmad, may he be forgiven.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on recitation in qada (make-up) prayers for jahri prayers (Fajr, Maghrib, Isha) when offered after the time has passed, specifically after sunrise. The author distinguishes between two scenarios: praying in congregation and praying alone. The proof is the hadith of Laylat al-Aris, where the Prophet prayed Fajr qada in congregation and recited aloud. For a munfarid (alone) after the time, the correct view (qawl sahih) is that ikhfa (quiet recitation) is obligatory. Some Hanafi scholars (al-Sarakhsi, Fakhr al-Islam) held that jahr is superior because qada follows ada, and in ada the munfarid has a choice with jahr being better. However, the preferred view is that jahr and ikhfa are tied to specific conditions: jahr is only prescribed for congregation or for a munfarid within the time. Since after sunrise neither condition exists for a qada prayed alone, ikhfa becomes wajib. This is a ruling based on textual prescription (tawqif), not mere analogy.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Audible recitation in prayer.
إخفاء (ikhfa): Quiet recitation in prayer, barely audible to oneself.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory prayer after its time has expired.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi view, what is the ruling on recitation for a person praying Fajr qada alone after sunrise?
A) He must recite aloud (jahr).
B) He must recite quietly (ikhfa).
C) He has a choice between jahr and ikhfa.
D) He should recite in a moderate voice.

Key Takeaway
For a munfarid praying qada of a jahri prayer after its time, ikhfa is wajib.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Jahr vs Ikhfa in Qada for Munfarid
States the intra-Hanafi dispute on jahr vs ikhfa in qada for munfarid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi positions on recitation in qada for munfarid and evaluate the preferred view.

Core Idea
Some Hanafi scholars said jahr is afdal in qada for munfarid, but the relied-upon view says ikhfa is wajib.

In this lesson, we examine the intra-madhhab disagreement between the majority view (ikhfa wajib) and the view of al-Sarakhsi and Fakhr al-Islam (jahr afdal). Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens our ability to identify the mufta bihi position and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Position 1: ikhfa is wajib for munfarid in qada after time (correct view). Position 2: jahr is afdal (superior) but optional (view of Sarakhsi and Fakhr al-Islam).
2
Examine the proof for the minority view
They argue that qada follows ada. In ada, a munfarid in night prayers has a choice, and jahr is better. So it should be the same in qada.
This is based on qiyas (analogy) on the principle that qada replicates ada.
3
Examine the proof for the majority view
Jahr is confined to two situations: congregation (wajib) and munfarid within time (optional). Neither exists here, so ikhfa becomes wajib by default.
This is based on tawqif (textual prescription) rather than pure analogy.
4
Evaluate the tarjih (preponderance)
The correct view is that ikhfa is wajib because the conditions for jahr are absent. The majority view is stronger because it relies on the specific legal cause for jahr.
The passage states this is the qawl sahih.
5
Note the practical consequence
If one follows the minority view, he may recite aloud without sin but loses the virtue of following the stronger view. If one follows the majority, he must recite quietly.
The mufta bihi is ikhfa wajib.

Source Text

تشریح مسئلہ اگر کسی شخص کی عشاء یا مغرب اور فجر کی نماز فوت ہو گئی پھر اس کو آفتاب طلوع ہونے کے بعد قضا کیا تو اس کی دوصورتیں ہیں ، توبا جماعت قضاء کرے گیا یا تنہا اگر جماعت کے ساتھ قضاء کی ہے تو جہر کرے اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ لیلتہ العریس کے موقع پر جب آپ نے فجر کی نماز کو با جماعت قضاء کیا تو آپ نے جہر فر مایا تھا۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے قضاء نماز میں قرآت بالجبر فرمائی مختصر واقعہ یہ ہے کہ سفر جہاد سے واپسی میں صحابہ کی درخواست پر آپ مع اشکر اترے اور حضرت بلال نے جاگنے کی ذمہ داری لی مگر سو گئے اور اس وقت جاگے کہ ان پر دھوپ آئی پس حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے وہاں سے کوچ کا حکم دیا اور آگے بڑھ کر جب آفتاب ایک نیزہ بلند ہوا تو اتر کر وضو کیا اور موذن کو اذان کا حکم دیا پھر دور کعتیں پڑھیں یعنی سنت فجر، پھر نماز کی اقامت کہی گئی پھر نماز فجر پڑھی جیسے روز پڑھا کرتے تھے اور ظاہر ہے کہ آپ فجر کی نماز میں بالجبر قرآت کرتے تھے پس ثابت ہوا کہ آپ نے لیلتہ العریس کے موقعہ پر فجر کی نماز کو قرآت بالجبر کے ساتھ قضاء کیا۔
تنہا جری نماز کی قضا کرتے وقت اخفاء واجب ہے اور اگر مذکورہ قضا نماز تہا پڑھنے تو اختفاء واجب ہے اور اس کو جہر اور اخفاء کے در میان اختیار نہیں ہے۔ یہی قول صحیح ہے میں الائمہ السرخسی اور فخر الاسلام وغیرہ نے کہا کہ جبر افضل ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ قضاء ادا کے موافق ہوتی ہے اور رات کی نمازوں میں ادا منفرد کے حق میں اختیار ہے کہ جہر کرے یا اختفاء کرے اور جہر افضل ہے پس ایسے ہی قضا میں ہوگا۔ قول صحیح کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جہ جہر کرنا دو صورتوں میں مختص ہے ایک یہ کہ نماز با جماعت ہو دوم یہ کہ نماز وقت کے اندر ہو پہلی صورت میں جہر واجب ہے اور دوسری صورت میں منفرد کے حق میں بطور اختیار کے ہے۔ حاصل یہ ہے کہ جہر اور اخفاء شرعی توقیف پر موقوف ہے اور ہم نے شریعت میں جہر دو طریقوں سے پایا ایک تو جہر واجب یہ اس وقت ہے کہ جماعت سے جہری نماز پڑھے خواہ ادا ہو یا قضاء ہو اور دوم جہر خیر یہ اس وقت ہے جب کہ منفر دوقت کے اندر جہری نماز پڑھے۔ اور یہاں جب کہ منفرد طلوع آفتاب کے بعد جہری نماز پڑھتا ہے تو دونوں باتوں میں سے کوئی بات نہیں پائی گئی یعنی نہ جماعت ہے اور نہ وقت اس لئے اس صورت میں نہ جہر واجب ہوگا اور نہ جب مخیر بلکہ اخفاء واجب ہوگا۔ جمیل احمد عفی عنہ

Making Up Missed Fatiha or Surah in Isha Prayer
Ruling on qada of Fatiha or surah when missed in first two rak'ahs of Isha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada of Fatiha and surah in Isha and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Qada of missed recitation must preserve the prescribed order: Fatiha before surah.

This passage addresses a practical scenario in Isha prayer: when a worshipper omits either Fatiha or an additional surah in the first two rak'ahs. The Hanafi school has an internal difference on whether and how to make up these missed recitations in the last two rak'ahs. The core legal reasoning revolves around the prescribed sequence (tartib) of recitation and the general rule that a missed wajib is not compensated without specific evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Recognize the two cases: (1) surah recited without Fatiha, (2) Fatiha recited without surah. The ruling differs for each according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
2
State the positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: In case (1) no qada for Fatiha; in case (2) qada both Fatiha and surah with jahr. Abu Yusuf: no qada for either.
3
Analyze the evidence for each position
Abu Hanifa/Muhammad rely on preserving the order (Fatiha must precede surah). Abu Yusuf relies on the principle that a missed wajib cannot be made up without specific proof.
4
Evaluate the rebuttal
Sahib al-‘Inayah counters Abu Yusuf by arguing that reciting a surah in the last two rak'ahs is mandub, so qada of surah is possible. For Fatiha, order prevents qada.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is the relied-upon position in the school, as it is supported by later authorities and practical reasoning.
