فرق بھی ہے کہ فاتحہ کا پڑھنا ایسے طور پر مشروع ہوا ہے کہ سورت اس پر مرتب ہو فاتحہ ایسے طور پر پڑھے کہ اس کے بعد میں سورت پڑھے پس پہلی صورت میں جب سورت پڑھی اور سورۃ فاتحہ نہیں پڑھی اگر اخرین ہے اس فاتحہ کی قضاء کی تو سورۂ فاتحہ سورت پر مرتب ہوگی یعنی صورت پہلے پڑھی گئی اور سورۃ فاتحہ بعد میں اور یہ حالت موضوع شرع کے خلاف کیونکہ پہلے فاتحہ پھر سورت پڑھنا مشروع ہے۔ اور یہاں برعکس ہو گیا اس لئے کہ اس صورت میں فاتحہ قضاء کرنے کا حکم نہیں دیا۔ رہی دوسری صورت یعنی جب اولیین میں فاتحہ پڑھی اور سورت نہیں پڑھی تو اخرین میں قضاء کرے گا کیونکہ اس صورت میں مشر طریقہ پر قضاء کرنا ممکن ہے اس لئے کہ مشروع طریقہ یہ ہے کہ فاتحہ کے بعد سورت ہو اور وہ یہاں موجود ہے۔ صاحب عنایہ نے امام ابو یوسف کے قول کا جواب دیتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ ہمیں یہ بات تسلیم نہیں کہ اخربین میں سورت غیر مشروں۔ کیونکہ فخر الاسلام نے شرح جامع صغیر میں فرمایا کہ اخربین میں سورت کا پڑھنا مندوب ہے اسی وجہ سے اگر اخر بین میں سورت پڑھا سجدہ سہو واجب نہیں ہوگا۔
What is the ruling if one recited a surah in the first two rak'ahs of Isha without reciting Fatiha, or recited Fatiha without adding a surah? And whoever recites in Isha in the first two rak'ahs a surah and does not recite Fatiha, he should not make it up in the last two rak'ahs. But if he recites Fatiha and does not add anything else to it, he should recite Fatiha and a surah in the last two rak'ahs and recite aloud (jahr). This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He should not make up either of them, because when an obligation (wajib) is missed from its time, it is not made up without evidence. The proof for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and the difference between the two cases: The recitation of Fatiha is prescribed in such a way that the surah follows it. So if he makes up Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs, Fatiha would follow the surah, which is contrary to the prescribed order. Conversely, if he omitted the surah, it can be made up in the prescribed manner. Then here he mentions what indicates obligation, while in al-Asl it is expressed with the word istihbab (recommendation), because if it is delayed, it is not connected to Fatiha, so it is not possible to observe its prescribed object from every aspect.
Translation: And whoever recited a surah in the first two rak'ahs of Isha but did not recite Fatiha should not repeat Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs. But if he recited Fatiha and did not add anything else to it, then in the last two rak'ahs he should recite both Fatiha and a surah, and recite aloud. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He should not make up either of them, because when a wajib is missed from its time, it is not made up. And the proof for both sides and the difference between the two cases: Fatiha is prescribed in a manner that the surah follows it. So if he makes up Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs, Fatiha would follow the surah, contrary to the prescribed order. This is unlike the case where he omitted the surah, because making up the surah is possible in the prescribed manner. Then here he mentions what indicates obligation, while in al-Asl it is with the word istihbab, because if it is delayed, it is not connected to Fatiha, so it is not possible to observe its prescribed object from every aspect.
Explanation of the issue: A person recited a surah in the first two rak'ahs of Isha but did not recite Fatiha. He should not make up Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs. But if he recited Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs and did not recite anything after it, then in the last two rak'ahs he should recite both Fatiha and a surah, and recite aloud with both. This is the ruling of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: He should not make up either Fatiha or the surah. His proof: Both Fatiha and surah are wajib (obligatory). When an obligatory act is missed from its time, it is not made up unless there is evidence for making it up, and such evidence is not present here. Therefore, neither should be made up. The explanation of the proof: The term qada means turning what is prescribed as a right (mā lahu musharra‘an) to what is obligatory (mā ‘alayhi). Here, in the last two rak'ahs, reciting a surah is not prescribed. So when the surah is not prescribed as a right in the last two rak'ahs, one cannot make up the surah that was missed in the first two rak'ahs. The proof for the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and the difference between the two cases: Fatiha is prescribed in such a way that the surah follows it. So in the first case (surah recited but no Fatiha), if one makes up Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs, Fatiha would follow the surah—this is contrary to the prescribed order. Hence, in that case, making up Fatiha is not commanded. As for the second case (Fatiha recited but no surah), he should make up in the last two rak'ahs because making up in the prescribed manner is possible: the prescribed method is that the surah follows Fatiha, and here Fatiha is already present (in the first two rak'ahs), so by reciting both in the last two, the order is maintained. The author of al-‘Inayah responded to Abu Yusuf's statement by saying: We do not accept that the surah is not prescribed in the last two rak'ahs, because Fakhr al-Islam said in Sharh al-Jami‘ al-Saghir that reciting a surah in the last two rak'ahs is mandub (recommended). For this reason, if one recites a surah in the last two rak'ahs, sajdat al-sahw is not wajib.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling for a person who, in the first two rak'ahs of Isha prayer, either recited a surah without Fatiha or recited Fatiha without a surah. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two), if he omitted Fatiha but recited a surah, he does not make up Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs because making it up would reverse the prescribed order (Fatiha before surah). However, if he omitted the surah but recited Fatiha, he should make up both Fatiha and a surah in the last two rak'ahs and recite aloud, because the order can be preserved (Fatiha first, then surah). Abu Yusuf holds that neither is made up, because both are wajib and once missed, they are not made up in later rak'ahs without specific evidence. The passage notes that in the original text (al-Asl) the word istihbab (recommendation) is used, indicating that the obligation level might be different. The commentator (likely the author of Ashraf al-Hidaya) explains that the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is based on the ability to observe the prescribed order (tartib). Sahib al-‘Inayah rebuts Abu Yusuf by citing Fakhr al-Islam that reciting a surah in the last two rak'ahs is mandub, not non-prescribed, so making up the surah is possible. The core of the dispute is whether the missed wajib can be compensated in later rak'ahs while maintaining proper sequence.

Key Terms
الفاتحة (al-Fatiha): The opening chapter of the Quran, recited in every rak'ah of prayer.
السورة (al-surah): An additional chapter or verses after Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs for wajib prayers.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed wajib element in a later part of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if a person in Isha prayer recited only a surah (no Fatiha) in the first two rak'ahs, what should he do?
A) Recite Fatiha only in the last two rak'ahs.
B) Recite both Fatiha and surah in the last two rak'ahs.
C) Do not make up Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs.
D) Recite only a surah in the last two rak'ahs.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, qada of missed Fatiha or surah in Isha is allowed only when the prescribed order (Fatiha before surah) can be preserved; otherwise, sajdat al-sahw suffices.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Qada of Missed Recitation in Last Two Rak'ahs
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada of Fatihah and surah in last rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada of missed Fatihah and surah in the last two rak'ahs and explain the intra-madhhab disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifah/Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
When recitation is missed, only the surah is made up, not the Fatihah, to preserve the prescribed order.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in 'Isha prayer where a person omits recitation in the first two rak'ahs. The Hanafi school has an internal dispute over what must be made up and how. Understanding this dispute clarifies the importance of the prescribed order (Fatihah then surah) and the principle that qada of an obligatory act requires specific proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Determine what was missed: was it only Fatihah, only the surah, or both? The ruling depends on which case occurred.
Scenario 1: Fatihah missed, surah recited. Scenario 2: Fatihah recited, surah missed.
2
State the positions of the two groups
Imam Abu Hanifah and Imam Muhammad require qada of the surah only (scenario 2), but not of Fatihah. Imam Abu Yusuf rejects qada entirely in both scenarios.
The mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifah and Muhammad.
3
Analyze the proofs
Abu Hanifah and Muhammad argue that making qada of Fatihah would reverse the prescribed order. Abu Yusuf argues that a missed wajib cannot be made up without specific proof, which is lacking.
The hanafi response cites Fakhr al-Islam: the surah is mandub in the last two, so qada is possible.
4
Consider the manner of recitation
When making qada, should one recite aloud or silently? The correct view (al-sahih) is to recite both aloud to avoid mixing jahr and ikhfa in one rak'ah.
Alternative narrations exist: only surah aloud, or both silently.
5
Identify the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: if only the surah is missed, the mufta bihi requires qada with jahr; Abu Yusuf requires no qada at all.
This affects the validity of the prayer and the need for sajda sahw.

اس لئے کہ واجب جب اپنے وقت سے فوت ہو گیا تو بی مذکور ہے کے اس کی قضا نہیں کی جاتی۔ اور طرفین کی دلیل اور وہی دونوں صورتوں میں فرق بھی ہے کہ فاتحہ کا پڑھنا ایسے طور پر شروع ہوا۔ امر کے سورت اس پر مرتب خواہ شفع ثانی میں اس کی قضاء کرے یا قضاء نہ کرے ) اور واجب جب اپنے وقت سے فوت ہو جا۔ وہ فاتح اس کی قضاء نہیں کی جاتی الا یہ کہ کوئی دلیل قضاء پائی جائے اور دلیل قضاء یہاں موجود نہیں اس لئے ان دونوں کی قضاء بھی نہیں ہوگی تشرت دلیل اس لئے موجود نہیں کہ قضاء کہتے ہیں مالہ مشروعا کو ماعلیہ کی طرف پھیر دینا یعنی شریعت نے اس کے لئے جو حق مشروع کیا تھا ؟ اس کی طرف پھیر دینا جو اس پر واجب ہے اور یہاں حال یہ ہے کہ آخر کی دو رکعتوں میں سورت مشروع نہیں ہوئی پس جب آخر کی ان کے رکعتوں میں سورت اس کا حق بن کر مشروع نہیں ہوئی تو پہلی دو رکعتوں میں فوت شدہ سورت کی آخر کی دو رکعت میں قضاء نہیں کر سکتا۔ بالکل اور پر طرفین کی دلیل اور یہی دونوں صورتوں میں وجہ فرق بھی ہے کہ فاتحہ کا پڑھنا ایسے طور پر مشروع ہوا ہے کہ سورت اس پر مرتب ہو فاتحہ ایسے طور پر پڑھے کہ اس کے بعد میں سورت پڑھے پس پہلی صورت میں جب سورت پڑھی اور سورۃ فاتحہ نہیں پڑھی اگر اخرین ہے اس فاتحہ کی قضاء کی تو سورۂ فاتحہ سورت پر مرتب ہوگی یعنی صورت پہلے پڑھی گئی اور سورۃ فاتحہ بعد میں اور یہ حالت موضوع شرع کے خلاف کیونکہ پہلے فاتحہ پھر سورت پڑھنا مشروع ہے۔ اور یہاں برعکس ہو گیا اس لئے کہ اس صورت میں فاتحہ قضاء کرنے کا حکم نہیں دیا۔ رہی دوسری صورت یعنی جب اولیین میں فاتحہ پڑھی اور سورت نہیں پڑھی تو اخرین میں قضاء کرے گا کیونکہ اس صورت میں مشر طریقہ پر قضاء کرنا ممکن ہے اس لئے کہ مشروع طریقہ یہ ہے کہ فاتحہ کے بعد سورت ہو اور وہ یہاں موجود ہے۔ صاحب عنایہ نے امام ابو یوسف کے قول کا جواب دیتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ ہمیں یہ بات تسلیم نہیں کہ اخربین میں سورت غیر مشروں۔ کیونکہ فخر الاسلام نے شرح جامع صغیر میں فرمایا کہ اخربین میں سورت کا پڑھنا مندوب ہے اسی وجہ سے اگر اخر بین میں سورت پڑھا سجدہ سہو واجب نہیں ہوگا۔

ويجهر بهما هو الصحيح لان الجمع بين الجهر والمخافتة فى ركعة واحدة شنيع وتغير النفل وهو الفاتحة اولى ترجمہ اور سورت اور فاتحہ دونوں کا جبر کرے۔ یہی صحیح ہے کیونکہ جبر اور اختفاء کا ایک رکعت میں جمع کرنا برا ہے۔ اور نفل کا متغیر کرنا اور وہ فاتحہ ہے اولی ہے۔

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جب اخر بین میں سورت کی قضاء کرے گا تو سورۂ فاتحہ اور سورت دونوں کے ساتھ جہر کرے یہی صحیح قول ہے۔ ابن ساعد نے امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف سے روایت کی ہے کہ صرف سورت کے ساتھ جبر کرے اور ہشام نے امام محمد سے روایت کی کہ بالکل ہم نہ کرے نہ فاتحہ کے ساتھ نہ سورت کے ساتھ ۔ ہشام کی روایت کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جبر اور اخفاء دونوں کو ایک رکعت میں جمع کرنا شفیع اور برا ہے اور سورت کا متغیر کرنا یعنی بجائے جہر کے سورت کو بالسر پڑھنا اولی ہے کیونکہ فاتحہ اپنے محل میں بھی ہے اور سورت پر مقدم بھی ہے اس لئے فاتحہ اصل ہوئی اور سورت اس کے تابع ہوئی اخربین میں فاتحہ کا حق یہ ہے کہ اس کے ساتھ اخفاء کیا جائے پس اس کے تابع ہو گر عورت کے ساتھ بھی اختفاء کیا جائے گا۔

روایت ابن ساعہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اخر مبین میں فاتحہ کا پڑھنا اداء ہے اور سورت کا پڑھنا قضاء ہے اور ا دا اپنے محل کے مطابق ہوتا ہے اور قتنا بحسب الفوات ہوتی ہے پس چونکہ سورت صفت جبر کے ساتھ فوت ہوئی ہے اس لئے اس کی قضا ، صفت جہر کے ساتھ ہوگی اور فاتحہ چونکہ اپنے محل میں ہے اس لئے فاتحہ میں اس کی صفت کی رعایت کی جائے گی اور فاتحہ کی صفت آخرین میں اختفاء ہے اس لئے فاتحہ کے ساتھ اخفاء ہوگا۔ رہی یہ بات کہ اجہبر اور اخفاء کا ایک رکعت میں جمع ہونا لازم آیا تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ قضاء اپنے مقام کے ساتھ لاحق ہوتی ہے پس سورت اگر چہ اخربین میں پڑھی گئی مگر محسوب اولین میں ہوگی۔ اس وجہ سے تقدیرا ایک رکعت میں جہر اور اخفاء کا جمع کرنا لازم نہیں آئے گا۔

اور قول صحیح کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک رکعت میں جہر اور اخفاء کو جمع کرنا تو شرعا مذموم ہے اب دو ہی صورتیں ہیں یا تو دونوں میں اختفاء
Chapter on the description of prayer. Scenario: He recited Fatihah and did not add anything to it, then in the last two rak'ahs he recites both Fatihah and a surah and recites them aloud. This is the view of Imam Abu Hanifah and Muhammad. Imam Abu Yusuf said: Do not make qada of either of them, because when an obligatory act is missed beyond its time, it is known that qada of it is not performed. The proof of the two (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad) and the distinction between the two cases is that reciting Fatihah is prescribed in such a way that the surah follows it. So if one makes qada of Fatihah in the last two rak'ahs, then Fatihah would follow the surah, which is contrary to the prescribed order. This is the reason why when one omits the surah in the first two rak'ahs, it is possible to make qada of it in the prescribed manner. Then here the word that indicates obligation is mentioned, while in al-Mabsut it is with the word 'istihbab' (recommendation), because if the surah is delayed, it is not connected with the Fatihah. Therefore observing the prescribed order completely is not possible. Explanation of the scenario: A person in Isha prayer recited a surah in the first two rak'ahs but did not recite Fatihah. This person will not make qada of Fatihah in the last two rak'ahs. If he recited Fatihah in the first two rak'ahs but nothing after it, then in the last two rak'ahs he recites both Fatihah and a surah and recites both aloud. This is the ruling according to the two (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad). Imam Abu Yusuf said: Do not make qada of either Fatihah or surah. His proof is that both Fatihah and surah are obligatory. (This is why if one omits either of them, sajda sahw becomes obligatory, whether he makes qada in the second pair or not.) When an obligatory act is missed beyond its time, its qada is not performed unless there is a proof for qada, and such proof is absent here. Therefore qada of neither is performed. The proof is absent because qada means turning something that was prescribed as a right to what is obligatory, but here in the last two rak'ahs, a surah is not prescribed. So since in the last two rak'ahs a surah is not prescribed as a right for him, he cannot make qada of the surah missed in the first two rak'ahs. Completely. And the proof of the two (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad) and the distinction between the two cases is that reciting Fatihah is prescribed in such a way that the surah follows it: one recites Fatihah then afterwards recites a surah. So in the first case, when he recited a surah and did not recite Fatihah, if he makes qada of Fatihah in the last two, then Fatihah would follow the surah—i.e., the surah was recited first and Fatihah later—and this is contrary to the prescribed order because the prescribed order is Fatihah then surah. Here it is reversed, so in this case he is not commanded to make qada of Fatihah. As for the second case, when he recited Fatihah in the first two and did not recite a surah, then he makes qada in the last two because in this case it is possible to make qada in the prescribed manner: the prescribed manner is that the surah follows Fatihah, and that is present here. The author of al-'Inayah, in responding to Imam Abu Yusuf's statement, said: We do not accept that the surah is not prescribed in the last two rak'ahs. Because Fakhr al-Islam said in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir that reciting a surah in the last two rak'ahs is recommended (mandub); for this reason, if one recites a surah in the last two, sajda sahw does not become obligatory. And he recites both aloud—this is the correct view—because combining jahr (loud recitation) and ikhfa (silent recitation) in a single rak'ah is objectionable, and changing the optional act—and that is Fatihah—is more appropriate. Translation: And he recites both surah and Fatihah aloud. This is the correct view because combining jahr and ikhfa in one rak'ah is bad, and changing the optional act—which is Fatihah—is more appropriate. Explanation of the issue: When he makes qada of the surah in the last two, he recites both Fatihah and surah aloud—this is the correct statement. Ibn Sa'dah narrated from Imam Abu Hanifah and Imam Abu Yusuf that he recites only the surah aloud. Hisham narrated from Imam Muhammad that he does not recite either aloud at all—neither Fatihah nor surah. The reason for Hisham's narration is that combining jahr and ikhfa in one rak'ah is shameful and bad, and changing the surah—i.e., reciting it silently instead of aloud—is more appropriate because Fatihah is in its place and is also prior to the surah; thus Fatihah is the original and the surah is its follower. In the last two, the right of Fatihah is that it be recited silently, so following it, the surah should also be recited silently. The reason for Ibn Sa'dah's narration is that in the last two, reciting Fatihah is an actual performance (ada') while reciting the surah is a qada, and ada' is according to its place while qada is according to what was missed. So since the surah was missed with the attribute of jahr, its qada will be with the attribute of jahr, and Fatihah, being in its place, will be observed with its attribute, and the attribute of Fatihah in the last two is ikhfa, so Fatihah will be recited silently. As for the objection that this necessitates combining jahr and ikhfa in one rak'ah, the answer is that qada attaches to its original place. So although the surah is recited in the last two, it is considered as if in the first two. Therefore, combining jahr and ikhfa in one rak'ah is not necessitated even implicitly. And the proof of the correct view is that combining jahr and ikhfa in one rak'ah is legally reprehensible. Now there are only two possibilities: either both are recited silently... (text cut off)
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, a commentary on al-Hidayah, discusses a scenario in the 'Isha prayer where a person misses reciting either Surah al-Fatihah or an additional surah in the first two rak'ahs. It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifah and Imam Muhammad hold that if Fatihah was omitted, it is not to be made up in the last two rak'ahs because that would reverse the prescribed order (Fatihah then surah). However, if only the surah was omitted, it should be made up in the last two rak'ahs together with Fatihah, both recited aloud. Imam Abu Yusuf argues that neither should be made up because both are obligatory acts whose time has passed, and qada of an obligatory act requires specific proof, which is lacking. The commentary then addresses the question of whether to recite aloud or silently when making qada. The relied-upon position (al-sahih) is to recite both aloud to avoid mixing jahr and ikhfa in the same rak'ah. Alternative narrations from Ibn Sa'dah and Hisham state to recite only the surah aloud or to recite both silently. The reasoning revolves around whether the surah's qada is considered as belonging to its original place (the first two rak'ahs) or its actual place (the last two). The correct view preserves the original attribute of the missed recitation.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Making up an obligatory act after its prescribed time has passed, here specifically recitation missed in the first two rak'ahs.
جهر (jahr): Loud recitation, required in the first two rak'ahs of Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha (for imam).
إخفاء (ikhfa'): Silent recitation, prescribed in the last two rak'ahs and in Zuhr and Asr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct (sahih) view in this passage, how should one recite Fatihah and the surah when making qada of the surah in the last two rak'ahs?
A) Both silently
B) Both aloud
C) Fatihah silently, surah aloud
D) Only surah aloud, Fatihah not recited

Key Takeaway
When recitation is missed in the first two rak'ahs, only the surah (not Fatihah) is made up in the last two, and both are recited aloud according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Ruling on Qada' of Missed Surah in the Last Two Rak'ahs
Intra-Hanafi textual analysis on wajib vs mustahab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi positions on whether qada' of the surah in the last two rak'ahs is wajib or mustahab, and state the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Qada' of the surah in the last two rak'ahs is mustahab, not wajib, because the surah is separated from the first Fatiha by a second Fatiha.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi textual dispute between two foundational sources: Jami' al-Saghir and al-Mabsut. The former appears to require making up a missed surah as an obligation, while the latter treats it as a recommendation. We will examine the reasoning behind each view and determine the operative ruling (mufta bihi).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two textual sources
Locate the specific phrases from Jami' al-Saghir (قرأ في الأخريين, interpreted as a command) and al-Mabsut (أحب أن يقضيها, 'I prefer that he makes it up'). Understand how each phrase signals a different legal status.
In Hanafi usul, an imperative (amr) indicates obligation unless there is a contextual reason (qarīnah) to the contrary.
2
Analyse the evidence for each position
Jami' al-Saghir's wording implies wujūb because the command is unqualified. Al-Mabsut's wording uses 'ahabba' which indicates istihbāb (recommendation). The author then provides a substantive reason for istihbāb: the surah is not directly attached to the first Fatiha due to the intervening second Fatiha, so its connection is weakened.
The reasoning is based on the structure of the prayer: the surah is meant to follow directly after Fatiha in each rak'ah, but in the last two rak'ahs, the first Fatiha is already superseded.
3
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If qada' were wajib, omitting it would require sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). If mustahab, no compensation is needed. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that it is mustahab, so the imam or individual may leave it without sin or required prostration.
This practical difference is not explicitly stated in the text but is derived from the ruling level.

Chapter on the Description of Prayer. The difference in wording is mentioned here. It is said that in Jami' al-Saghir, a word is mentioned that indicates obligation of qada' of surah in the last two rak'ahs, because in Jami' al-Saghir it says 'He recites in the last two' and this is like a command. And a command indicates obligation. So from the wording of Jami' al-Saghir it is known that qada' of surah in the last two is obligatory. And the evidence is that which passed in the previous lines. And in al-Mabsut it is mentioned with the word istihbab, because the wording of al-Mabsut is 'That he does not leave the surah in the first two, I prefer that he makes it up.' And it is obvious that the word 'aheb' indicates recommendation. So from al-Mabsut it is shown that if one left the surah in the first two, then making it up in the last two is mustahab, not wajib! And the evidence for istihbab is that the surah was delayed after Fatiha, but it was not connected to the first Fatiha because between the first Fatiha and the surah, a second Fatiha (which is better to recite in the last two) interposed. So it became impossible to observe the surah in every respect. Therefore in al-Mabsut it is said that making up the surah is mustahab, not wajib. And he recites both Fatiha and surah aloud. And it is correct to recite both aloud because combining jahr and ikhfa' in one rak'ah is reprehensible, and changing the nafl, which is the Fatiha, is preferable. Translation: He should recite both surah and Fatiha aloud. This is correct because combining jahr and ikhfa' in one rak'ah is bad. And changing the nafl, that is the Fatiha, is preferable. Explanation: When he makes up the surah in the last two, he should recite al-Fatiha and the surah both aloud; this is the correct statement. Ibn Sa'id narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf that he should recite only the surah aloud, and Hisham narrated from Imam Muhammad that he should not recite aloud at all, neither with Fatiha nor with surah. The reason for Hisham's narration is that combining jahr and ikhfa' in one rak'ah is ugly and bad, and it is preferable to change the surah (i.e., recite it silently instead of aloud) because Fatiha is in its place and is prioritized over the surah. So Fatiha is the original and the surah is its subordinate. In the last two rak'ahs, the right of Fatiha is to be recited with ikhfa', so its subordinate (the surah) should also be recited with ikhfa'. The reason for Ibn Sa'id's narration is that reciting Fatiha in the last two is an ada' (actual performance), while reciting the surah is a qada' (make-up). Ada' is according to its place, and qada' is according to how it was missed. Since the surah was missed with the attribute of jahr, its qada' will be with jahr. And since Fatiha is in its place, its attribute is observed: the attribute of Fatiha in the last two is ikhfa', so Fatiha will be recited with ikhfa'. As for the objection that combining jahr and ikhfa' in one rak'ah becomes necessary, the answer is that qada' is attached to its original place; the surah, although recited in the last two, is counted in the first two. Therefore, there is no actual combination of jahr and ikhfa' in one rak'ah. And the evidence for the correct statement is that combining jahr and ikhfa' in one rak'ah is legally blameworthy. Now there are only two possibilities: either to recite both with ikhfa' as Hisham narrated from Imam Muhammad, or to recite both with jahr. In the first case, it would necessitate making the stronger subordinate to the weaker, which is in no way appropriate because reciting the surah with jahr was wajib, and reciting Fatiha in the last two with ikhfa' is sunnah and of a lower grade. So to observe the attribute of Fatiha (which is sunnah) and thus ignore the attribute of the surah (which is wajib) is to make the stronger subordinate to the weaker, which is inappropriate. So this case is incorrect. Now only the second case remains: reciting both with jahr. There is no objection in this because in this case, due to the wajib (surah) having its attribute (jahr), the nafl (Fatiha) has to change its attribute (ikhfa'). This is preferable because the weaker becomes subordinate to the stronger.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding two issues: (1) whether making up the missed surah in the last two rak'ahs is wajib or mustahab, and (2) how to recite Fatiha and the surah aloud or silently in that case. The author first notes the difference between Jami' al-Saghir and al-Mabsut. In Jami' al-Saghir, the word 'qara'a fi al-akhirayn' is interpreted as a command, making qada' wajib. In al-Mabsut, the word 'ahabba' indicates recommendation. The reasoning for istihbab is that the surah is delayed by a second Fatiha, so its connection to the first Fatiha is broken. Then, the dispute over jahr and ikhfa' is presented. Three riwayat exist: (i) from Ibn Sa'id from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: jahr only for surah, ikhfa' for Fatiha; (ii) from Hisham from Muhammad: no jahr at all; (iii) the correct view: jahr for both. The reasoning for each is explained. Hisham's view argues that combining jahr and ikhfa' in one rak'ah is bad, and since Fatiha is the original, its ikhfa' should be followed. Ibn Sa'id's view distinguishes between ada' (Fatiha) and qada' (surah), applying each attribute appropriately. The correct view avoids making the stronger (wajib surah's jahr) subordinate to the weaker (sunnah Fatiha's ikhfa'). The tarjih is that reciting both with jahr is correct.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed recitation (of surah after Fatiha) in the last two rak'ahs.
أمر (amr): A command; in usul, it indicates obligation unless there is a contextual clue.
استحباب (istihbab): Recommendation; an act whose performance is preferred but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on qada' of the surah in the last two rak'ahs?
A) Wajib, because the surah is a mandatory part of each rak'ah.
B) Mustahab, because the surah is separated from the first Fatiha.
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah, requiring sajdah al-sahw if omitted.
D) Haram, because the surah should not be recited in the last two rak'ahs.

Key Takeaway
Qada' of the surah in the last two rak'ahs is mustahab, not wajib, because the surah is disconnected from the first Fatiha.
